Report on the results of parallel checks of the value added tax administration between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic carried out in 2005
Introductory word
The material presented reports on the progress and results of the parallel controls carried out by the Supreme audit office, Czech republic and Najvyšším kontrolným úradom of the Slovak republic, which were aimed at the area of the administration of value added tax and the use of information system VIES (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System – a System for the exchange of information on value added tax).
In may 2004, joined the Czech republic and the Slovak republic to the European union, revenue from value added tax, therefore, not only affect the state budgets of both countries, but also the budget of the European union as a whole.
Parallel control actions were mainly focused on the control procedure of tax administrators in examining the amount of value added tax paid on the commercial transactions effected between the member states of the European union.
The introduction of the VIES allow the electronic exchange of information on the registration of payers of value added tax in the individual member states of the European union and of the commercial transactions carried out by these payers.
A mismatch between the data in the VIES and data in the tax return for value added tax submitted by the payer should the tax administrator to draw attention to suspected cases and to allow detection of tax evasion or fraud.
The contribution made parallel controls consisted not only in the exchange of information on the procedure of the financial or tax authorities in the administration of value added tax, but in particular in the examination of the use of VIES in monitoring the application of the right to exemption from value added tax on the intrakomunitárních transactions.
The knowledge gained in the implementation of parallel checks are beneficial for the development of mutual cooperation and will be used in the implementation of other parallel controls in cooperation with the audit institutions of the member states of the European union.
Report on the results of parallel controls of value added tax administration for the period from 1. 5. 2004 to 30. 6. 2005
Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 05/19 (SK) 22/2005
Subject control: (CZ) the Administration of value added tax, (SK) the Control procedure the tax authorities in the management, control and enforcement of value added tax and the fulfilment of tasks within the system VIES for the exchange of information between the member states of the EU
The supreme audit office, Czech republic (hereinafter the "NKU, the CZECH republic") and the Najvyšší kontrolný úrad Slovenskej republiky (hereinafter referred to as "SAO SR") entered into on 12. 9. 2005 contract for cooperation in control activities.
The subject of the contract was the cooperation when conducted parallel control actions of the "Administration of value added tax", included in the audit plan of the SAO, the CZECH republic for the year 2005 under no. 05/19 and "Control procedure of tax orgánov pri administration, control and vymáhaní dan z pridanej values and plnenia task within the system VIES to exchanging informácií between the member countries of the EU", included in the audit plan of the SAO SR under no. 22/2005.
In parallel, the control actions carried out were of the nature of coordinated control.
The result of the joint coordinated control was processed within the meaning of the European Enforcement Regulation No 31 for INTOSAI control standards.
Cooperation consisted in the exchange of information to the extent provided for in the concluded treaty and in the preparation of a joint final report on the outcome of parallel checks.
The purpose of the coordinated audit was the verification of selected cases of the supply and acquisition of goods at suspicious commercial transactions between the payer of value added tax from the Czech republic (hereinafter "CR") and the Slovak republic (hereinafter "SR").
Both the parties contractually committed themselves to mutually provide information from public sources, from the electronic system VIES (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System) and the data about the received and sent requests for verification of business transactions between the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA.
Checks were carried out in parallel between June and December 2005.
On the territory of the CZECH republic the audit was carried out by the department of the state budget and territorial departments of central Bohemia, north-west Bohemia, south Bohemia, south Moravia, central Moravia and north Moravia.
The audited entities were the Ministry of finance and 12 financial authorities: Financial office in Mlada Boleslav Financial office in Cologne, the tax office in Teplice, the Financial office in Karlovy Vary, the Financial office in the Camp, the Financial office Brno III Financial office in Znojmo, the Financial office in Zlin, the Financial office in Šumperk, the Financial office in Ostrava as well, the Financial office for Prague 7 and the Financial office for Prague 9.
Control on the territory of SR was carried out Financial and tax sections of the SAO SR, in cooperation with the Expoziturami the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice on 9 selected tax office: Tax office Bratislava I, Daňový úrad Komárno, the Tax office in Trenčín, the Tax office Prievidza, the Tax office is Elected, the Tax office in Dolný Kubín, the Tax office Košice II, the Tax office Košice In and the Tax office in Michalovce.
Objective of controls:
The aim of parallel monitoring of the actions was to review the procedure of the financial or tax authorities in the administration of value added tax (hereinafter "VAT") after the integration of the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA into a single internal market of the European union (hereinafter "EU") and explore the use of the electronic information system of VIES, in particular in monitoring the application of the entitlement to exemption from VAT.
The controlled period of coordinated control was from 1. 5. 2004 to 30. 6. 2005.
A summary of the results and evaluation of parallel control actions In the member states, the EU has introduced an electronic system VIES, which allows the tax authorities to check whether the supplier was entitled to exempt the chargeable event of VAT, and in the country of destination allows to check, whether the purchaser acquired the goods properly admitted and taxed.
The VIEs system is not centralised within the EU, each member state is developing its own system.
The Control identified differences between national vies systems in the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic in the following areas:
In the summary reports shall indicate the value of supplies of goods to other EU member states, of the value of the services provided in the summary report not specified.
Data from summary reports submitted by the Czech payer in the CZECH republic are processed at the level of the financial authorities, where they are compared with data on supplies of goods to other EU member states referred to in the VAT returns.
The tax authorities transmit the data from the aggregate reports to the Ministry of Finance (Customs), which sends them to other EU member states.
In the SR data are from the summary report submitted by the Slovak payer of the tax authorities only transferred into electronic form and processed centrally in the Tax directorate SR (CUSTOMS).
In the CZECH republic the payer, show the value of the supply of goods and the value of the provision of services to other EU member states on separate lines of the VAT tax returns, which allows you to compare the values referred to in the summary reports with the values of the delivery of the goods according to the VAT tax returns and identify any differences.
In SR are the values of the goods and services supplied to other EU member states reported collectively on a common line of the VAT return.
As a result, in the SR system does not allow to automatically identify differences between the values of delivery of goods according to VAT tax returns and aggregate reports.
Separate reporting of the values of delivery of goods in VAT tax returns makes it possible to use the results of the comparison of data when checking the exemption of supplies of goods to the EU from VAT.
Data received from the summary report submitted to the payer in the other EU member states are treated on DUTY and compared with the value of the acquisition of goods specified payer from the CZECH republic or SLOVAKIA in the VAT returns.
In SR, these data are sent to the tax authorities and the tax authorities to decide which cases differences test.
In the CZECH republic designates the Ministry of finance (CUSTOMS), which quantified the differences between the values of the supply and acquisition of goods must tax check, and the locally competent financial authorities shall transmit the list of such cases.
This ensures that, for the most significant derogations, it will be checked whether VAT has been awarded in the correct amount when the goods are purchased.
Check further to draw attention to some problems in the system of VAT administration complications caused by the different reporting intrakomunitárních transactions (i.e., delivery and acquisition of goods made by the payer from different EU member states):
Recapitulative statements in the EU are served for each calendar quarter and the maximum time limit for processing and sending data to other EU member states is set at 3 months from the end of the relevant quarter.
The shortening of the period for which the summary report served, for one month together with the shortening of the time limits on their processing allowed early access to the data in VIES.
Thus, tax administrators could more effectively check whether VAT has been declared in the right amount in intracommunitary purchases.
At the same time, the submission of VAT tax returns and recapitulative statements for the same tax period (month) allowed faster verification of whether the payer reported in the recapitulative statement and VAT return the same value of the supply of goods to the EU.
The differences between the values of delivery of goods reported by EU payers and the values of acquisition of goods reported by Czech payers or SR were due, inter alia, to different reporting of intracommunitary delivery and acquisition data in each EU member state.
It was, for example, concerning the placing of advance payments received in the summary report, or reporting intrakomunitárních delivery in the recapitulative statement vendor in another quarter than intrakomunitárních acquisition in the VAT return of the maker.
Harmonising the conditions for reporting such data within the EU would lead to a streamlining of member states 'tax administrations' control activities.
Cooperation between the SAO, the Czech Republic and the Sao SR was also aimed at examining selected intracommunitary transactions between the two states.
Together, it was examined a total of 40 cases of commercial transactions carried out between 29 Czech and 32 Slovak tax subjects, for which there were doubts as to their realisation, or suspicion of tax evasion on VAT.
The SAO, the Czech Republic and the Sao SR have identified, among others, the following facts:
tax entities reported in their tax returns for VAT for the purpose of unlawful acquisition of an excessive deduction of VAT implementation intrakomunitárních of transactions whose execution, in fact, not;
tax entities reported intracommunitary deliveries in Carousel stores, where there was a deliberate multiple reduction in the value of supplies in order to draw excess VAT deductions;
suppliers reported in their VAT returns and recapitulative statements intracommunity supplies of goods exempt from VAT pořizovatelům, who were the so-called "lost companies" and the tax on acquired goods admit;
suppliers have made intracommunity supplies of goods exempt from VAT for tax entities not registered for VAT in another member state.
In such cases, the supply should not be exempt from VAT and should be subject to tax in the supplier's country;
suppliers reported in their tax returns for VAT intracommunity delivery in a higher value than what reported makers intracommunity acquisition, and in some cases VAT was granted in a wrong amount.
The findings of the control action show that the VIEs system provides tax authorities with the information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intracommunity transactions.
Tax administrators should pay particular attention to the rigorous examination of the differences between the data reported by VAT payers and the data in the VIES system and the use of all information in tax proceedings.
Issue of Value Added Tax after the entry of the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic into the EU
Value Added Tax
1. 5. 2004 the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic became members of the EU.
After joining the EU, internal borders and border controls on the movement of goods within the EU territory were abolished.
He was a VAT administrator until he was 30. 4. 2004 the relevant financial and / or tax office, with the exception of imports of goods and occasional bus services in the country where the tax authorities were administrators.
In connection with the adoption of the new Act No. 235/2004 Coll., on value added tax (hereinafter " Act No. 235/2004 Coll.") or act no 222/2004 Z. z., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter referred to as "law no 222/2004 Z. z.“ ) the administration of VAT on the acquisition of goods and services (formerly imports) from other EU member states from customs offices to financial or tax authorities.
Delivery of goods in the Czech Republic according to the provisions of Section 13 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll. means the transfer of the right to dispose of goods as the owner.
The delivery of the goods from the CZECH republic to another EU member state is delivery of goods which were actually dispatched or transported to another EU member state.
According to the provisions of Section 64 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll. this is an exempt taxable supplies with an entitlement to deduct VAT when the goods are delivered to a person registered for VAT in another EU member state.
For the delivery of goods in the SR according to the provisions of Section 8 of Law No. 222/2004 Z. z. it considers the delivery of tangible property, in which there is a change in the right of ownership.
For the delivery of goods is deemed to be the transfer of goods, which is owned by a taxable person from the territory of the country to another member state, if the goods are dispatched or transported, by that person or on its behalf to another member state for the purposes of its business.
According to the provisions of Section 43 of Law No. 222/2004 Z. z. is the delivery of goods from a country to another member state exempt from VAT, if the acquirer by a person identified for VAT in another member state.
The acquisition of goods from another EU member state in the Czech Republic pursuant to Section 16 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. means the acquisition of the right to dispose as owner of goods which are dispatched or transported to the customer by a person registered for VAT in another EU member state.
The Czech payer buys goods at a price without VAT and is obliged to grant VAT in the Czech Republic according to the provisions of Section 25 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll. subject to the conditions laid down in paragraph 73 of this law, he is entitled to deduct VAT.
Acquisition of goods domestically from another EU member state is in SR according to the provisions of Section 11 of law no 222/2004 Z. z. means the acquisition of the right to dispose, as owner, of movable tangible assets dispatched or transported by the supplier or the purchaser or on their behalf to the national territory of another member state.
The tax liability in the SR is incurred by the payer when acquiring goods domestically from another member state under the provisions of Section 20 of law no 222/2004 Z.z.
The payer May, according to the provisions of Section 49 of Law No. 222/2004 Z. z. deduct VAT if the tax is applied by him when acquiring goods domestically from another member state under the provisions of §§ 11 and 11a of this law.
Tripartite trade is understood according to the provisions of Section 17 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll., respectively, section 45 of Law No. 222/2004 Z. z. the store closed between three persons registered for VAT in three different EU member states, when the subject of the transaction is the delivery of the same goods between these three persons.
Intracommunitary transactions are the supply and acquisition of goods made between VAT payers from different EU member states.
The total volumes of intracommunitary transactions between the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic are shown in the table below.
VIES system
In order to control the application of the right to VAT exemption in intracommunitary supplies of goods, a system of exchange of information in the field of VAT has been established within the EU.
His part is the electronic system VIES, which allows the tax authorities of the member states of the EU to check whether the supplier was entitled to exempt the chargeable event of VAT and, conversely, whether the purchaser acquired the goods properly admitted and taxed.
The VIEs information system is not centralised within the EU.
Each member state shall develop its own vies system.
National systems work on a common principle and are interconnected through the common communication network (CCN).
In the CZECH republic was the VIES system interfaced with the automated tax information system (hereinafter referred to as "ADIS"), in the SR with the application software of the tax information system (hereinafter referred to as "APV DIS").
These systems use financial, or tax authorities as a technical support executive and management activities in the administration of taxes and fees.
International administrative cooperation
Through the international administrative cooperation of tax administration of each member country of the EU information on tax entities, which would without this cooperation has not been able to obtain alone.
The main objective of international administrative cooperation is to combat tax evasion and tax losses.
According to Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003, each member state shall set up, within the internal organisational structure, a central office in the field of administrative cooperation between EU member states in the management of VAT, the so-called Central Liaison Office.
In the CZECH republic to perform tasks arising from international cooperation, the Ministry of finance – Central financial and tax directorate, where was established the department of International cooperation in the administration of VAT (hereinafter referred to as "MF DUTY").
The duties function in the SR shall be carried out by the Tax Directorate of the Sr, the Department of international administrative cooperation (hereinafter referred to as "DR duties").
This department, inter alia, communicate with foreign administrations of the EU, in particular in the field of information exchange in the framework of the VIES, the exchange of spontaneous information and information at the request of the tax administrations of the EU, coordination of multilateral (simultaneous) tax audits, verification of tax identification numbers (hereinafter referred to as "TIN") of the persons registered for VAT in other EU member states and communicate with the European commission.
In order to verify a certain intracommunitary transaction or to obtain additional information relating to a particular tax entity, the financial and / or tax authorities shall send requests for information to the EU through MF customs or DR customs.
Through these applications, they obtain information from the requested member states which they can use for the correct determination of VAT.
Requests for information are sent mostly in electronic form between customs duties of EU member states, using a standardised SCAC form.
Selected control findings in the verification of business transactions
The cooperation of the SAO, the CZECH republic and the SAO SR was mainly focused on the examination of selected intrakomunitárních transactions carried out between the two states and further to the level of use of information obtained in the form of international cooperation, financial, or tax authorities.
The SAO, the Czech Republic requested the Sao SR to examine in 30 cases commercial transactions between 19 Czech and 25 Slovak tax entities.
The Sao SR requested the SAO, the Czech Republic to examine in 10 cases commercial transactions between 7 Slovak and 10 Czech tax entities.
The examination of intracommunitary transactions, among other things, was found:
on
The SAO, the Czech Republic asked the Sao SR to examine the procedure of the tax administrator, to which the reply to the request for information was sent.
The Slovak Tax Office requested through the SCAC form to verify the delivery of goods (footwear) in 3. quarter 2004 from Slovak payer worth 2 847 THS. Sk.
The financial office in the CR replied that the Czech payer of the said acquisition of the goods in this value in the additional tax declaration for VAT and the same goods by the end of 2004 added back to the Slovak tax subjects worth 2 550 thousand Rubles.
On the basis of international cooperation between the SAO, the Czech Republic and the Sao SR, it was found that the local tax office recognised to the Slovak supplier in its entirety the right to excess VAT deduction resulting, inter alia, from this supply.
This tax office did not provide information on the suspicion of reexport to the tax authorities locally competent customers of goods imported back from the Czech payer.
These will be an incentive to further investigate commercial activities in connection with possible carousel fraud.
on
The Czech tax administrator requested through the SCAC form to verify the delivery of the technology line to the SR worth 4 850 thousand CZK in 2. quarter 2004.
The tax procedure carried out in the SR showed that only part of the technology line was delivered, components worth CZK 3,395 thousand were not delivered.
When examining this case, the Sao SR found that the VAT on the taxable transactions carried out was the Slovak tax entity, which was awarded CZK 4,850 in the VAT return ("DAP") for the tax year 7/2004.
NKU, the CZECH republic found that the Czech payer reported for that quarter in its DAP an excessive deduction of VAT in the amount of $ 655 thousand Rubles, which was created by the application of VAT deduction from the purchase of this technological line from another domestic payer.
The Czech financial office on the basis of the results of the investigation came to the conclusion that the Czech and Slovak tax entity establish a business relationship for the purpose of unlawful acquisition of an excessive deduction of VAT, questioned the chargeable event and did not recognize the Czech payer portion of the claim for tax deduction in the amount of $ 647 thousand Rubles.
on
The Slovak tax administrator asked in 2004 through the form SCAC to check the supply of the goods (copiers) to the Czech payer in the amount of $ 24 246 ths. Sk effected in December 2002.
This product, the Slovak payer purchased in November 2002 in the SR from another tax entity worth 29 667 ths. Sk, and subsequently sold it to the Czech payer.
The Slovak tax entity applied an excessive deduction of VAT for the relevant tax period.
In the tax investigation carried out in the Czech Republic it was found that the Czech tax entity does not cooperate with the tax administrator and DAP for 4. it did not file for the quarter of 2002 or the following period.
The Sao SR found that the Slovak tax administrator had failed to recognise, on the basis of the result of the tax inspection, the claim for an excess deduction of Sk 5 541 THS applied in the DAP for the month 11/2002 and set a tax liability of Sk 1 750 THS.
At the same time, wasn't this tax entity granted exemption from VAT arising from exports of goods in December 2002.
on
The Czech tax administrator received an order from MF customs to verify the value of the Goods acquired for 3. quarter 2004.
According to data from VIES, the Czech payer should have purchased a product (thinner) worth 3 767 thousand Sk.
This tax entity, the tax administrator did not cooperate, the DAP has not filed and VAT for the months 7 to 12/2004 was assessed ex officio in the amount of $ 0.
The Czech tax administrator requested through the form SCAC to check, whether the supply of goods from SLOVAKIA to the CZECH republic took place, in what quantity and price (as per invoices).
In response, the Slovak local tax office sent a copy of the invoice, bills of lading and a call for payment of the invoice.
The Sao SR found that the Slovak payer was granted an exemption with a right to deduct VAT for that supply.
NKU, the CZECH republic found that the Czech tax administrator in response to the request for information received from the SR have been evaluated as means of proof demonstrating that the company acquired goods from another EU member state.
On the basis of further investigation, the tax office in the Czech Republic asks the superior authority to review the tax liability.
on
The Slovak company supplied goods (chipboard products), among others, to the American company which stored these goods in the Czech Republic in a free customs zone.
The operator of this free zone was indicated on the invoices as the consignee of the goods.
In 2004 the american company e.g. purchased from the Slovak payer of the chipboard tiles worth 57 600 USD (at the unit price 100 USD/piece), which placed in a free customs zone.
Subsequently, this company transferred its property rights to the goods to the swiss company, at a value of 14 $ 400 USD (unit price 25 USD/piece), and the goods were exported back to the SR.
The goods were not unloaded in the Czech Republic but left the area of the free customs zone on the same means of transport.
The Slovak tax administrator started with the supplier of goods on suspicion of revolving trades tax audits each tax period of the years 2004 and 2005.
The examination of the transactions carried out was requested with the Czech local tax administrators through several SCAC forms.
Individual responses gradually create a picture of the stores and confirmed the involvement of stakeholders from SLOVAKIA and the CZECH republic into a revolving trades.
The SAO, the Czech Republic in cooperation with the Sao SR found that there was a deliberate gradual decline in the value of the goods in these trade relations.
The tax directorate of the SR made on the basis of the information obtained, the conclusion that in this case karuselového trade, it is the free formation of prices (i.e. imports understating of the product and its overvaluation of the domestic companies, which are located in the chain between the importer and the exporter), which is not in the SR violation of the law on VAT.
In the current legislation cannot prevent the payment of excessive VAT export companies, since they fulfil all the conditions of the law on supplies exempted from VAT.
on
The Czech payer was on Day 12. 7. 2005 revoked VAT registration.
27. 10. In 2005, following a voluntary application for VAT registration, this entity again became a taxpayer.
The Czech tax entity stated in the DAP for the month of 8/2005 (i.e. the period when he was not a VAT payer) value of acquisition of goods (printing printing machine) from the SR in the amount of 1 174 ths. Czk, and apply to the right to deduct VAT.
This value corresponded to the supply of goods from the Slovak payer in the amount of 1 530 ths. Sk, which the Slovak payer stated in the DAP as delivery of goods to another EU member state with a right to deduct VAT.
The Slovak tax administrator requested to verify the delivery using the SCAC form because the Slovak supplier did not show how the goods delivered to the Czech Republic were acquired.
The Sao, CR found that the Czech payer does not cooperate with the tax administrator and does not reside at the address listed in the commercial register.
In the framework of the international exchange of information will be in the CZECH republic locally competent tax administrator performed a local investigation for the purpose of verifying data.
on

The Slovak tax administrator requested to verify these facts through the SCAC form.

Local inquiries and tax checks were not carried out with the Czech entity, its current residence is unknown.
On the basis of the international exchange of information, the Czech tax administrator learned that the Czech tax entity had become a VAT payer by accepting the service.
The Slovak tax entity shall be subject to a tax inspection for 1. up to 4. quarter 2004.

1. quarter 2004 filed DAP with high turnover at both input and output.
The locally competent tax administrator has initiated the tax proceedings, the entity with the tax administrator did not cooperate, therefore, due to the suspected involvement in karuselového trade has been assessed to VAT in the amount of $ 0.

on
The following 2 cases concern companies suspected of involvement in carousel fraud.
Transactions with goods (work clothes) were carried out between the Czech Republic and SR in 4. quarter 2004 and 1. quarter 2005.
Slovak payer No. 1 supplied goods to Czech payer No. 2.
In the Czech Republic the goods were then sold to payer No. 3, who delivered it back to SR payer No. 4 (See diagram No. 2).
And)
The Czech payer No. 2 was to be acquired by Slovak payer No. 1 at 4. quarter 2004 goods (work clothes) worth CZK 4,847 thousand and in 1. quarter 2005 goods worth CZK 17 050 thousand.
Since the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in the DAP did not correspond to the data in the VIES system, the local tax administrator sent it to the SR on 25. 5. 2005 request for information.
The Slovak tax administrator, in reply, expressed doubts about the realisation of the business cases and the implementation of payments.
8. 6. 2005 a request for information relating to goods worth Sk 16 575 thousand was received by the Slovak payer No 1 to the Czech payer No 2 in December 2004.
The Slovak side demanded to check whether the Czech payer No. 2 actually accepted the goods, admitted in the DAP and paid VAT.
From the official record, which drafted the locally competent tax administrator in the CR, it follows that the Czech payer's no. 2 for a long time do not reside at the address registered in the commercial register.
Although it was a VAT payer with a monthly tax period, the DAP filed for the quarterly tax period.
In view of this, the Czech tax administrator could not collect VAT.
Chargeable event between Slovak payer no 1 and Czech payer no. 2 referred to in the request in the amount of $ 16 575 ths. Sk was not due to the above, it is possible to verify.
The Czech tax administrator suspected the involvement of the two entities in the carousel trade in order to draw excess VAT deduction.
B)
The Czech payer no. 3, engaged in the purchase and sale of passenger cars, filed for the tax period months 1 and 2/2005 DAP, which showed a delivery of the goods (work clothes) to the Slovak payer no 4 in a total value of 21 935 thousand Rubles.
These work clothes were to be purchased by Czech payer No. 3 from Czech payer No. 2 between December 2004 and January 2005.
The local tax office sent a request for information to the SR, which was aimed in particular at verifying whether Slovak payer No. 4 acquired goods worth CZK 1 025 thousand from Czech payer No. 3 in December 2004 and in 1. quarter 2005 worth CZK 21,935.
From the responses to this request for information is received from the SR showed that in the DAP for the month of 12/2004, the Slovak payer no 4 said zero value the acquisition of goods from another EU member state and in the DAP for the months of 1 and 2/2005 said the value of acquisition of goods from another EU member state only in the amount of 1 193 ths. Sk.
The Slovak payer No 4 did not respond to the call for tax documents for the tax period 10/2004 to 3/2005.
In a local investigation carried out in SR, it was found that the company was not located at the address listed in the commercial register.
In response it was further stated that the payer complies with all the characteristics of the so-called "lost company", and therefore there is a reasonable suspicion of karuselového fraud.
The SAO SR was informed that the Slovak tax administrator sent to the DR, the DUTY impetus to perform simultaneous checks with the tax administration of the CZECH republic, which will be carried out by the participating tax entities.
In the course of the coordinated inspection, the Czech tax administrator collected documents that would confirm or deny the existence of the goods.
VAT will be measured according to the outcome of the investigation.
The case is also dealt with by the police of the Czech Republic.
Course of control action
In the preparation of parallel control actions, a coordination meeting of representatives of the SAO, the Czech Republic with representatives of the Sao SR took place in the first half of July 2005.
Participants in this meeting were familiar with the VAT legislation in both states and the integration of the VIEs electronic system into national databases.
The outcome of the negotiations was to specify the scope of cooperation and to establish the conditions for the selection of control samples.
Both sides agreed that cooperation will focus on the following areas: a) verification of the validity and correctness of the VAT number of the persons registered for VAT in the CZECH republic or SLOVAKIA in the intrakomunitárních respect of the supply; b) screening data on intrakomunitárních pořízeních referred to in the DAP payers in the CZECH republic using information from the summary report (hereinafter referred to as "SH") payers of SR contained in the VIES, and vice versa; c) the exchange of information between tax administrations in the CZECH republic and in the SLOVAK republic on the underlying commercial transactions.
It was further agreed that the selection of taxpayers for inspection will be carried out in the following volume intrakomunitárních supplies between CR and SR and by the number of requests for international cooperation sent and received between the CR and SR through the form to SCAC.
5.1 Intracommunitary transactions
The procedure for processing information by the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and SR when intracommunitary delivery and acquisition of goods is shown in the following scheme.
5.1.1 Intracommunitary delivery
If the VAT payer makes an intracommunitary delivery, he is obliged to do 25. the day after the end of the calendar quarter submit SH.
The payer in the Czech Republic provides summary information on the delivery of goods to another EU member state exempt from VAT for the previous calendar quarter.
The payer in SR is obliged to indicate to SH the value of goods that have been exempt and delivered domestically to other EU member states for the calendar quarter period.
Data on the value of the goods delivered are presented in the Czech and Slovak currencies broken down by tax entity, indicating their tin under which they were registered in their country.
Service data is not included in the SH.
If the payer in the Czech Republic finds that he has indicated incorrect data in SH, he is obliged to submit subsequent SH.
If the payer in the SR finds that the information specified in SH was incomplete or incorrect, he shall submit a corrective SH before the expiry of the time limit for filing sh, after that time limit he shall submit an additional SH.
The VIES system allows for the exchange of information on the registration data of VAT-registered payers in EU member states.
Payers from the Czech Republic or the Czech Republic may verify that the tin of the respective purchaser is registered in that EU member state.
The data from the submitted SH are on MF DUTY, or DR. DUTY system VIES grouped by TIN purchasers.
The aggregate value of all deliveries is created for each tin of the purchaser and the code of the way of filling from all his Czech and Slovak suppliers, called l1qd files.
Data from l1qd files shall be sent to the relevant EU member states no later than three months after the end of the quarter to which the data relate.
The total value of intracommunitary fillings between the Czech Republic and SR (from l1qd files) is shown in the table below.
If the VIES system in another member state detects an erroneous tin in the sent l1qd files, it shall generate a so-called o_mctl report containing all the erroneous tin indicating the type of error.
This message is subsequently sent to MF customs or DR customs.
Report O_MCTL can contain 4 types of errors: formally incorrect TIN, TIN is not in the state registered or has never been allocated, the customer with a certain TIN was not a VAT payer in a given quarter, registration for VAT, the purchaser was terminated during the quarter.
In the Czech Republic, the MF transmits customs data from the received reports ON_MCTL to the tax authorities.
If an erroneous EU payer tin is used in one of the sent lines of sh or subsequent sh, the so-called "VAT ID notification"is generated at the relevant tax office by the ADIS system.
The tax office shall examine whether to implement the supply to the payer registered for VAT in another EU member state actually occurred and recorded into the system the result of the verification.
In SR processes the DR DUTY in VIES all messages O_MCTL and electronically is sent to the locally competent tax authorities together with the identification of tax payers, who in their SH said erroneous TIN.
The tax authorities subsequently invited the payer to submit additional SH and the indication of the applicable VAT number, or tax office when reporting an invalid TIN in the filed of SH examines the delivery of the goods at the appropriate payer.
Data on the number of erroneous tins relating to intracommunitary transactions between the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic are shown in the table below.
Of the 41,728 tins of Czech payers listed in the SH Slovak payers in the period from 2. quarter 2004 to 1. quarter 2005, there were 929 erroneous tin, i.e. 2.23%.
Of the 62,997 tin companies listed in the same period, 416 were wrong tins, or 0.66 per cent.
In reporting intracommunitary transactions between the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic, Czech VAT payers reported fewer erroneous tins in their SH on average than SR payers.
In examining the activities of the financial or tax authorities, it was found that the VIES system did not provide in all cases, current information on the validity of the registration of taxpayers for VAT.
Example.:
- although at the request of the tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the VIES system confirmed the validity of the registration of the tax entity in 4. quarter 2004, the o_mctl report was subsequently generated due to the termination of the payer's registration in this quarter.
The investigation found that the termination of the marketing authorisation did not take place until 1. 1. 2005;
- The Sao Sr also found that 6 tax entities had filed an SH indicating the wrong tin, but the o_mctl reports did not contain the tin.
In the SR, The filed SH is transferred to the tax authorities in electronic form and the data from it is sent to the DR duty.
After the subsequent processing of such data in VIES, DR Will send customs duties to the relevant tax authorities so-called breakdowns of errors in SH filed by tax entities for the relevant quarters.
Sao SR compared the data on the occurrence of erroneous data in SH to 26. 7. 2005 (i.e. data processed before the start of the inspection) and 2. 2. 2006 (i.e. data processed after the end of the exercise of the control).
The data comparison contains the following table.
From the above data it is evident that the control of the SAO SR had an effect not only on the reduction in the number of SH with a wrong VAT number (an average of 199 SH for the quarter), but also on reducing the number of unpatched bugs in SH (an average of 431 errors per quarter).
In the Czech Republic, the value of intracommunitary deliveries specified by the payer in the respective DAP lines is compared to the value of intracommunitary deliveries specified by that payer in the quarterly SH.
The ADIS system automatically indicates the differences between these values.
The tax administrator should examine the differences, remove any confusion and use the data obtained in determining the tax liability.
The Sao, CR found that the audited tax authorities had not verified these differences in 27 cases.
The total difference between the sh and DAP values was CZK 537,231.
From 3. quarter 2004, the ADIS system allowed the tax administrator in the Czech Republic to consider the difference between Sh and DAP values of up to 0,5% of the total value of intracommunitary deliveries according to SH as a match and set it up in the ADIS system.
For payers with a large volume of intrakomunitárních delivery for one quarter represents 0.5 % of the value of a substantial sum, therefore, the tax authorities in those cases did not set a match SH and DAP without the elucidation of the causes of the differences.
For example, the tax administrator, without checking, set a match for the difference in values of CZK 1,561 thousand.
Examining differences in the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA was hampered by the fact that the SH for each calendar quarter submit to the payer within 25 days after the end of this quarter.
Tax administrators could not compare the intracommunitary delivery values given in these daps to those given in SH for the first two months of the calendar quarter for payers with the monthly tax period at the time of filing DAP.
In these cases, the tax administrators only became aware of any mismatches in DAP and SH when the tax liability or excess deduction of VAT was levied. rolled.
5.1.2 Intracommunitary acquisition
The VIEs system provides, inter alia, information on the values of intracommunitary transactions carried out within EU member states.
Acquisition of goods in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the received data from SH submitted by payers from other EU member states (delivered L1QD) is processed by MF customs duties.
When the processing data are converted into minimum and maximum daily currency rates of the Czech national bank for the relevant period and are then compared with the value of the acquisition referred to by the Czech payer in the DAP for the relevant quarter.
The value of the acquisition of goods declared by the payers in DAP should be within the minimum and maximum converted values of L1QD (values L1min and L1max).
If the value reported in DAP is lower than L1min, a so-called verification command is generated for payers with the most significant irregularities.
Commands to verify acquisition of goods are warning of problematic tax bodies and are passed on to the locally competent financial authorities, which must be transmitted to the data investigated.
The number of verification orders relating to the audited tax authorities in the Czech Republic is shown in the table below.
The Sao, CR found that in 33 cases the audited tax authorities did not check irregularities in the intracommunitary acquisition values referred to in the sent verification orders.
The total difference between the sh values of payers from other EU member states and the DAP of Czech payers in these cases amounted to at least CZK 148,319 thousand.
The SAO, the Czech Republic collected 533 files of tax entities for which the audited tax authorities received an order for verification from the MF customs.
Control were identified following most frequent causes of the differences between the values referred to in the DAP maker and in SH supplier: on the side of the maker (the Czech payer) in 263 cases, the acquirer did not put the acquisition of goods in a proper DAP, in 93 cases the payer admitted the acquisition of goods in another tax period other than that in which he had the obligation to declare tax, in the 6 cases reported, the person acquiring the value of the purchased goods to the wrong line of DAP, on the side of the contractor (the payer of the EU) in 88 cases, the payers of the EU into their SH include the value of services provided to the Czech payer, of the 54 cases, it was the payer of the SR, in 39 cases suppliers include the SH of delivery of the goods in a different tax period than the makers from the CZECH republic to their DAP, in 22 cases, the suppliers stated in the PS incorrect TIN of the Czech payer, in 16 cases the contractors have stated in the SH the erroneous value of the supply of goods, in 12 cases suppliers include the SH value of the goods delivered to the CZECH republic before 1. 5. 2004, in 5 cases, suppliers included in the SH the value of the received advances.
On the part of SR payers, the most frequent errors were the inclusion in SH of the value of the services provided.
54 such cases have been identified in the audited tax authorities.
For example, when investigating the verification order, it was found that the difference in the value of CZK 10 974 thousand arose by putting the Slovak payer in SH for 1. quarter 2005 provision of services (construction work and delivery of goods including Assembly in the territory of the Czech Republic).
Another reason for the differences was the inclusion of the values of advance payments received in the SH, e.g. 2 Slovak payer indicated in SH advance payments received from Czech payers, with the result that was generated by the command to verify the difference in the amount of eur 3 580 thousand Czk.
Orders to verify the purchased goods are generated only once in one quarter.
In cases where there is subsequently in the EU member states to change the data from the SH, such as the change of consumer goods in the CZECH republic or the increased value of supplies of goods to the CZECH republic, with new commands to verify the do not generate.
Due to the fact that the VIES system to these changes automatically does not alert, it may not locally relevant tax administrator the purchaser of the goods, without any other complaint about the facts decisive for the correct determination of tax obligations of the acquired goods learn and there is a great probability of the occurrence of tax evasion on VAT.
The audit of the SAO, the Czech Republic found that this situation occurred, for example, in the following cases:
The Slovakian payer listed in SH for 2. quarter 2004 value of delivery of goods for Czech payer in the amount of 1 504 THS. Sk.
1. 2. 2005 the tax office sent a request for information to the local Czech payer to the SR, since the Czech payer granted the acquisition of the goods only in the amount of CZK 425 thousand.
On the basis of the tax procedure, the Slovak payer submitted on 1. 3. 2005 additional SH, in which he corrected the data on the delivery of goods to the Czech Republic, by reducing the value of the delivery for the originally mentioned Czech payer to 538 THS. Sk and increasing the value of the delivered goods for another Czech payer from 194 THS.Sk to 1 160 THS. Sk.
Four Slovakian payers listed in their SH for 2. quarter 2004 intracommunitary delivery to payers from the Czech Republic for a total amount of 10 240 THS. Sk (i.e. 8 183 THS.CZK).
However, Czech purchasers did not declare INTRACOMMUNITARY acquisition in DAP.
On the basis of the international exchange of information it was found that the goods have been delivered in all cases other Czech payer, which wasn't in the SH submitted by the Slovak payer listed.
During 1. in the 2005 quarter, Slovakian payers increased in additional SHARES2. quarter 2004 value of intracommunitary deliveries for this Czech payer a total of 10 240 THS. Sk.
In view of the above, the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic could not have doubts as to the correctness of the data in the DAP filed for 2. quarter 2004, although the actual acquirer did not fulfil the obligation to grant intracommunitary acquisition for this quarter.
NKU, the CZECH republic found that on the basis of the international exchange of information between tax administrations was above the Czech payer additionally assessed VAT for the tax period, 5 and 6/2004 eur 3 640 thousand Czk and for the 3. quarter 2004 in the amount of 3 305 thousand CZK of goods purchased during these periods.
From the above it is apparent that the tax authorities had to in the tax procedures examine not only the differences arising from the errors in the DAP of the maker, but also differences caused by different reporting of data on intrakomunitárním delivery and acquisition in the individual member states of the EU.
Harmonising the conditions for reporting such data would make the control activities of tax administrations more efficient.
Acquisition of goods in SR
In the SR, the APV DIS system allows you to compare data on the value of purchased goods obtained through the VIES system from other EU member states with the data in the DAP of Slovak purchasers.
The method by which the data are compared is called the "min-MAX" method.
Using this method takes place the conversion of the values of supplies of goods referred to in the SH payers from other EU member states the minimum and maximum exchange rate for the relevant quarter.
A MIN-MAX interval is created, which is used for comparison with the values of acquisition of goods specified in the DAP of Slovak payers.
DR duty will send tax authorities information on intracommunitary acquisition values specified in DAP and EU delivery values in VIES.
The Tax Administrator shall decide which persons registered for VAT will be screened for the difference, taking into account other risk analysis criteria.
The SAO SR on the basis of data provided by DR. DUTY chose to controlled tax offices to control 57 the writings of Slovak purchasers of goods, of which 25 payers prefer goods from the CZECH republic, which they found the highest differences between the values of acquisition obtained from the VIES and the values registered in the DAP.
Carried out by the control of the SAO SR has confirmed the fact that the tax authorities consistently neprověřovali differences obtained using the method of MIN-MAX and didn't check so the accuracy of the data referred to in the DAP Slovak acquirers.
As part of the audit, the Sao SR asked the tax authorities to conduct 47 local investigations with specific tax entities.
In the course of the audit of the Sao SR at the tax authorities, 31 local investigations were terminated.
For Slovak companies which saw significant differences in MIN-MAX values in the acquisition of goods from EU member states, the following facts were found, inter alia:
At DAP in 4. quarter 2004 Slovak payer did not specify the value of the acquisition of goods from the EU.
The Tax Office found that the company from the Czech Republic listed in SH for 4. quarter 2004 mistakenly tin of this payer, with goods worth CZK 19,184 in fact supplied to another Slovak payer.
According to the VIES system, the Slovak company had 4. quarter 2004 acquire goods from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria worth mins 682 692 THS.Sk and MAX 715 105 THS. Sk.
This company filed a DAP for the period in which the reported value of acquisition of goods from EU in the amount of 480 599 ths. Sk.
The tax administrator performed a local investigation, while found that the taxpayer was purchasing electricity from the CZECH republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria.
Suppliers to SH and DAP did not specify the date of issue of the invoices but the date of delivery.
Due to other irregularities in the acquisition of goods from these EU states, the tax administrator will ask to check the value of the goods delivered through SCAC forms.
Acquisition of goods from EU member states in 4. quarter 2004 Slovak payer in DAP did not specify.
According to the VIES system, this payer was to acquire goods worth min 11 286 THS. Sk and MAX 11 845 THS. Sk.
The Tax Office conducted a local investigation, the inspection showed that the tax entity in 4. he did not procure any goods from EU member states in the 2004 quarter.
Sao SR advised the tax office to request a verification of the delivery of goods from EU member states through the SCAC form.
In the VIES system, the delivery of goods for the Slovak buyer was reported for mins 557 THS. Sk and MAX 565 THS. Sk.
In the DAP for the tax period of 10 to 12/2004, the payer did not report any acquisition of goods.
A local investigation by the tax administrator found that the tax entity received on 10. 12. 2004 from the supplier of the Czech Republic invoice for the material consumed in the repair of the hydraulic loader.
The Sao SR recommended that a tax inspection be carried out on the payer.
In the course of the Sao SR inspection, in 16 cases, the tax authorities did not end the local investigation.
In 10 cases, the Sao SR asked the tax administrator to carry out a tax inspection on tax entities.
Reports on the results of local investigations and tax inspections shall be submitted by the tax authorities after their implementation by the Sao SR.
For example, these cases:
The Slovak purchaser did not specify in DAP for 4. quarter 2004 acquisition of goods from EU member states and for the tax period of the months 10 to 12/2004 did not admit any tax and claimed the refund of excess VAT deduction totaling Sk 1 236 thousand.
The tax administrator performed a local investigation, which showed that the taxpayer got from the CZECH republic goods worth $ 683 thousand EUROS (about 27 080 thousand. Sk).
The goods were transported from the Czech Republic by a Czech supplier to the customs office in Čierný nad Tisa, from where the transport continued to the Russian Federation.
The Slovak payer for buyers in the Russian Federation issued an invoice for the amount of 683 thousand euros, which he did not specify in the filed DAP.
With the tax entity, the tax administrator conducts a tax inspection.

The invoices were accompanied by an export single customs declaration.
The acquisition of goods in DAP, the tax body did not include, according to the observations of the agent of the company was goods under transit are transported directly from the CZECH republic to Ukraine.
The tax entity has not submitted any VAT records to local investigations.
A tax inspection has been launched for the payer.
5.2 international exchange of level L3 information
The exchange of information at the level of L3 is initiated by the locally competent tax administrator, that its request for information (hereinafter referred to as "RFIS") or spontaneous information (hereinafter referred to as "SPI"), relating to a fiscal entity or the transaction, sent through the ministry of finance, customs DUTY, respectively.
DR duty to another EU member state. The aim of the Joi is, for example, to demonstrate the execution of a given transaction in the framework of intracommunity transactions, to check a certain tin, etc.
In the case of SPI, it is a communication of information relevant to tax authorities in another EU country.
Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003 provides for cooperation in the field of information exchange.
The maximum time limit for reply to the Joi was set in art. 8 this regulation for 3 months.
The conditions for admissibility of applications are governed by a decision of the commission of the European Communities of 15. 11. 2004, which provides that if the participating states agree otherwise, it must RFIS concern the business transactions worth at least EUR 1 500 excluding VAT.
In the case of a business transaction worth less than EUR 15 000 excluding VAT, the requested authority may refuse to reply in view of its workload.
The procedure of handling incoming RFIS tax administration of the CZECH republic including the indication of the internal time limits laid down for processing at individual to organizational levels shows the following scheme.
In SR was internally established deadline for the processing of RFIS by the tax authorities on 2 months so that it can be adhered to the three-month time limit under Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003.
MF has accepted customs duties from SR since 1. 5. 2004 to 30. 6. 2005 total 29 ŽOI and 3 SPI.
Of the 29 recruits received, 26 (i.e. 89,7 %) were settled within a 3-month period and 3 (i.e. 10,3%) were settled after that period.
During the same period, Dr duties from the Czech Republic received a total of 71 ŽOI and 7 SPI.
Of the 71 enrollees received, 64 (i.e. 90,1 %) were settled within a 3-month period, 5 (i.e. 7,0%) were settled after that period (for the remaining 2 cases it was not possible to determine the time limit from the materials submitted).

Conclusion
On the basis of international cooperation was examined compliance with the Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of VAT and on the use of VIES to the exchange of information between the member states of the EU, in particular in monitoring the application of the entitlement to exemption from VAT.
International cooperation has made it possible to examine selected intracommunitary transactions between VAT payers from the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic.
By examining the selected transactions, it was found that on the basis of the international exchange of information have revealed the tax administration of both countries, the cases of companies that made the fictional intracommunity commercial transactions in order to obtain excessive deductions of VAT and also cases where the makers not paying the VAT from the received supply of the goods in the correct amounts.
Furthermore, the checks identified differences in the processing and use of VIES data by the tax administrations of both countries.
The inspection also highlighted the problems caused by the different reporting of intracommunitary supplies and purchases of goods in each EU member state.
Harmonising the conditions for reporting such data within the EU would lead to a streamlining of member states 'tax administrations' control activities.
Clearance procedure, financial, or tax authorities in the administration of VAT and the use of VIES, it was found that the financial or tax authorities have not been using enough all the system options VIES and the relevant statutory permissions.
Furthermore, it was found that the VIES system did not provide in all cases, current information on the supply of goods and the validity of the registration of tax subjects to VAT.
The Sao SR compared the data on the occurrence of erroneous data in the SH, processed before the start of the inspection, with the data processed after the end of the inspection.
From the comparison of these data it became clear that the Sao SR control had an effect not only on reducing the number of SH with incorrectly indicated tin but also on reducing the number of unrecovered errors in SH.
In the event of irregularities in the reported data, the Sao SR asked the tax authorities to conduct local investigations or, where appropriate, to carry out tax checks.
The SAO, the Czech Republic had no such possibility under the current legislation in the Czech Republic.
The findings of the control actions showed that the VIEs system provided the tax authorities with the basic information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intracommunity transactions.
As there is still scope for tax evasion in this area, there is a need to pay increased attention to INTRACOMMUNITARY transactions when managing VAT.
Communique
This report has been prepared in Czech, English and Slovak language and signed by the president of the Supreme audit office, Czech republic and the president of the Najvyššieho kontrolného office of the Slovak republic.
Parallel control of the administration of Value Added Tax and excise duties between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Introductory word
This informational material provides an overview of the progress and results of the parallel control actions performed by the Supreme audit office and the Najvyšším kontrolným úradom S-skej of the republic, which were aimed at the area of the administration of the value-added and excise taxes.
Cooperation between the supreme audit offices of the two countries was implemented on the basis of a cooperation agreement in the control activities concluded in February 2004.
The theme of parallel control actions were selected with regard to the fact that indirect taxes are a significant contributor to the income of the state budgets of both countries.
The design of the value added tax, allowing the return of the excess deduction, provides room for tax fraud or evasion.
High excise tax rates, in particular for tobacco and tobacco products, ethyl alcohol and mineral oils, they mean a high profit for those who escape from taxation of the illegal sale of these goods.
Tax fraud is a problem not only in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, but also in other countries of the European Union.
Due to the need to address this issue comprehensively in the context of the whole of the European union the supreme audit institutions of the member countries of the European union created a working group of the VAT Working Group, to whose activities they are actively involved and miti-er control authorities of both countries.
The biggest benefit of control actions can be seen not only in the exchange of experience, but in particular in a joint effort to identify the problem areas of the administration of indirect taxes with the aim of reducing the space for tax evasion.
Obtained experience and knowledge will be utilized in the framework of planned inspections of indirect taxes, focusing primarily on the involvement of administrators of the taxes of the two states to the system VIES, allowing to control the movement of goods between member states of the European union.
Report on the results of the control of Value Added Tax Administration and excise duties for the years 2002 and 2003
1. Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 04/07 (SK) 18/2004
Subject of inspection:
(CZ) Value Added Tax and excise duty
(SK) control of the procedure of the tax administrator for the administration, control and enforcement of Value Added Tax and excise duties
11.2. 2004 was signed the Agreement on cooperation in supervisory activities between the Supreme audit office (hereinafter "SAO") and Najvyšším kontrolným úradom of the Slovak republic (hereinafter referred to as "SAO SR"). The subject of the contract was the cooperation when conducted parallel control events "value added Tax and excise taxes", included in the audit plan of the SAO for the year 2004 under no. 04/07 and "Control procedure of the administrators of dane pri administration, control and vymáhaní dan z pridanej values and spotrebních taxes", included in the audit plan of the SAO SR under no. 18/2004.
Cooperation consisted in the exchange of information to the extent provided for in the concluded treaty and in the preparation of a joint final report on the outcome of the checks.
Both parties in the treaty have undertaken to each other to provide information from public sources, from the database of the customs administration and from the files of the tax bodies conducted by the financial authorities in the Czech republic and tax authorities in the Slovak republic, which the contracting parties could not obtain in monitoring the application of value added tax and excise taxes on imports and exports from sources on the territory of the competent state.
Checks were carried out in parallel between January and August 2004.
On the territory of the Czech republic (hereinafter "CR") the audit was carried out by the department of the state budget and territorial unions of south Bohemia, northeast Bohemia, south Moravia, central Moravia and north Moravia.
Controlled persons were the General directorate of customs and 12 selected financial authorities: Financial office for Prague 1, the Financial office for Prague 3, Financial office in České Budějovice, the Financial office in Frýdek-Místek, the Financial office in Hodonín, the tax office in Jihlava, the Financial office in Kostelec nad Orlicí, the Financial office in Kroměříž, the irs in the Sand, the Financial office in the city of rožnově pod Radhoštěm, the Financial office in Ústí nad Orlicí, Financial office in velké Meziříčí.
Control on the territory of the Slovak republic (hereinafter "SR") was carried out Sections of the tax and customs administration, the SAO SR, in cooperation with the Expoziturami the SAO SR in Banská Bystrica and Kosice on 10 selected tax offices:
Daňový úrad Bratislava pre selected tax entities, the Tax office Bratislava III, the Tax office in Trnava, the Tax office Pooh-breeding, the Tax office Banská Bystrica Also, the Tax office Liptovský Mikuláš, the Tax office Žilina Also, the Tax office Žilina II, the Tax office Košice I and the Tax office Košice IV.
Objective of control
The aim of the control actions was to examine the performance of obligations of financial or tax offices and customs offices in the administration of value added tax and excise taxes, focusing on the selection of these taxes on imports and exports of goods and services.
The aim of international cooperation was the verification of imports and exports of selected commodities between the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA in the customs database of the CZECH republic and the customs database of SR and their subsequent verification in the tax returns for the relevant financial or tax offices.
The period under review was 2002 and 2003.
2. Recap of control results
2.1. General evaluation of control activities
In the framework of international cooperation, the SAO handed over the SAO SR from the customs database of the CZECH republic 22 206 items of the uniform customs declaration (hereinafter referred to as "JCD") on the imports and exports of goods between the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA and on the contrary, the SAO SR handed over the SAO from the customs database SR 30 of 221 items JCD.
A comparison was made between source-targeting items JCD from tariff database of the CZECH republic and the customs database SR.
Of the 5,883 selected JCD items from the Czech Customs database, a total of 43% of related JCD items were assigned.
Of the 12,343 selected JCD items from the SR Customs database, a total of 26% of related JCD items were assigned.
On the basis of the undistributed items JCD was on the financial or tax authorities carried out a selection of writings tax entities, which have been declared by the imports and exports subject to further verification, in cooperation with the customs administrations of the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA.
On the basis of the exchange of information from the supporting documents to the customs administrations of the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA and the financial or tax authorities was on the territory of the second state of the verified implementation reported imports and exports between the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA.
The SAO and the SAO SR carried out a joint pilot control at the border customs crossing Starý Hrozenkov - Drietoma, in which both parties closely cooperate in the verification of the correctness of the data on the movement of goods between the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA.
The inspection found deficiencies in the records of selected cases of imports and exports of goods realized in 2002.
International cooperation has allowed the examination of the business transactions between business partners from both states and pointed out the deficiencies in the registration of imports and exports.
2.2. Summary of control results
Check the SAO and the SAO SR in the field of international cooperation focused on the imports and exports of ethyl alcohol and spirits, tobacco and tobacco products, computers and computer components, mobile phones and their components, or even other types of goods.
On the basis of the writings of taxpayers to the selected financial, or tax offices, the SAO asked for verification of implementation of the exports of goods as reported on 40 JCD in the total statistical value 15 301 093 Czk and the SAO SR on the verification of the export, the statistical value of 56 989 Sk.
The SAO and Sao SR have identified, inter alia, the following facts:
- business transactions were on both sides declared the same way, which made it difficult the possibility of identifying appropriate imports and exports in the customs database of the CZECH republic and the customs database SR,
- errors in the entry of data into customs databases made it impossible to identify certain imports or exports,
- some exports from the Czech Republic have not been shown to produce adequate imports into the Czech Republic.
In these cases, there is a reasonable suspicion of fictitious exports of goods for the purpose of unauthorized application of deductions for Value Added Tax,
- tax entities did not comply with certain statutory obligations when reporting imports and exports in value added tax returns,
- in the activities of the financial or tax authorities in the administration of value added tax and excise taxes and their interaction with the customs authorities, deficiencies were identified.
In the field of value added tax and excise taxes will continue to need to pay attention to international trade in order to effectively minimize tax evasion.
In particular, it is important to improve the activity of tax administrators in the exercise of value added tax administration.
The basis of effective control of excise duties is the control of circulation of documents, a systematic physical inspection of the goods and the mutual exchange of information on import and export of goods.
3. Description of the state of Value Added Tax and excise duty
Value Added Tax
Value added tax (hereinafter "VAT") was levied by the financial or tax authorities of the taxable transactions carried out in the territory of the country and the customs authorities upon importation of the goods.
Tax revenues were due to the difference between the tax liability collected and the excess VAT deductions refunded.
VAT revenues at customs offices were determined by the amount of tax collected by them.
Tax collected by customs authorities, in accordance with the basic principles of the VAT mechanism, was reflected in the tax deductions applied to financial or tax authorities.
For most financial and tax authorities, excess deductions exceeded the tax liability.
The VAT is in terms of revenue of the state budget one of the flagship tax, since the tax revenues of the state budget of the CZECH republic in 2003, contributed about 31 % and the tax revenue of the state budget of the SR to approximately 42%.
The total VAT collection in the Czech Republic was CZK 162.9 billion in 2003.
The financial and customs authorities collected a total of CZK 394.3 billion in VAT in 2003 and the excess VAT deductions returned were CZK 231.4 billion in total.
The total VAT collection in SR amounted to SKK 83.8 billion in 2003.
In 2003, the tax and customs authorities levied CZK 187.0 billion in VAT and the excess VAT deductions refunded amounted to CZK 103.2 billion.
Excise duties
The collection of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as "SpD") was carried out by the relevant financial and / or tax authorities and on importation of products subject to SpD by customs authorities.
The SpD's share of the tax revenues of the state budget in the Czech Republic was approximately 16% in 2003 and about 19% in the Czech Republic.
Total collection of SpD selected in the CZECH republic, financial and customs authorities in the year 2003 amounted to 85,6 billion and SR achieve the above 38,0 billion Sk.
4. Course of control action
Cooperation between the SAO and the Sao SR took place in two stages.
In the first stage, a comparison was made between the imports and exports of selected commodities from customs databases in the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA, in the second stage were the results of this comparison used in the mutual verification of the implementation of selected business transactions between the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA and during the checks carried out on the territory of both states.
4.1.
Preparation of control action
The first proposal for cooperation in parallel checks on VAT and SpD was presented at the working meeting of representatives of the SAO and Sao SR in April 2003.
In November 2003, held a coordination meeting, at which it was inter alia agreed on the selection of commodities - goods, which accounted for a significant risk when compliance with customs and tax regulations: - alcohol and spirits, items of the customs tariff no. 2207 and 2208, - tobacco and tobacco products, items customs tariff heading no 2401, 2402 and 2403, - computers and computer components, items and sub-items of the customs tariff heading no 8471 and 8473 30, - mobile phones and their accessories, the subheading of the customs tariff no 8525 20 91, 8525 20 99, 8529 90 40.
Both parties agree that the selection of taxpayers for inspection will be carried out: a) from undistributed items identified by comparing the exports and imports of selected commodities between the CZECH and SLOVAK republics, b) of operators taking imports and exports regularly or once in a large volume, c) on the basis of the findings of checks carried out by the selected financial and tax authorities.
4.2. Comparison of Customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic
In the first leg was on a sample of imports and exports of selected commodities for the month of October of the year 2002 tested the mechanism of mutual matching items JCD registered in the customs databases of the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA.
Subsequently, the portion of exports from the Czech Republic was compared with imports into the SR for 2002 and vice versa for selected commodities according to the customs tariff:
- 2207 undenatured Ethyl Alcohol of an alcoholic strength by volume of 80% Vol. or more; ethyl alcohol and other spirits denatured, of any alcoholic strength,
- 2208 undenatured Ethyl Alcohol of an alcoholic strength by volume of less than 80% Vol. spirits, liqueurs and other spirit drinks,
- 2401 unprocessed tobacco; tobacco waste,
- 2402 cigars (whether or not with cut ends), cigarillos and cigarettes of tobacco or tobacco substitutes,
- 2403 other tobacco products and tobacco substitutes; homogenised or reconstituted tobacco; tobacco extracts and punishments (essences),
- 8525 20 91 transmitting apparatus containing receiving equipment: for cellular network (mobile phones),
- 8525 20 99 transmitting apparatus containing receiving equipment: other,
- 8529 90 40 parts suitable for use solely or principally with apparatus of headings 8525 to 8528.
Other: Parts of apparatus falling within subheadings 8525 10 50, 8525 20 91, 8525 20 99, 8525 40 11 and 8527 90 92.
Items JCD from tariff databases of the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA were each other are on the basis of the conformity of the individual paragraphs of JCD (e.g. the invoiced price, quantity, weight, registration number of the vehicle carrying the cargo, the date of crossing the state border, the item of the customs tariff, etc.).
The results of the comparison are presented in the following tables and charts.
The mutual mapping of individual imports and exports has made it more difficult, inter alia, the fact that commercial transactions were on both sides declared the same way.
For example, exports from the CZECH republic, declared on the single export JCD was on the territory of the SR declared on more import JCD, or should export JCD different number of items from import JCD.
Other factors that had an impact on the success of the association, was the different mix of data in the customs databases of the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA, and also the time shift between the records of exports in the customs database in one country and the records of the corresponding imports in the customs database of the other country.
The results of the comparison were used in the selection of control samples at the audited financial and / or tax authorities.
Preferably selected some of the tax entities that were imports or exports between the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA, which failed to identify in both databases.
Furthermore, to verify the commercial transactions reported in the VAT returns selected some of the tax bodies, for which there were data on imports or exports between the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA in both databases found.
4.3. Pilot control at the border customs crossing Starý Hrozenkov-Drietoma
Border customs crossing for the performance of the pilot control was selected on the basis of a joint analysis of undistributed items JCD in the tariff databases of the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA.
On the basis of a bilateral agreement between the customs authorities of the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA was from 1.6.1998 was introduced at the border customs crossing points between the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA for use of the check sheets.
The aim of this measure was to eliminate customs and tax evasion, to ensure an overview of the movement of means of transport carrying the goods of a business nature in the customs area and to create conditions for the mutual comparison of customs records.
A joint pilot check was carried out on 8 days. 3. 2004 to 26. 3. 2004 and was aimed at examining this customs control system.
Procedure for using control sheets at the border customs crossing Starý Hrozenkov-Drietoma:
1) weighing the vehicle, issuing a control sheet and passing it on to the driver.
2) weaning of the vehicle in the marked sector in the parking lot.
Customs consideration in the check-in Hall of check-in by the police of the Czech Republic, the police of the Czech Republic, the customs administration of the Czech Republic, the customs administration of the Czech Republic.
The check-in process was confirmed by stamping each component in the check sheet.
3) the addition of the vehicle to the physical inspection area.
Presentation of a control sheet, JCD, or other documents to a customs officer, where appropriate - control of the execution of all prescribed acts and documents.
Physical inspection by the relevant components.
Discharge of the vehicle from the customs area.
Pozru: when the goods were imported into the Czech Republic, the weighing of the vehicle was carried out directly by the customs officials of the Czech Republic.
When importing goods into the SR, weighing vehicles were carried out by workers authorized by the legal entity.
The vehicles were registered in computer records after consideration.

2. tax entities were selected from the Register of financial and tax authorities according to the following: (a) VAT deductions applied on importation, (b) excess VAT deductions applied, (c) SpD refund entitlement, (d) VAT exemptions applied on export,
3. tax entities for which a tax inspection has been carried out.
Sampling was carried out regardless of the country of destination with a focus on risk commodities.
