5.2.1. Checking the selected sample at the tax authorities
The Sao focused mainly on the audited tax authorities:
- the procedure of the tax authorities for verifying the correctness of the VAT declared,
- cooperation between the tax authorities and the customs administration,
- comparison of data from the customs database with JCD in the financial offices focusing on the comparison of the declared value, the application of the correct VAT rates following the customs classification of goods or services, or. comparison of data on JCD and attached invoices with data in the Customs database,
- comparison of data from VAT returns on transactions effected and received from abroad with data in the JCD database at the tax authorities or in the Customs database,
- method of verification of the right to exemption from VAT when goods or services are exported abroad,
- comparison of the volume of exports of goods or services rendered in VAT returns with data from the Customs database.
Database JCD on tax offices contained records only of those imports and exports which create tax entities the obligation to indicate the import or export to tax returns.
The tax authorities audited examined the files of tax entities which reported imports totalling CZK 60,396,379 in VAT returns in 2002 and 2003 and corresponding VAT totalling CZK 12,644,052.
In addition, the files of tax entities reporting in the tax returns for the years 2002 and 2003 were checked for exports totaling 47 323 111 thousand rubles.
Tax entities for which imports and exports between the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic were examined carried out imports into the Czech Republic from the Czech Republic in 2002 and 2003 with a total VAT base of CZK 3,759,352, VAT of CZK 767,607 and exports from the Czech Republic to the Czech Republic with a total statistical value of CZK 1,989,090.
The differences found between the records in the JCD database at the tax authorities and in the Customs database of the Czech Republic were examined as follows:
- JCD items that were missing in the Customs database of the Czech Republic were requested directly at the Directorate-General of customs of the Czech Republic,
- for JCD items that were missing from the IRS database, it was verified that they were not cancelled documents,
- for items JCD, which they found to have different values between the customs databases of the CZECH republic and databases of tax offices, it was requested at the General directorate of customs of the CZECH republic the relevant JCD in written form, including accompanying invoices.
The examination found that the JCD database did not contain, for example, records of import JCDS with a total value of VAT of CZK 3,622 thousand and records of export jcds with a total statistical value of CZK 9,359 thousand.
5.2.1.1. Differences found
By comparing the database JCD on tax offices and the accumulated tax liability for the year 2002 and year 2003 in the VAT returns for the selected sample of tax entities were detected the following differences:
Differences in values were mainly due to:
- The time shift between the implementation of imports and the claim for deduction of VAT charged on importation of goods.
A tax entity can make a claim for deduction when goods are imported within 3 years from the end of the tax period, in which the release of the goods into the appropriate mode, or in the case of temporary importation, at the latest within 3 years from the end of the tax period in which the scheme was terminated.
- The time shift between the implementation of the export and the moment when the tax entity received the JCD.
The taxpayer was obliged to provide the data on realized exports exempt from the obligation to apply the output tax to the VAT tax return for the tax period in which goods withdrawn from the territory of the country, if at the same time a tax document, which was JCD.
- Failure to fulfil the obligations of tax entities in the reporting of imports and exports in VAT returns.
In some cases, tax entities did not provide the correct data on imports and exports in their VAT returns.
Since tax entities did not have to attach JCD lists to the VAT returns filed, the control of the right to deduct VAT or the exemption from VAT by the tax authorities was made more difficult.
5.2.2. Synergies between financial and customs authorities
During the period under review, the customs authorities decided to refund or waive import or export duties and VAT.
Tax bodies has a statutory duty to reduce the previously exercised the right to deduct VAT by the amount of tax returned by the customs office, and it in the tax return for the period in which the tax was refunded.
No legislation regulated the sending of information on changes in the amount of customs duties and VAT from customs offices to tax authorities.
Some controlled financial authorities, following information received, however irregularly or with a considerable time delay and only from certain customs offices.
One IRS supervisor did not receive this information at all.
If the irs has not received information about changes in the amount of customs duties and VAT directly from the customs office, did not have available the data necessary for checking the fulfilment of the legal obligations of tax subjects.
In 2002, the customs authorities returned VAT of more than £ 319m. CZK and in 2003 in excess of CZK 398 million. CZK.
Inspection results have pointed to persistent shortcomings in the activities of tax administrators, some of the system errors in the cooperation of tax authorities with the customs authorities, and the non-performance of certain obligations of payers making tax returns to VAT and SpD.
In the management of VAT and SpD, deficiencies have been identified in particular in the following areas:
a) when you cancel registration for VAT was the fulfilment of the obligations of the payers of the payment of VAT from the business property registered, or that should be registered to the date of cancellation of registration, for which the payer has applied tax deduction, examined only sporadically,
(B) the tax authorities have not consistently made use of the possibility of carrying out a tax inspection or a local investigation.
This resulted in in some cases inadequate verification of the legitimacy of the right to deduct VAT,
(c) the official records and the oral records did not contain all the necessary data showing the legitimacy of the excess VAT deductions applied,
(d) the tax authorities have not adequately verified imports and exports declared in VAT returns.
5.3. Control findings in SR
5.3.1. Checking the selected sample at the tax authorities
For the selected sample, the Sao SR verified or carried out a tax inspection for the tax years 2002 and 2003.
After analysis of the submitted tax returns and applications for refund of the tax for the selected tax subjects the SAO SR asked the tax office about ensuring the appropriate JCD, showing import and export invoices and documents on tax payment.
Subsequently, the SAO SR to check whether they are submitted by the JCD registered in the customs database of the imports and exports and the fulfilment of the decisive facts and the legal conditions for application of the deduction of input tax from the title imports, in the refund of excess VAT, in the application of the exemption from the title of the export and during the return of the SpD.
The SAO SR on the 10 controlled tax offices to verify the selected cases of imports and exports of goods between the SR and the CR, in the structure according to the tribute items JCD and the sum of the statistical values listed in the following table.
In total, imports of a statistical value of 856,2 million were checked. Sk, representing 5,11% of the total value of imports of selected commodities from the Czech Republic to the CF.
Exports of selected commodities were checked for a total statistical value of 176 million. Sk, which represents 6,87% of the total value of exports of selected commodities from the SR to the Czech Republic.
In addition, 618 cases of imports of other goods and services (mainly white equipment, packaging equipment and software) from the EU to the SR were checked, with a total statistical value of £ 532.8 m. Acts.
5.3.2. Synergies between tax and customs authorities
The Sao SR inspection at the tax authorities found irregularities between the data registered in the Customs database of the SR and the data reported in specific VAT returns, e.g.:
- 2 tax entities (physical persons) indicated in the tax returns, imports of goods in total value of 1 589 261 Sk, on the basis of which you apply entitled to a refund of excess VAT.
During local investigations carried out on the initiative of the SAO SR tax entities have failed to prove to the irs the legitimacy of the application of input tax relevant documents on the implementation of imports and payment of VAT,
- tax entity (s. r. o.) in the tax return for the tax period January 2003 declared adopted by the chargeable event, the value 77 of 167 576 Sk, exports of goods worth 18 006 041 Sk and applied to an excessive deduction of VAT in the amount of eur 17 157 101 Sk.
Of VAT tax returns filed for the year 2003 shows that the difference between the volume of purchase and export in the value of 59 161 535 Sk, which was created in January 2003, was during the year 2003 equalized.
In the abovementioned cases, the Sao SR asked the competent tax authorities to carry out a tax inspection of the excess VAT deductions applied.
- in another case, the tax entity (s.r. o.) for the Tax Period January to June 2002 indicated in the VAT tax returns the export of goods with a total value of CZK 87 199.
The verification in the Customs database of the SR found that the tax entity carried out exports in that period at a statistical value of Sk 296 747.
The tax office repeatedly carried out the local investigation at the headquarters of the company, and found that the company director (Uk citizen) traveled and the company abandoned the leased premises without termination of the lease in August 2002.
At the time of exercising the control of the Sao Sr, the tax administrator filed a notice to law enforcement agencies on suspicion of committing a crime of non-tax evasion.
Based on the results of the inspection at the selected tax authorities, the Sao SR notes that the biggest problems in the administration and control of VAT and the SpD occurred mainly in the following areas:
- use the options to conduct a tax audit of VAT on problematic tax bodies, in particular the application of high values of the excess VAT,
- the tax inspection protocols did not contain an inventory of the documents checked
- JCD on import and export of goods,
- inadequate screening of reported imports and exports of goods in tax returns,
- lengthy management support taxes when issuing the decision, in particular in the framework of the calculation procedure, even with the demise of the law on determining penalties,
- non-compliance with statutory conditions in the provision of deferral of payment of taxes,
- NONCOMPENSATION of VAT arrears within the time limit for reimbursement of excess VAT deduction,
- inadequate use of all forms of security and recovery of tax arrears.
On the basis of the examination of the identified shortcomings, the Sao SR asked the relevant tax authorities to carry out a VAT tax inspection, focusing on the legitimacy of the excess VAT deductions applied to 14 tax entities.
On all controlled tax offices have been taken measures to eliminate control deficiencies identified, the performance of which will be the SAO SR to monitor and control.
6. Conclusion
International cooperation has allowed the examination of the business transactions between business partners from both states and pointed out the deficiencies in the registration of imports and exports.
The result of the checks was further to identify persistent deficiencies in the performance of VAT and SpD obligations, in the activities of financial and tax authorities, in the system of cooperation and exchange of information between tax and customs authorities, which ultimately reduced the efficiency and effectiveness of tax controls.
The findings also revealed that the tax authorities in the Czech Republic have basic data on imports and exports from the Czech Customs database in the tax information system. In the SR there is no similar system of transmission of information on imports and exports of goods between the Customs and tax administrations.
The procedure for verifying the exercise of VAT management and the SPD was not identical in view of the different legislation and conditions in the territory of both states.
The Sao verified the necessary data from the information obtained with the customs administration of the Czech Republic and from the documents available at the audited tax authorities. The SAO SR verified the execution of business transactions from documents taxpayers requested by the tax authorities.
In case of detection of irregularities, he asked the tax authorities to carry out tax checks.
Made to a parallel control in the field of VAT and SpD assess the status of the administration of these taxes in the period prior to the entry into the European union and pointed out the necessity of further cooperation in this area.
Mutual cooperation will further deepen in controlling the activities of the financial or tax authorities in connection with the adoption of the new VAT law.
One of the new responsibilities associated with the delivery of goods to other member states of the European union's filing of a so-called recapitulative statement.
All VAT payers who have delivered goods to another member state to a person registered for VAT in another member state must submit this report.
Tax authorities are obliged to enter data from aggregate reports into the VIEs (VAT Information Exchange System) System, to which tax authorities from the member states of the European Union have access.
Financial, or tax authorities are then able to compare these data with the data specified in the submitted VAT returns.
This system is also used to verify the validity of VAT registrants, to verify the legitimacy of the VAT exemption applied when goods are delivered to another member state and to check the proper taxation of goods.
The implementation of parallel control actions has demonstrated the possibilities of cooperation between Sao and Sao SR.
The results of these control actions will be confronted with the outputs of the upcoming control actions, which inter alia will focus on the examination of the VIES, which is to prevent tax evasion in the so-called "intrakomunitárních supply".
Given the importance of VAT and SpD for the budget revenues is the need to control activities focus primarily on the monitoring and identification of risk areas in order to limit the scope for tax evasion on indirect taxes.
Communique
This report has been prepared in Czech, English and Slovak language and signed by the vice president of the Supreme audit office and the chairman of the Najvyššieho kontrolného office of the Slovak republic.
Report on the results of checks at asylum facilities in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
State property and funds allocated to security activities of the refugee facilities Administration of the Ministry of internal affairs
The control action no. 04/23 "state Property and funds allocated to security activities of the refugee facilities Administration of the Ministry of internal affairs"
Control action no 15/2004 " control of the management of assets and financial facilities for the granting of asylum and temporary refuge of cudzincom in SR"
1. Introduction
Migration of the population belongs to phenomena that have a global character and became an integral part of the current development stage of the Czech republic and the Slovak republic.
Its cause is in particular the escape of the citizens from the country of origin or last permanent residence before persecution, in particular on grounds of racial, religious, ethnic, political, as well as from the consequences of military conflicts and ethnic cleansing.
Their goal is to obtain asylum and integration into society, especially in some of Europe's advanced democratic countries.
A large group is also formed by foreigners, whose reason for Migration is unfavorable economic and living conditions.
Migration is not a new phenomenon.
The determination of specific principles to help the refugees brought the adoption of the Geneva agreement of 1951 and new york protocol of 1967 relating to the status of refugees, whose acceptance of the governments of the signatory countries committed themselves to apply them in their foreign-policy orientation.
The Czech and Slovak Federative Republics ratified the New York protocol in 1991 and the Geneva Agreement in 1992.
The Czech republic and the Slovak republic after the split in 1993, declared its position on the refugee issue of the continuation in the implementation of adopted international documents and their binding force in the framework of the national legislation is confirmed by the legal act.
Both republics have enshrined asylum in their constitutional laws.
On the asylum process and related questions were aimed parallel checks by the Supreme audit office, Czech republic and Najvyšším kontrolným úradom of the Slovak republic, the results of which contains a common final report.
Cooperation between the supreme audit authorities of the two countries was implemented on the basis of the "Agreement on cooperation in inspection work" (hereinafter referred to as the "Agreement") closed in April 2004.
Both parties in the Treaty have undertaken to each other to provide information about the legislation governing asylum procedures in the state of the other contracting party, selected statistical data relating to the number of asylum seekers and the results of the asylum process, as well as information about the asylum facilities.
Trying to parallel control action was vytypovat identical problem areas and point out the consequences that this entails for the migration of the population.
Cooperation consisted in the unification of the programme of control actions, the exchange of information to the extent provided for in the Treaty and the drawing up of a joint final report on the outcome of the checks.
At the first joint meeting on 5.4. until 7.4.2004, the same headings of controlled issues and control procedures have been established in the preparation of control actions.
At the second meeting, which took place on 28.6. up to 30.6. 2004, the common points for the Control Action Programme have been specified.
At the third joint meeting held during the control action on 8.11. until 10.11.2004, there was an exchange of experience from ongoing checks.
Specify the forms of outputs from the controls and pre-determined structure and content of the joint final report, which was drawn up in the days of 14.2. up to 17.2. 2005 at the last joint meeting.
Checks were carried out in parallel between September 2004 and January 2005.
In the Czech Republic the inspections were carried out by the inspectors of the Department of Defense and security and selected territorial unions.
The persons controlled were the Ministry of Interior (hereinafter referred to as "MV") and the administration of refugee facilities of the Ministry of Interior (hereinafter referred to as "SUZ").
In the Slovak Republic, the Department of Defense, vnútra and štátnych úradov carried out inspections.
The audited body was the migration office of the Ministry of vnútra SR (hereinafter referred to as "MÚ").
The period under review was 2001, 2002 ,2003 (the period under review).
In some cases, the joint report also uses statistics for a longer period of time.
2. Recap of control results
2.1. Evaluation of control activities
The subject of parallel checks was: - asylum process, - asylum facilities, - management of state funds and property, - internal control system.
Mutual exchange of gained experience among the Supreme audit office, Czech republic and Najvyšším kontrolným úradom of the Slovak republic took place at the stage of preparation and implementation of the control actions.
This exchange has enabled more thoroughly evaluate the submitted documents, analyze the causes of the differences detected quality of the asylum process.
Thus, it was possible to focus on the decisive problems affecting the activity of asylum facilities.
Ultimately, this positively affected the quality of the performance of the control activity.
2.2. summary of control results
Harmonisation of asylum law in the Czech republic and the Slovak republic with documents of the European union (hereinafter "EU") was the subject of the evaluation reports of the European commission to the preparedness of both countries for accession to the EU.
The adoption of legislation governing this area continues after the entry of the two countries into the EU with a view to further harmonisation with EU law.
The number of asylum seekers in the Czech Republic increased significantly in 2001.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of applicants has a steadily increasing trend, with a significant increase in applicants in 2001.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic provide financial and material security for asylum seekers within the meaning of international agreements.
The state budget of both countries allocates the necessary funds for this purpose.
The amount of expenditure drawn from the state budget of both countries is affected especially by the number of applicants, duration of the asylum procedure the granting or refusal of asylum, and also the state of health of the applicants.
The amount of some levies collected is comparable in both countries.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic set up asylum facilities in which they gradually created suitable conditions for the stay of the parties to the asylum procedure.
Accommodation, meals, healthcare and basic material equipment and sanitary supplies are provided to asylum seekers during their stay.
At the same time, courses are organized in the framework of leisure activities, and applicants are created conditions for cultural and sports activities.
Asylum facilities include reception centres and residential centres, in the Czech Republic and integration centres.
The cost of one day of stay depends on the occupancy and amenities of the resort and is comparable in both countries.
In the Czech Republic, the capacity of asylum facilities is essentially stabilized.
In the Slovak Republic, it is expected to increase by almost 1,000 seats in the next two years.
The goal is to create conditions for the applicant, whose growing number is expected in subsequent years to continue in connection with the application of the Dublin convention.
In the Czech Republic, the highest part of the approved budget expenditure was spent on the provision of services. The crucial expenditure of this item, expenditure on accommodation and food of applicants in the asylum facilities operated on a contract basis, expenditure on health care provided to asylum seekers and the cost of a permanent security service providing protection of refuge facilities.
Salaries, payments for the work carried out and premiums also contributed significantly to the total expenditure.
In the Slovak republic were of budget management quality of migration policy and asylum process marked by the many budgetary measures that address the legitimate demands related to the increase in the number of asylum seekers.
Expenditure on Wages, Salaries and premiums, material and service expenses and expenditure on security services contributed decisively to the drawdown of current expenditure.
The results of the inspection in the Czech republic and in the Slovak republic have drawn attention to some of the similar weaknesses that had a major impact on financial management and management of state property.
It was about the shortcomings especially in the area of use of state budget funds contrary to the purpose for which they have been specified by the law on the state budget, when they were of the common expenses borne by the event having the character of technical improvements of tangible fixed assets.
The Inventory Accounting Act and the non-compliance with the accounting curriculum were also violated.
In the Czech Republic, minor deficiencies were found in the management of state property when it was left for use by another person without a contract.
Failure to comply with the deadline for reporting changes in the cadastre data violated the Land Registry Act, and leaving waste for disposal to a person who was not authorized for waste management, the Waste Act was violated.
In the Slovak republic were further identified shortcomings in the granting of disproportionately large advances on the collection of electricity and natural gas, weaknesses in procurement procedures and in the management of state property, when not sufficiently assured of his records and have not been shown the way of disposal of surplus assets.
The internal control system was ensured in the Czech republic and in the Slovak republic within the meaning of applicable generally binding legal regulations, which govern the method of implementation of financial control.
There were no deficiencies in the written documentation submitted.
The supreme audit office, Czech republic and Najvyšší kontrolný úrad Slovak republic despite some identified weaknesses, evaluates positively the procedure of RFA and MOO in the delivery of services to asylum seekers.
On the basis of the knowledge obtained in the course of inspection, the Supreme audit office, Czech republic and Najvyšší kontrolný úrad of the Slovak republic state that despite the significant increase in the number of asylum seekers in recent years the relevant departments of the two countries made the tasks associated with the care of asylum seekers at an appropriate level.
The evaluation shows that the system is functional and stable.
The results of the inspection were discussed with the interested statutory representatives of the relevant organizational bodies of the state on the Czech and Slovak sides.
Based on the results of the inspection, we recommend that positive methodological control experience be used in other joint control actions within the framework of international cooperation of the Supreme Audit Institutions.
3. Legislative framework
In the Czech republic and the Slovak republic is based on asylum law from the 1951 Geneva convention (Convention relating to the status of refugees and the associated new york protocol of 1967).
The first legislation was implemented by Act No. 498/1990 Coll. refugees.
In the Czech Republic it is from 1. 1. 2000 effective act no 325/1999 Coll. on asylum and Amending Act No. 83/1991 Coll., about the police of the Czech Republic.
This law has been amended five times in total (Act No. 2/2002 Coll., Act No. 217/2002 Coll., Act No. 320/2002 Coll., Act No. 519/2002 Coll. and act no 222/2003 Coll.).
Two more amendments to Act No. 325/1999 Coll are currently in the legislative process. asylum, and the adoption of other amendments will be bound to European legislation.
At the time of the formation of Law No. 325/1999 Coll. for asylum, the asylum area was part 3. EU pillars and asylum documents were political documents in terms of binding force.
Already in the framework of the adoption of this law, efforts have been made to make it as compatible as possible with EU law.
A significant change for asylum policy within the EU was the transfer of the asylum issue from 3. 1. pillars where asylum law has become part of community law since 1.5. 1999 under the Treaty of Amsterdam.
This shift caused the need to create appropriate legislation, i.e. to create legal instruments in the corresponding legal commitment.
The compatibility of Czech asylum law with EU documents has been the subject of regular European Commission evaluation reports.
Key community rules on asylum were adopted shortly before or after the Czech Republic's entry into the EU and their transposition period at the time of control of the Supreme Audit Office has not yet expired.
Once they are implemented into the Czech legal order, the Czech Republic will be obliged to notify the European Commission of the transposition.
In the Slovak republic the procedure of state bodies in the proceedings for refugee status and determine the duties of aliens who applied for refugee status or who was granted temporary asylum in the territory of the Slovak republic, established with effect from 1.1.1996, the law of the National council of the Slovak republic no. 283/1995 Of. z. the refugee.
Since 2003, the Refugee Act has been replaced by Law No. 480/2002 Z. of " asylum and amending and supplementing certain laws incorporating the harmonisation of the legislation of the Slovak Republic with council of Europe directive 2001/55 / EC of 20. 7. 2001 on minimum standards for giving temporary protection in the event of a mass influx of displaced persons and on measures to promote a balance of efforts between member states in receiving such persons and endure the resulting consequences.
After two amendments to Law No. 480/2002 of the z., asylum, in 2003 and 2004, a third amendment was approved at the beginning of 2005, which entails further harmonisation of the law of the Slovak Republic with EU legislation on migration and asylum.
Its major elements are, for example, the determination of responsibilities for asylum seekers to attend for the duration of the stay in the integration centre course on the basics of the Slovak language, appointment of guardian courts for underage foreigners, if present on the territory of the Slovak republic without a legal representative, allowing applicants to enter into an employment relationship under certain circumstances, referred to in the amendment to the act.
Harmonisation of the law of the Slovak republic with EU law in the area of migration and asylum process was evaluated in regular reports to the European commission on the preparedness for the entry of the Slovak republic into the EU.
In 2002, the report highlighted the MU's lack of personnel capacity, which did not correspond to the increased number of asylum seekers.
4. Asylum process
In the Czech Republic since 1990, matters relating to refugees fall under the competence of the MV.
Effective from 1. 1. 1996 established the MV organizational branch of the state of SUZ. The reason was the separation of the performance of state administration in the field of asylum procedures, which is exercised through the department of asylum and migration policies MV, from the delivery of services to applicants for asylum.
SUZ's task is to provide accommodation, catering, health and other services to asylum seekers and asylum seekers for the MV.
In the Slovak republic performs the critical tasks in the field of asylum process of the MOO, and in particular in terms of financial and material-technical security of the asylum process to the extent defined by special regulations.
Priority tasks are issues related to the decision-making of asylum applications by foreigners in I. degree of administrative management and comprehensive operation of refuges in the field of accommodation, catering, health, financial and material security of applicants for asylum.
In addition, it prepares concepts for the migration policy of the state.
The results achieved in the area of the creation of the asylum system in the Slovak republic in recent years, significantly affected the cooperation and support from the Office of the UN High commissioner for refugees (hereinafter "UNHCR").
A particular benefit was his financial contribution to the reconstruction of the housing fund for asylum seekers.
The UNHCR has also co-financed social, cultural and sporting activities for applicants.
4.1. evolution of the number of asylum seekers and the results of the asylum process
The development of the number of asylum seekers in the Czech Republic is shown in the graph.
A significant increase occurred in 2001 due to the kosovo crisis and in 2003 reected the increased number of refugees from Chechnya.
An overview of the results of the asylum procedure in the Czech Republic is given in Table 1.
A total of 394 cases were granted asylum during the period under review, including 83 in 2001, 103 in 2002 and 208 in 2003.
A total of 22,731 cases were not granted asylum during the period under review and 22,636 cases were terminated.
Number of parties at 1.1. includes how a person, whom has not yet issued a decision, so you, which decision was not passed.
Furthermore there are included persons who have been excused from the missed period for appeal, or which was the previous decision is revoked and has not yet been exposed to the new.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of asylum seekers has a steadily growing trend.
If 96 applicants were registered in 1993, in 2003 it was already 10 358 people.
There was a significant increase in the number of applicants in 2001, when 8,131 applicants were registered, an increase of 423% compared to 2000, in which 1,556 people applied for asylum.
Data on the results of the asylum procedure in the Slovak Republic during the period under review are given in Table 2.
A total of 49 asylum seekers were granted during the period under review and their number did not exceed 0,22% of the registered number of applicants in each year.
Asylum was not granted in 860 cases.
The asylum procedure was halted in a total of 23,088 cases.
The bulk of the applicants, by staying outside the asylum facility without permission, voluntarily left the asylum procedure before its termination.
In 2002 it was more than 82% of the total number of registered applicants and in 2003, about more than 94% of persons.
The length of residence of one applicant in one of the asylum facility based on the average number of days was 13 days in 2001, 18 days in 2002, and 19 days in 2003.
From the findings WE also show that for the majority of applicants entering into the asylum procedure in the Slovak republic regards the search for better living conditions, i.e. the so-called economic migration, which is not reflected in the documents adopted by the international community, to which they applied and the Slovak republic.
In these cases, the asylum system is used for the purpose of the applicant.
An application for asylum based on economic reasons, such as finding employment or better living conditions, is not a reason for granting asylum.
Such an application should be under the provisions of § 12 ods. Point 1 (a) Act no 480/2002 Z. z. asylum seekers are assessed as manifestly unfounded and should be decided within 30 days.
Not yet formed the internationally recognized principles to identify the economic migrants, which would distinguish them from the applicants persecuted in their country of origin and which would allow to speed up the asylum process.
In view of the above it can be concluded that the Slovak republic is in terms of international migration, transit countries and target countries of migration were and remain the western european states.
The Czech republic and the Slovak republic after accession to the EU acceded to the Agreement determining the state responsible for examining applications for asylum lodged in one of the member states of the European communities (the Dublin convention).
The convention prevents multiple special-purpose applications for asylum in multiple EU states.
Applicants return to the country of first registration after positive identification in EURODAC.
The Slovak republic is a part of the exterior border of the EU countries, therefore, the application of the Dublin convention may have in the next period resulted in an increase in the number of applicants, which will be needed to create the conditions for residence in the Slovak republic until the decision of granting or not granting asylum.
4.2 drawdown of funds
The Czech republic and the Slovak republic are obliged in terms of international agreements and resulting national legislation to provide financial and material security of applicants for asylum.
The state budget of both countries allocates the necessary funds for this purpose.
The amount of expenditure drawn from the state budget is affected primarily by the number of applicants, duration of the asylum procedure until the final decision on the granting of asylum and also their state of health.
A growing number of people entering the asylum process has a direct impact on the higher drawdown the statutory allowances for the applicant, such as living expenses, pocket money, spending on the basic material, equipment, other material equipment and other social contributions.
The amount of some levies collected is comparable in both countries.
In the Czech Republic, during the controlled period, meals were CZK 58 per person per day, pocket money CZK 12 per person per day and CZK 6 per child under 15 years of age.
The cost of one asylum seeker per day of stay was on average CZK 351 in 2001, CZK 383 in 2002 and CZK 345 in 2003.
Outside allowances, asylum seekers staying in self-cooking resorts and those staying privately outside asylum facilities may be granted a contribution up to the subsistence minimum.
Act no 325/1999 Coll., on asylum, as amended, inter alia, admits in section 84 of the municipalities entitled to a contribution to cover the costs incurred in connection with the asylum facility in its territory.
The amount of the contribution was determined annually by the government's resolutions and during the period under review was CZK 7 per person and stay Day.
At the same time, municipalities are granted the right to a contribution to cover the non-investment costs of primary schools attended by asylum seekers.
The amount of the contribution was in a controlled period of 120 Czk per student and month, provided, that in any given month the attended the school for at least 10 days.
In the Slovak republic was in a controlled period of subsistence 70 Sk per person per day, an allowance of 12 Sk per person per day and 8 Sk on a child under 15 years of age.
The cost of one asylum seeker for one residential day were on average 442 Sk in 2001, 447 Sk in 2002 and 445 Sk in 2003.
The municipalities on whose territory the asylum facility is located comply with law no 480/2002 Z. z. about azyle, a contribution to partially cover the expenses that the village incurs in connection with the establishment and operation of the asylum facility.
So far, municipalities have only partially benefited from the possibility of applying for a contribution, which is set at Sk 1 500 per bed and calendar year.
National legislation in both countries for the issue of a decision on the asylum sets 90-day deadline from the start of the asylum proceedings, and at the same time admits, in justified cases, extend this period.
The most common reason for the extension of the asylum proceedings, which affects the amount of state budget expenditures, filing legal remedies against decisions on refusal of asylum.
In the Czech Republic, the highest number of final decisions were issued between 90 and 180 days (31.54%).
The second highest number was within 90 days of the date of application for asylum (17,61%).
In total, 73% of asylum procedures launched in 2001-2003 were finally decided within one year of their initiation.
Within two years of the opening of the procedure for granting asylum, 92% of asylum applications were final.
In the Slovak Republic, up to 90% of applicants who have not been granted asylum use the legal option of extending the period by bringing an appeal to court, according to MÚ data.
In some cases, extend for more than a year and the time of the power control were not proceedings in the court ended.
Some benefit in shortening the asylum procedure is expected from the establishment of joint departments of the MUNICIPAL and the Office of the hraničnej and cudzineckej police Policajného zboru in reception centres in Adam's-Gbeloch, Opatovskej New Village and in the Liptov Vlachoch, to which it acceded at the time of the exercise of control from 1.10.2004.
This is intended to simplify procedures and reduce the time limits for procedures between the two elements of the asylum process.
5. Asylum facilities
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic set up asylum facilities in which they gradually created appropriate conditions for the provision of services to asylum seekers.
Accommodation, meals, healthcare, pocket money and basic material equipment and sanitary supplies are provided to asylum seekers during their stay.
At the same time, there are courses organized in the framework of leisure activities and applicants are created conditions for cultural and sports activities.
5.1 asylum facilities in the Czech Republic
The RFA manages and operates asylum facilities and is competent to manage state property in the grounds of the reception centre Vyšní Lhota, the admissions and residential centre Červený Újezd, residential centres Bělá-Jezová detention centre, a Stop at Brno, Kostelec nad Orlicí, Havířov, and in the objects of the integration asylum centres Jaroměř and Stop at Brno.
In early 2002, a reception centre was set up in transit prostom Prague-Ruzyne airport.
The RFA further ensures the operation of the asylum facility in Guard pod Ralskem, Patch, Bruntál, Zbysov and Kašavě, which are operated by a legal person on the basis of § 80 para. 3 of Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on asylum.
The total accommodation capacity of reception centres is 747 sites and the total accommodation capacity of residential centers is 1 of 977 seats.
Reception centres are closed facilities, which allowed asylum seekers to leave the pending implementation of the prescribed medical examination and basic receiving operations referred to in the act no. 325/1999 Sb. asylum seekers.
Violation of the obligation to reside in the reception center is assessed as an offense.
The residential centres to which asylum seekers come from reception centres are used to accommodate asylum seekers until the decision on their application for or not to grant asylum becomes legal.
Under certain conditions, asylum seekers are allowed to leave the resorts or reside in private.
Applicants for asylum are in reception and accommodation centres in which they are residing, the right to free accommodation, providing meals, other services and pocket money provided that the bore acts necessary to determine their financial and property ratios, and these ratios are such that from them can not be fair to ask for or partial payment of the listed services.
Integration asylum centres are used for temporary accommodation of persons who have been granted asylum.
Clients are at the centre accommodated on the basis of the accommodation contract, which is normally closed for 6 months with possibility of extension until is for them to manage to ensure adequate housing, or to ensure themselves in the framework of the state integration programme.
At the Integration Center, clients pay all the costs of accommodation and eat individually.
Persons with recognised refugee status have the same rights and obligations as Czech citizens, and have the same access to social security.
5.1.1. costs of asylum facilities
For comparison of asylum facilities, it was chosen as the best indicator of the amount of the cost of one physical stay Day.
It is based on the de facto number of persons who have actually been provided with services provided by asylum facilities on a daily basis.
In Table 3 and in the chart, Suz-operated facilities are designated as own and those operated by legal entities pursuant to Section 80 of Act No. 325/1999 Coll. asylum, as contractual.
The cost of a one-day stay at its own asylum facility operated by SUZ is falling as these facilities become increasingly crowded. The reason is that the fixed cost of running the premises is budgeted for more asylum seekers.
The amount of total costs incurred to provide services for asylum seekers is directly proportional to their increasing number.
In 2001 and 2003, asylum seekers were accommodated in crisis capacity in their own asylum facilities.
In the year 2003 was even to address the capacity crisis refuges, caused by the mass arrival of asylum seekers of chechen nationality of Poland, used the emergency accommodation capacity in residential containers (total 320 beds).
This capacity was provided by renting 80 residential and 6 sanitary containers.
The expenditure per applicant per day of stay was then lower in those years.
However, long-term maintenance of high fulfillment of these devices is not possible.
Account should be taken of the risks of an unexpected influx of refugees and The Associated requirement for the need for higher accommodation capacity.
At the same time, it is not possible to carry out some repairs, maintenance and investments with fully occupied accommodation capacity.
Form of shelter facilities operated by contracted allows, if necessary, the adoption of operational solutions in the field of capacities of refuges.
5.2 asylum facilities in the Slovak Republic
Asylum facilities are reception centers and residence centers.
The MÚ has in its administration reception centers Adamov-Gbely, Cornovce, Opatovská Nová Ves and the residence Center Brezová under Bradlom.
The total capacity of the reception centers is 470 seats, and the Residential Center is 100 seats.
A growing number of asylum seekers dealt with MOO the establishment of the residential centre in Gabčíkově in the leased premises of the Slovak technical university in Bratislava with a flexible disposable capacity from 250 to 940 jobs.
According to the concluded contract, the lease also provides for the provision of services related to the operation of the center.
In this form, the MU addressed the lack of its own staff.
The residential centre was also temporarily established in 2002 and 2003 in rented premises in Jazierciach with a capacity of 160 seats.
Reception centres had occupancy between 57% and 62% on average during the controlled period, while residential centres were between 33% and 50% on average.
Occupancy varied by season and was highest in the last months of the year, when he applied for asylum on the much larger number of applicants compared with other months of the year.
Further increase of accommodation capacity of about 450 seats will be possible after reconstruction of resorts in Opatovský nový Vsi and Vlachoch.
After the construction of the resort in Humennom in 2006, the number of seats will increase by another 550 people.
5.2.1. costs of asylum facilities
Data on the amount of the cost of operating asylum facilities are given in Table 4.
From their analysis it follows that the operation of the asylum facility by another entity, which will provide premises and ensure operation of the equipment, including related activities, is one of the options, how to secure a reasonable cost basis tasks resulting from the stay of applicants for asylum in the Slovak republic.
6. Management of state funds and assets
6.1 management analysis
In the Czech Republic, the approved budget expenditure of SUZ was increased by CZK 103,077 by 13 budget measures in 2001.
Of which 89 979 thousand rubles (87,29%) were assigned funds. The bulk was intended to address the consequences of the Kosovo crisis (CZK 44,538) and to provide healthcare to asylum seekers (CZK 38,870).
In 2002, SUZ's expenditure was increased by CZK 88,362.
Of these, CZK 62,282 (70,48%) were assigned funds, the bulk of which (CZK 53,200) was intended for healthcare provided to asylum seekers.
In 2003, SUZ expenditure was increased by a total of CZK 88,078 by fourteen budget measures.
Of which CZK 82,000 (93.09%) was assigned funds released from the general treasury.
The amount of CZK 51,000 was allocated to the health care provided to asylum seekers, CZK 24,000 to deal with the influx of Chechen refugees and CZK 7,000 to the humanitarian evacuation programme for the disabled people of the Republic of Iraq.
An overview of the drawdown of Suz expenditure collected during the audited period is given in Table 5.
From the above review it becomes clear that the highest part of the expenditure was spent on providing services.
The amount of expenditure spent on the purchase of services ranged from 37.07% to 38.23% of total expenditure.
Rozhorlujícími expenditure in this item, expenditure for accommodation and food of applicants in the asylum facilities operated on a contract basis, expenses for the medical care provided to asylum seekers and the cost of a permanent security service to ensuring security in the various asylum centres.
Salaries, payments for work done and insurance premiums (23.99% - 24.97%) contributed significantly to SUZ's total expenditure.
Last but not least, purchases of material (around 14%) contributed significantly to SUZ's total expenditure, with food purchases (7.61 % ? 9,83% of total expenditure).
In the Slovak republic was the budgetary management of the MUNICIPAL security migration policy and asylum process marked more by the budgetary measures that address the legitimate demands related to the increase in the number of asylum seekers.
For the proposal and a breakdown of the budget in the expenditure section was especially in the years 2001 and 2002 characterised by an imbalance between the demands of the MOO, which were based on the increase in the number of applicants for asylum and of the financing needs of their statutory claims, and provided resources primarily in the main category of current expenditure.
The manager of the budget chapter addressed disproportion over the course of the year with multiple budgetary measures, increasing the current expenditure limit by 41,8% in 2001 and up to 71,7% in 2002.
An overview of the drawdown of the expenditure collected by the MOA during the audited period is given in Table 6.
Expenditure on Wages, Salaries and premiums ranged from 24.47% to 30.51% and expenditure on materials and services ranged from 21.04% to 38.82% of total expenditure.
Spending on security services accounted for more than 10 per cent, and from 3.92 per cent to 7.20 per cent, spending on food purchases.
Spending on accommodation and catering services accounted for another significant proportion, ranging from 10.82% to 26.96%.
Capital expenditure accounted for a relatively low share in the range from 1.03% to 6.25%.
6.2 deficiencies identified
The results of the inspection in the Czech republic and the Slovak republic have pointed to some similar deficiencies, which did not have a major impact on the management of funds and property of the state.
It was about the shortcomings in particular in the following areas: a) the use of state budget funds in contravention with the purpose for which they were intended by the law on the state budget, when they were of the common expenses borne by the event having the character of technical improvements of tangible fixed assets; b) violation of the act on accounting in the field of inventories and in non-indicative chart of accounts.
In the Czech Republic, minor deficiencies were found in the management of state property, when it was left for use by another person without a proper contract; failure to comply with the deadline for reporting changes in cadastre data violated the Land Registry Act; leaving waste for disposal to a person who was not authorized to waste was violated the Waste Act.
In the Slovak republic were further identified shortcomings in the granting of disproportionately large advances on the collection of electricity and natural gas, weaknesses in procurement procedures and in the management of state property, when not sufficiently assured of his records and have not been shown the way of disposal of surplus assets.
7. Internal control system
In the Czech Republic he was at SUZ on 1.7. 2002 introduced an internal control system within the meaning of law no 320/2001 Coll., financial control, defining the competences of the individual employees responsible for conducting preliminary, interim and subsequent checks.
At the same time, an internal audit system was introduced and an internal Suz auditor was appointed.
Each year the RFA published the plan of financial, social and operational and technical controls aimed at comprehensive verification of finances and the property of the state in the various asylum centres managed by the RFA.
In 2002, 42 management checks were carried out and 54 were carried out in 2003.
In the Slovak republic direct the performance of audit work in departments and organizations of the Ministry of interior of the Slovak republic from the point of view of compliance with the generally binding legal regulations and internal regulations ensures the Office of the control of the minister.
During the period under scrutiny, the performance of tasks in the asylum policy section was not checked.
The internal control system of the MU is mainly aimed at carrying out preliminary and ongoing financial control under law no 502/2001 Z. z. about financial control and vnutornom audite.
The exercise of financial control is also regulated by the internal rules of the director of the MOA.
The substantive focus of the control activities as part of the management of the various departments was established under the annual mo plan.
Responsible for the performance of control in this area were appointed directors of unions.
According to the written documentation submitted, there were no deficiencies.
Since the period of application of the Order of the Ministry of internal affairs of the Slovak Republic No. 28 of 23. 4. 2004 is obliged to handle and investigate complaints under the complaints act.
Organizational security of this task will need to be resolved in the near term.
Communique
This report has been prepared in Czech, English and Slovak language and signed by the vice president of the Supreme audit office and the chairman of the Najvyššieho kontrolného office of the Slovak republic.
Joint report on parallel checks on expenditure on the construction of the Prague – Dresden motorway
Introductory word
Without the existence of trans-European transport networks, a modern, dynamic and, above all, united Europe would be hard to imagine.
Quality transport networks are a necessary condition for maintaining and increasing the standard of living of Europeans.
Creating the conditions for rapid, secure, reliable and cheap transportation of persons and costs is an important task for the state administration.
It is a very demanding task, both organizational and technical, and financially.
European efforts for sustainable mobility often and hardly seek compromises with Europe's interest in maintaining a healthy and Human Environment.
Construction of transport infrastructure, even through the necessary measures for the benefit of the environment, is financially demanding.
Considered the procedures and decisions of the state administration in the preparation and acquisition of the road construction may bring significant savings of public financial resources, which can be for the benefit of citizens to use otherwise.
One of the tasks of audit institutions is to actively search for flaws, which led to a lower than achievable economy, efficiency and effectiveness of expenditure on the construction of transport infrastructure.
Audit institutions should not only highlight the identified shortcomings, but recommend measures that will lead to improvements in the state, for the benefit of the Citizens, for the benefit of Europe.
Short summary
Two of the supreme audit institution of the Federal republic of Germany and the Czech republic (hereinafter referred to as GERMANY and the CZECH republic) Bundesrechnungshof (hereinafter referred to as "BRH") and the Supreme audit office (hereinafter "SAO") carried out in 2005 and 2006, parallel control of expenditure on the construction of the motorway Prague – Dresden (highway D 8 in the CZECH republic and the highway And 17 in GERMANY).
The highways are connected by a border bridge, which is co-financed by both countries.
Thanks to cooperation with the Sao, BRH was able to conduct a thorough check on the effectiveness of the funds spent on the construction of the border bridge.
On the basis of close cooperation with the BRH, the Sao obtained the necessary data on the amount of German costs for bridges and tunnels for comparative purposes.
The Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany concluded a contract for the construction of the border bridge in 2000.
According to the construction process, the completion date was finally scheduled for the end of 2006.
However, during the award of the contract, the Directorate of roads and motorways of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "RSD") made errors that led to an extension of the competition period and a shortening of the construction time.
Thus, the contract with the contractor was signed later than expected.
The contractor agreed to build the bridge in a shorter time and ensure its completion in 2006.
As a result, however, the RSD had to accept a significant increase in the price of the bridge.
In the context of joint inspection of the work compared the prices of bridges on the highways D 8 and 17, and on the basis of per m2 area of bridge construction.
Statistical analysis of prices made it possible to identify bridges with high cost per m2 of area.
Analysis revealed that the border bridge was the most expensive bridge in a group of large bridges with a length of over 100 meters.
The price increase could also be attributed to the delay that occurred during the procurement procedure.
When analyzing the cost of building tunnels, inspectors found that the prices of tunnels on Highway D 8 are significantly higher than those of comparable tunnels in Germany.
The BRH and the Sao now have a database of prices for bridges and tunnels on which they will be able to rely in future efficiency checks of the means used for transport infrastructure purposes.
To the construction of bridges the two control institutions recommend: the standardization of the construction of bridges and the use of composite steel-concrete and special structures only in cases when they are not prestressed reinforced concrete bridges adequate.
Among the main signs of cooperation was her team spirit and informality.
In the course of parallel control, the controllers participated in their specific knowledge and skills.
Introduction
This report informs on the progress and results of the parallel controls of the funds spent on the construction of the highway connecting Dresden and Prague (D 8 in the CZECH republic and 17 in GERMANY).
The checks were aimed at the economy, efficiency and effectiveness of the expenditure incurred.
Parallel checks were carried out by the BRH in Germany and the SAO in the Czech Republic.
Parallel checks took place in 2005 and 2006.
NKU controlled the economy, efficiency and effectiveness of expenditure in the amount of approximately 20 billion Rubles including VAT (approximately € 690 million €) on the border section of the highway D 8, which has a number 0807.
Of this amount, € 64 million from European funds (ISPA) was to be used as planned.
In addition to the parallel inspection carried out together with the Sao, BRH checked the preparation and construction of the highway a 17 in 2003 and 2005.
The funds spent on the construction of all three sections of the highway and 17 amounted to around € 670 million, of which € 277 million will be co-financed by European funds (EFRE).
The highway from Prague to Dresden is part of the Trans-European Transport Corridor IV. Dresden – central and southern part of Eastern Europe-Istanbul.
Highway D 8 runs from Prague through the mouth above the Elbe at the state border.
Highway a 17 runs from the state border of the Czech Republic/Germany to Dresden.
At the time of the inspection, the border sections of both highways were under construction.
These sections were put into operation 21. December 2006.
On the German side is so of the highway completed to Dresden, while on the Czech side of the highway D 8 finished not, because of section no. 0805 in the length of 16,4 km through the Czech central mountains between Řehlovicemi and Lovosicemi is still in the preparatory stage.
Under the plan section no. 0805 between Prague and Ústí nad Labem browse the protected landscape area České středohoří.
According to the projections made in the CZECH republic in 2001 should be in 2008 at the border section no. 0807 highway D 8 the intensity of the operation 22 940 vehicles per day.
According to German forecasts, in 2010 the intensity of traffic at the Czech border will be about 25 000 vehicles per day.
GERMANY and the CZECH republic have concluded in the year 2000, the Treaty between the Federal republic of Germany and the Czech republic, linking the German highway And 17 and the Czech motorway D 8 on the common state border through the construction of the frontier bridge.
On the construction of the bridge involved in both states, therefore, was to control the construction of this bridge, an important aspect of parallel controls carried out by the two audit institutions.
Cooperation between the BRH and the Sao
Since mid-2005, the two Supreme Audit Institutions have negotiated close cooperation in the control of the construction of the motorway connecting Prague and Dresden.
Both sides had serious reasons for such cooperation:
1.
Germany is financially involved in the construction of the border bridge.
Its planning and construction rests on HSD.
Therefore, the BRH itself did not have the opportunity to conduct a check on this construction project.
2.
The Sao did not have the comparative database needed to assess whether the funds were used economically in relation to the overall cost level of bridges and tunnels on D 8.
3.
NKU needed to make sure about the effectiveness of the expenditure, taking into account the main technical parameters of the highway, in particular the arrangement of the bridges and tunnels that would be on both sides of the border should allow the same ride quality.
After the preparatory negotiations was on 4. January 2006 signed by the presidents of both supreme audit institutions agreement on coordinated inspection of Highway D 8 / a 17.
The joint working meetings of the BRH and Sao controllers took place throughout 2006 at an interval of approximately six to eight weeks.
The negotiations will address the current problems and challenges, in particular the preparation of a uniform methodology to control prices of bridges and tunnels, exchange findings from the inspections of the construction of the frontier bridge and the preparation of joint reports.
An important feature of cooperation was the ongoing exchange of information.
While BRH was doing most of the work on the comparison of the technical parameters of bridges and tunnels and the procurement procedure, the SAO for the most part prepared a methodology to control prices of bridges and tunnels.
The applicable legal standards for control in the state administration differ in the way in which control actions are concluded in both countries.
For these reasons, both the supreme audit institutions draw up their own inspection conclusions about their findings obtained during their inspections.
This report reflects the results achieved in parallel controls.
The cooperation will be completed by signing the final communiqué in the first half of 2007.
Construction of the border bridge
The Czech republic and the Federal republic of Germany in the treaty of 2000, agreed on the date of completion of the construction of the frontier bridge referred to options in 2005.
The two sides then agreed to postpone that deadline until the end of 2006.
As an investor, HSD worked.
Germany is financially involved in the construction of the bridge from 42.13 %.
In the period up to 1999, the RSD proposed that the border bridge should have a pre-tensioned reinforced concrete structure.
In 1999, in agreement with its partners in Germany, the CSD agreed to a coupled steel-concrete structure.
This decision was justified by a reduction in the number of double pillars from seven to five and the subsequent environmental benefit of such a solution for the valley.
In addition, the comparative calculations made by HSD indicated that the coupled steel-concrete structure should be a less expensive option.
But there was a mistake in the calculations.
It said The New coupled steel-concrete structure would be only 397 m long.
In fact, it is 5% longer.
During the award of the border bridge contract, RSD made serious errors.
Prepared custom documentation that would adequately describe the assessment criteria and sub-criteria for comparing tenders.
This error led to the assessment and Evaluation Commission and the director-general evaluating tenders in a subjectively and problematic manner.
The unsuccessful bidder challenged the results of the procurement procedure.
The subsequent investigation by the competition authority led to the conclusion that the contract for the award of the construction contract was signed later than initially calculated.
This meant that the summer construction season 2004 after the evaluation of the offers was wasted and the time reserved for construction was shortened.
The construction company agreed to build the bridge in less time, but at the cost of a substantial increase in costs.
The offered procedure included a double installation of the bridge upper, a change in the design of the pillars and the establishment and equipment of the mounting premises.
In addition, the construction company was not able to acquire the originally designed type of steel within the necessary deadline.
A new type of steel – for a higher price by about 4 million €, that had to fully pay the RMD – enabled shortening the period for execution of corrosion protection, which subsequently reduced the total time of the construction of the frontier bridge.
Compared to the net price of € 18,3 million offered in the tender, the total cost of the construction of the border bridge as a result of the accelerated procedure and other financing adjustments will increase considerably.
The reduced time reserved for construction work led to a price increase of about €5.9 million.
At present, the net cost is around € 25.9 million, without taking into account automatic price increases (as of October 2006).
Comparison of bridge and tunnel prices
Both the supreme audit institutions carry out an analysis of the prices of bridges on the highways D 8 and 17 in order to identify bridges whose price was too high, and compare prices of bridges on the German and Czech side.
The analysis was based on methods of Mathematical Statistics.
In addition, tunnels on D 8 were compared with similar tunnels on highways in Germany (a 71, a 38 and a 4).
There are no similar tunnels on the highway and 17.
In preparing this part of the inspection, it was important to accurately identify the relevant prices.
Both the supreme audit institution for a comparison of the prices of bridges have laid down the following principles: be based on the actual price paid for the bridge without the value added tax (VAT rates in the CZECH republic and the SNR varies and is subject to change); not to take into account the prices for the special foundations of the bridge; converted at the prices in Czk into € according to the rates of the European central bank in force on 30. 12. 2005 (CZK 29 = € 1).
On D 8 And 17 occur bridges of various structures (steel-concrete, prestressed reinforced concrete, composite steel-concrete and steel) and different sizes.
In order to ensure the homogeneity of the structures examined, bridges were divided into groups according to the type of construction.
Within these groups, the size of the bridge was also taken into account in the analyses.
By far the most common type of construction were concrete bridges on both sides of the border (20 bridges on D 8, 36 bridges on and 17).
The analysis focused mainly on this group of bridges, since the numeracy of the set made it possible to use mathematical-statistical methods with a high degree of reliability of results.
Checks revealed that the prices for m 2 concrete bridges on the D 8 And 17 depends on the size of the bridge (its length, area): the bigger the bridge, the lower the price per m2 of bridge construction.
For German bridges, the price dependence on size was stronger than for Czech ones (see charts below).
Two concrete bridges on a 17 and four on D 8 were identified, the price of which is significantly higher.
To find these bridges was used both method enabling the detection of atypical values in the file numbers, the first regression analysis, taking into account the dependence of the price of the bridge on its size (to determine the atypically expensive bridges is the standard distance from regression curves upwards).
Information about the atypically high price of those bridges should, however, be regarded only as an indicator that bridges need to focus.
In order to draw a generally applicable conclusion, the causes of the high price in each identified case should be analyzed.
One such cause may be inefficient administrative measures or environmental requirements or other acceptable reasons.
With regard to the Czech concrete bridges are on average longer than German (see table below), demonstrated a negative dependence of the price of the bridge to its length could lead to the assumption that the Czech bridges should be cheaper.
The hypothesis of lower prices for Czech concrete bridges is also supported by lower labor costs in the construction industry in the Czech Republic compared to Germany.
However, the results of the analysis, on the contrary, show that the prices for concrete bridges on D 8 are higher than on a 17.
In the course of joint negotiations, two possible causes of this condition were identified:
1.
In Germany, most bridges are awarded as separate contracts.
Such an award allows small and medium-sized regional companies to participate in the competition for the contract.
In the Czech Republic, many bridges are awarded as part of the contract for the part of the highway route, which is several kilometers long.
Small and medium-sized companies do not participate in such a competition, because the contract is too large for them.
2.
In the Czech Republic there is more variability in the construction of bridges than in Germany.
In this connection, the Sao found that the type of construction of the bridge is decided long before its construction.
The decision shall be taken at the time when the RSD translates the application for a territorial decision.
RSD at this time selects bridge types from multiple variants, but economy plays a smaller role in decision making.
A general conclusion on the prices of bridges in the Czech Republic and Germany could only be reached on the basis of a thorough analysis of the construction market in both countries, but would go beyond this control action.
The border bridge is the most expensive coupled steel-concrete bridge on D 8 A and 17.
In the case of tunnels, it was found that the prices of tunnels on D 8 are twice that of tunnels in Germany.
However, the comparison of the main construction-technical parameters of tunnels on D 8 with tunnels in Germany showed no significant difference.
Significant price differences could be attributed to the fact that there is no real competition in the field of tunnel construction in the Czech Republic.
However, a small number of tunnels did not allow to draw generally applicable conclusions.
Efficiency and efficiency of Dresden motorway construction-Prague
A separate Czech Republic was created in 1993.
The government in the same year approved the concept of development of the highway network.
The D 8 motorway was to be gradually extended from Prague to the state border with Germany.
Section no 0805 via české městohoří was to be acquired earlier than Section no 0807.
The Czech Republic procures Highway D 8 as part of programming financing.
In programme no. 327 220 "Construction of highway D 8 Prague – Ústí nad Labem – state border CR/FRG" were identified as two objectives of the construction of highway D 8:
1.
improve the connection of Prague and the mouth above the Elbe-national objective;
2.
improve the connection between Prague and Berlin within IV. the Trans – European Transport Corridor Berlin – Istanbul-an international destination.
According to the programme, the construction of the section leading through the Czech central mountains was to be completed in June 2008 and the construction of the border section no 0807 in June 2007.
Here it is necessary to add that the term of completion is not identical to the date of commissioning.
The Sao found that the preparation of the construction of the section leading through the Czech central mountains is now at the stage of an official territorial decision.
Environmental activists have challenged the decision with lawsuits.
There is no final decision on the actions.
Therefore it cannot be excluded that the stretch leading through the Czech central mountains will be completed several years later than stated in the program documentation.
In the summer of 2006, the Czech Ministry of Transport proposed to postpone the completion date of Section no 0805 for 2010.
As a result of these facts, the construction of the border section did not achieve the national objective – improving the connection between Prague and the outhouse above the Elbe.
RSD carried out an estimate of capital expenditure for border Section D 8 no 0807 and Section 0805 through the Czech central mountains between 1999 and 2001.
The estimate for these capital expenditure included in the investment costs is around € 639 million combined for both sections no 0805 and no 0807.

Economic analysis carried out in 2001 was based on the assumption that the border stretch and stretch through the Czech central mountains will be completed in a timely manner.
However, at the time of the inspection it is clear that the section through the Czech central mountains will not be opened at the original date.
This will reduce the above EIRR values.
Cost of both sections excluding VAT, calculated at 31. 12. 2005, there were 897 million €, i.e. higher by 27.4% than the level of costs, which worked economic analysis in 2001.
But there is a risk that section 0805 will be run on another, more expensive route, which would affect the aforementioned boundary of economic viability.
Economic analysis showed that the construction of both sections of the highway is economically viable at an intensity of at least 18,000 vehicles per day in 2010.
The forecast for 2008 was 22,940 vehicles, but the study addressing the issue of roundtrips for the missing section across the Czech central mountains foresees an intensity of 12,600 to 13,750 vehicles per day, which pushes the investment below the limit of economic viability.
At higher load detour routes for the missing stretch through the Czech central mountains there is a high probability of congestion, and thus increase the external costs, which was not foreseen when the original economic analysis.
The abovementioned reduction in revenues and cost increases means that the already low EIRR that the construction of border section D 8 should have had will not be achieved.
Construction of the D 8 border section is therefore inefficient.
There were also similar cost overruns in the construction of Highway a 17 as in the case of these two sections on D 8.
As part of the overall economic assessment of the Federal Road Development Plan for long-distance transport for 1992, the Federal Ministry of transport of Germany calculated the cost of about €320 million.
The resulting cost-income ratio was then 4.6.
In the meantime, however, costs have soared to around € 670 million and the cost-income ratio has more than halved.
In addition to the parallel inspection carried out together with the SAO, the BRH checked in 2003 and 2005 the preparation and construction of Highway a 17.
BRH while found that the approval of the state authority demanded for the third section 17-terrain tunnel, which was not needed.
During the inspection, the BRH managed to convince the Federal Ministry and the German administration for the construction of roads that the tunnel was not necessary.
The result was savings of around € 10 million on construction costs alone and € 0.15 million on annual operating costs.
When assessing the first section a 17 BRH, he found that the construction project was not properly prepared.
This is evidenced by the following example:
In the pre-trial stage did not carry out management for the construction of roads, survey conditions, the bedrock in the rocks Dölzschen, because the site was difficult to access.
The latter was carried out only after the tunnel stamping machine hit the rock.
Tests showed the rocks were more weathered inside than expected during the tender process.
Therefore, had to be taken costly measures such as anchoring, grouting and protective nets against falling rocks, which claimed about 3.3 million €.
The road and motorway directorate had to bear the costs not only to other emergency operations such as security measures in the rocks Dölzschen, but also measures that would not have been necessary, if he was a construction project is first properly prepared.
Expenses of this kind include the costs associated with the interruption of construction operations (3.2 million €), additional training of personnel for drilling (0.5 million €) and rising wages and spending on goods as a result of exceeding the duration of the project (7 million €).
The cost overruns thus amounted to around € 10.7 million, which was not matched by any added value.
On the basis of lessons learned from this and other projects audited have asked BRH federal ministry, to apply more strict guidance in his supervision of the works on the construction of roads.
In doing so, the Federal Ministry should give the roads and motorways directorates the necessary incentive to implement quality assurance systems.
The benefits of cooperation for the BRH and Sao cooperation fulfilled the intention of the two audit institutions.
BRH has acquired control knowledge of the preparation, assignment and course of the construction of the border bridge.
The two Supreme Audit Institutions have built a database of prices for bridges and tunnels on which future checks will be based.
The Sao found that the main building-technical parameters of bridges, tunnels and the route of the D 8 motorway do not differ from the parameters and 17.
Officers of both institutions involved in the cooperation gained new experience, which they can use in other controls.
