Coordinated control of funding for projects implemented under the Operational Programme of cross-border cooperation Czech Republic-Poland 2007-2013
INTRODUCTION
Europe's emerging community is a driving force for cross-border cooperation as an integral part of the broader territorial cooperation that has been a part of our lives for the past 20 years.
So let this community give an introductory statement to this joint report by the two Supreme Audit Institutions of neighbouring countries:
"185 million EU citizens (that is, 37% of the population) live in border areas.
These areas are usually underdeveloped and marginal territories, often a relic of darker parts of Europe's history.
The main objective of cross-border cooperation is helping to alleviate the existence of borders as administrative, legal and physical barriers and to further help the development of the slumbering potential of the border regions.
The programmes cover different border regions: some cover coastal areas, other inland borders within the EU or borders shared with candidate countries.
Most programs are bilateral, but some include more than two neighboring countries.“
The programmes last seven years and are allocated a total of EUR 5.7 billion from the EU budget.
"Programs include the following activities: repair and reconstruction of cross-border roads, bike paths and bridges, investment in cross-border waste systems, medical facilities, research centres, anti-flood measures, etc., joint management of natural sites or the development of tourist destinations, development of joint services for the local population, advising on matters of employment, the creation of thematic networks and clusters for innovation.
Support from the programme shall be granted on condition that organisations from both sides of the border (such as regional authorities, universities or SMEs) join together to implement projects based on the needs of the border region.
Representatives of the cooperating regions, the relevant ministries and other local partners to meet regularly and decide, which projects will be supported.
This system should lead to a sustainable form of cooperation even after the programme itself ends.
Funds are granted with the condition that the project partners from both sides of the border cooperate in a way that fulfills at least two of the following four characters: joint development, joint implementation, joint personnel, joint financing.“
In the framework of the partnership are the tasks and the responsibility for the preparation, implementation, financing and control of the activities of the project clearly defined and distributed to relevant partners.
Among the main attributes of partnership include: the common choice of a leading partner, joint project preparation and application, the conclusion of the joint partnership agreement signed by all the partners, taking overall responsibility for the implementation of the project the lead partner, the total payment of the support receives the head of the partner and implementing their transfer to the competent partners of the project.
Eligible projects carried out in the territory of the regions and the Voivodeship adjacent to the common border may be supported.
OBJECTIVES AND SCOPE OF CONTROL
11. December 2007 approved by the European commission (EC) Operational programme of cross border cooperation Czech republic – republic of Poland 2007-2013 (op cbc CR–POL).
€258,187,467 were earmarked for the implementation of the Operational Programme.
The total included a contribution from the European funds (ERDF) totalling € 219,459,344 (85 %), which must be exhausted by the end of 2015.
Financial data on the use of EU funds from the Operational Programme of cross – border cooperation Czech Republic-Poland 2007-2013 at the end of 2013 are presented in the table below:
The cooperation agreement between the Supreme Audit Institutions of the Czech Republic (Sao) and the Republic of Poland (NIK) was concluded by the presidents of both offices on 27. February 2013 after the previous mutual negotiations at the meeting of the heads of the supreme audit institutions of the Visegrad four, Austria and Slovenia, which took place in September 2012 in Lovasberény, Hungary.
The aim of cooperation was to examine whether the implementation of the operational programme takes place in accordance with the legislation and with the binding programming documents or agreements, whether management and control system works reliably, whether they are achieved the objectives of the operational programme and whether the selected projects are implemented in accordance with the terms of the support provided.
This cooperation took the form of a parallel control in which the control authorities on the basis of its legal mandate to independently examine the topics, the content of which was in advance jointly discussed.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The audit carried out also contained elements of the performance audit.
The selected topics were examined on a sample of projects by project partners on both sides of the border.
As a result of the checks carried out, the control conclusions published in the usual way by both authorities were published.
On the basis of the two control conclusions set out in the annex, this joint report was established.
The joint control sample selected included six projects (Annex 1) which fall under aid area 1.1 – strengthening transport accessibility and aid area 2.2 – promoting tourism development.
Before starting the checks represented a disbursement of funds from these two areas of support more than 60% of the funds reimbursed to the beneficiaries by the end of 2012 from the ERDF for all projects implemented in the framework of the entire op cbc CR–POL.

In addition to checking the joint sample of six projects, the SAO has checked 13 more projects and two more (all from support 1.1 and 2.2).
The funds paid to the beneficiaries of the ERDF, which were controlled by the SAO and NIK, amounted to a total of € 25,362,174 (Sao) and € 8,450,784 (NIK).
The controlled volume of appropriations represented 41% of all appropriations paid to aid beneficiaries in the aid areas 1.1 and 2.2.
MAIN CONTROL CONCLUSIONS
The two checks, independently carried out by the SAO on the Czech side, and NIK on the Polish side showed that the level of identified irregularities did not exceed the level of significance.
The implementation of the OPPS CR-POL, involving the operation of the management and control system and the implementation of selected projects, was successful.
Controlled entities, which were part of the management and control system, take steps to limit the risk of improper use of funds and underutilization of the resources granted from the ERDF.
Evidence of the effectiveness of the implemented projects in the framework of the operational programme is the high level objectives set, which has been supported by the results of the survey of social assessment of the implementation of projects.
SUMMARY OF CONTROL RESULTS
And. Evaluation of the management and control system
The coordinated approach allowed to perform the control of the management and control system applicable to the op cbc CR–POL embedded in the following institutions in both countries: the managing authority (the Ministry for regional development of the CZECH republic), national coordinator (Ministry for regional development POL) and supervisors (Center for regional development and the voivodship).
At the same time, a coordinated audit made it possible to evaluate the tasks and functions carried out by the Joint Technical Secretariat and the monitoring committee.
During the evaluation of the control system to the inspection focused on the activities carried out in connection with the setup and performance of the functions of the managing authority and the national coordinator, in particular in connection with the setting of programme objectives and monitoring of progress, evaluation of activities and annual reports, assessment, evaluation, selection and approval of project applications, the uptake of the programme and fulfilment of obligations to publish accurate, complete and current information about subsidies, further with the control activities of the managing authority, setting the performance of the activities and outputs of the audits of the designated audit body and the system for reporting and monitoring irregularities and his compliance with, at the same time was investigated the coordination of tasks and cooperation between institutions involved in the op cbc CR–POL.
Furthermore, it was investigated the activity of the competent authorities in the field of risk analysis and drawing up control plans in place implementation of the projects and reviewed the evaluation of project applications carried out by independent evaluators.
Examination of the control system included a review of the administrative checks and inspections carried out on the spot, which allowed for the approval of e.g. the supply of goods and co-funded services, the eligibility of expenses submitted for payment and at the same time, the compliance of the disbursement of these funds, and related activities (or their parts) with the national legislation and EU legislation.
Significant shortcomings were identified by the Sao's control in the field of publishing correct, complete and up-to-date information on the subsidies provided.
The risk of non-transparency of this process has been identified in the field of Project Evaluation and approval.
Other deficiencies have been identified in the monitoring indicator settings and in the irregularity Reporting System Settings.
Based on these findings, assessed, the Supreme audit office control and the control system implemented by the managing authority as partially effective.
Discrepancies identified NICHES, which were related to the functioning of the management and control system in Poland in relation to violations of the applicable laws and rules, have not been assessed as significant.
The said irregularities had an impact only on individual projects and has not had a significant impact on the implementation of the op cbc CR–POL.
Despite the discrepancies identified, NIK evaluated the functioning of the system positively.
B. Evaluation of project results
The control did not show a discrepancy between the indicators and objectives set for each project and those defined by the Operational Programme.
In all the projects examined have achieved the expected results, the funded activities have been implemented and have been met indicators (measurable parameters) set out in the project applications operational programme.
The control conclusions are in line with the result of the social evaluation survey of project implementation described in the text below.
An important aspect, which the SAO and NIK pay attention to in its conclusions, is the limited possibility of an objective evaluation of the performance of the predicted results of individual projects with regard to the objectives of individual projects and at the same time, the objectives of the operational programme.
On the initiative of the Supreme Audit Chamber, an opinion poll was conducted in the summer of 2013 at the place of implementation of projects selected for the joint audit sample.
The survey and its evaluation were carried out by the School of higher vocational education in the NYSE (Poland).
After agreement with the Supreme audit office, the investigation was carried out on both sides of the border between the 2 820 respondents, both among the public in Poland in relation to the part of the project implemented by the Polish project partners in the Czech public in relation to the part of the project implemented in the Czech republic.
The survey mainly concerned the appropriateness, quality, information exchange, resource usage, social functions and projects including investments.
The number of respondents for each project is set out in Annex 2.
The assessment of responses from the survey indicated that the overall social evaluation of projects was good and reached the value of 4.8 points (on a scale with a maximum of 8 points), which means that the results of the projects were positively perceived by most respondents as having regard to the objectives, so according to the other parameters listed in the project applications.
According to the respondents, the projects examined met the criteria expressed in the Operational Programme.
Respondents also noted the positive impact of investments on improving the quality of transport and tourism infrastructure, transport accessibility, tourist attractiveness, business conditions, the quality of life of citizens and the resumption of contacts between the inhabitants of the border region.
On the other hand, the overall response assessment indicated a certain difference between the actual level of achievement of objectives/parameters (actual impact rate) and the level expected by the respondents.
This difference applies to the evaluation of the results of individual projects, where in some cases there is a significant difference.
The results of the survey were in accordance with the views of the participants of the panel discussions (focus groups) carried out under the control of NIK on the Polish side, who have pointed out the need for the implementation of projects and confirmed their positive public acceptance and fulfilment of expected results.
No. Evaluation of the legality of controlled projects
The beneficiaries examined the compliance of the project's factual and timing with the timetable and content of the project application, the implementation of the objectives and purpose of the project, the fulfilment of binding monitoring indicators, the management of changes in projects, the management of any revenues of the project, the fulfilment of the obligation of separate accounting of project transactions, compliance with the ban on eligibility of project expenditure, selection of suppliers and verification of delivered transactions on the basis of procurement contracts.
The total financial value of the shortfalls of qualified Sao and NIK as non-EU financing expenditure was found to be € 85,094.
However, this amount did not exceed the established level of materiality relating to the total controlled volume of funds for the sample of projects.
Despite the irregularities identified, the SAO and NIK evaluated the implementation of the selected projects positively by the beneficiaries.
In most cases, the obligations arising from the conditions of the aid were duly fulfilled by the beneficiary.
Funds for the implementation of controlled projects were spent in accordance with EU regulations and national law.
Nevertheless, seven of the eight beneficiaries of the aid controlled by NIK found irregularities in the fulfilment of material and financial obligations.
It was about individual cases of non-systemic nature and were especially inconsistent preparation of project documentation and violation of rules for public procurement, which, however, should not impact on the selection of the supplier or the delivery of the contractually agreed work.
Only in one of all projects controlled NICHES can be identified by the irregularity, which concerned failure to comply with obligations in the area of reporting, evaluated as ineligible expenditure in the amount of 43 003 PLN (8 of 231 € to be financed from the ERDF).
On the other hand, the Sao identified ineligible expenditure of CZK 2,098,053 in three of the 19 projects audited (of which € 76,863 financed by the ERDF).
Irregularities included the non-delivery of paid material and work or of the expenditure for upgrading of property owned by a person who didn't have feedback on the project either as recipient, or as a project partner.
RECOMMENDATION
The joint recommendations of the SAO and NIK refers to the improvement of the monitoring system, especially with regard to a consistent definition of the proper monitoring indicators for all specific objectives of the priority axis of the operational programme.
Generally it is also necessary to strive for the establishment of such indicators at the program level and projects, which will allow a more reliable verification of compliance impacts.
Notes and recommendations arising from the inspections carried out on both sides of the border are included in the separate audit conclusions of the SAO and NIK on the CD.
COMMUNIQUE
Report has been drawn up in Czech, English and Polish language and signed by the presidents of the supreme audit institutions of the Czech republic and the Polish republic.
Public works procurement and Prevention of corruption
Joint report on the parallel audit by the Czech Supreme audit office (SAO) and the German Federal court of auditors (BRH)
Introduction and overview
Procurement of goods and services by contracting authorities is very important for both the state and the private sphere.
The role of the state is to use public resources as effectively and efficiently and to ensure fair and regulated free competition.
In the European Union (EU), public procurement is a key factor in the success of the Single Economic Area.
The EU in its legislation has set limits above which the ca must meet certain requirements to guarantee the wide and limitless competitive environment across the EU.
EU member states must therefore transpose the European tender right into their national legislation and put it into practice.
Both the Czech Republic and Germany have already done so.
For public contracts that are below EU limits, the regulation of their procurement remains within the competence of individual countries.
In addition, public procurement is vulnerable to corruption with a consequent high potential for damage.
Therefore, contracting entities are obliged to adopt in their procurement procedures reasonable measures to prevent corruption and improper favoritism (prevention of corruption).
In January 2011 the Supreme audit office of the Czech republic (Czech SAI – SAO) and the Federal accounting court of Germany (the German SAI – BRH) agree to perform parallel inspections in the field of procurement management and prevention of corruption in land and road construction.
Cooperation was also focused on the area of european procurement law as transposed into national legislation.
The controls also included procurement under European limits with a view to affecting the area of corruption prevention.
The audit findings of both the supreme audit institutions are summarised in the joint report, which is inter alia determined by the international organisations, such as the International organisation of supreme audit institutions (INTOSAI).
Control areas and controlled institutions
Evaluation BRH comes from the circuit controls the above-mentioned areas, which have been carried out by the German building administrations responsible for the federal transport and building construction in the years 2011 to 2012.
For example, highway construction and large-scale construction projects were evaluated.
The BRH included findings from past inspections in the evaluation.
Evaluation of the SAO comes from the checks carried out during the years 2008 to 2012, which were focused on construction of roads, railway lines, hydropower projects, large buildings (hospitals, cultural facilities, universities) and some other buildings in the Czech republic.
In Germany, federal public procurement is mostly carried out by land-based construction administrations.
In the Czech Republic, state institutions for road and rail construction are responsible for public procurement in the field of transport infrastructure.
In the field of building construction, public procurement is realized by entities which are recipients of budgetary funds.
In both countries, the services of external experts are also used at each stage of the procurement procedure.
The evaluation shall take into account the differences in public procurement legislation and the peculiarities of the construction market in both countries.
Structure of the Public Procurement Act in both countries
In Germany, the course of European procurement procedures is governed by laws and under-law standards.
The procurement procedures limited to Germany shall be governed by budgetary law and the relevant administrative acts .
Internal administrative rules contain numerous additional provisions for both European and national procurement procedures.
Further details regarding the requirements of the european procurement law and prevention of corruption are embedded in the so-called procurement manuals of the federal government, in which the requirements are developed or formulated into greater detail with regard to the legal precedents in the area of procurement law.
In the Czech republic public procurement regulated by the law on public procurement and other laws and regulations that relate to contracts with a value above and below the european limits.
The procurement law made significant changes in 2012.
The new rules enhance transparency of procurement procedures, opened the space for more competition and reducing opportunities for corruption during the procurement procedure.
Basic aspects of the tendering law in both countries
As regards European procurement procedures, in particular open and closer procedures must be applied in both countries.
In Germany the contracts are below the european limit awarded in accordance with national legislation (public call to participation in the contest, limited the invitation to participate, the rules of procedure), you are however practically identical with the above mentioned terms for the european procurement procedure.
Public procurement in Germany is characterized by the principle of preference of open procedures (where they are invited by the candidates in the european scale) and public calls for participation (only in the case of national procedure).
In open procedures and in a call for competition, any candidate may submit an offer.
Another important feature of German procurement law is the support of small and medium-sized companies.
This is mainly achieved by dividing the total public contract into commercially specific parts and dividing it into sub-contracts.
The award of contracts divided into these parts gives the chance to participate in the procedure as many candidates as possible.
The two characteristics of German procurement law are time-tested instruments for obtaining good value for money.
In Germany, more than 330,000 construction companies with 1.9 million employees are registered.
In the Czech Republic, the conditions of European procedures must be applied even in cases of public procurement with a value below the EU limit.
The exception is a simplified sub-minimal procedure where the sponsor can apply less demanding procedures.
In accordance with European law, Czech procurement law includes the conditions under which the contract must be awarded in order to ensure competition and to obtain a favourable price.
The current Czech legislation allows contracting entities to choose between open and narrower proceedings.
In the Czech Republic, 85 000 construction companies are registered, of which about 1,900 have 20 or more employees.
Total volume of public works contracts by contracting authorities and share of each type of Management in both countries
In 2011, the total volume of construction works in Germany amounted to EUR 7 675 billion.
Czk, of which 1 138 billion (15 %) accounted for the proportion of public procurement, which in addition to the contracts awarded by the federal government include a contract awarded by the länder and municipalities.
The total volume of projects of Federal Road and land construction (without the construction of Railways and water structures) amounted to CZK 212.5 billion.
In 2011, the composition of the federal procurement of road construction works and road construction as follows: of 80.7 % open procedures and public calls; 12,7 % closer management and greater challenges;
6,6% negotiated procedures and direct procurement; 33,2% is the share of European procurement procedures.
The volume of public construction contracts in the Czech republic in 2011 amounted to 118,6 billion Rubles , which was about 25 % of the total volume of all construction works.
In 2009 it amounted to CZK 194.0 billion, which was 37 % of the total volume.
Structure of types of procurement procedures in 2011: 65,1% open procedures; 14,3% closer procedures; 9,5% negotiated procedures; 8,4% simplified procedures for sub-minimal contracts; 2,7% other procedures.
That information shall cover all supply, service and works contracts awarded by contracting authorities in 2011.
These figures reveal that: parallel control in both countries were aimed at a substantial part of public procurement procedures; prevention of corruption, which is a must-have in the conduct of procurement proceedings still in mind, has a significant financial impact; open meaning. procurement procedures are of key importance.
Summary of the main results
The SAO and BRH carried out parallel control of european orders for construction work with an emphasis on the prevention of corruption in their countries.
The checks were aimed at comparing legislation in both countries and the EU and implementing public procurement in the field of land and transport buildings.
Key findings are also given:
The EU public procurement directive has been transposed into the national rights of both countries (Points 1). and 3.1).
Prevention of corruption is not the only purpose of the EU directive, but the national procurement rules of both countries, which partly differ in focus and in detail.
In both countries, is an essential requirement that the procurement documents comply with, the inclusion of all information necessary for the preparation of the tenders.
The specifications shall be neutral and shall not contain any requirements restricting competition.
The tender documents in Germany generally meet these requirements.
In the Czech Republic, the problem is the lack of definition of the subject of the contract.
In Germany, procurement is required to be divided into parts where possible in order to promote a competitive environment.
According to the findings of the BRH, this requirement is complied with in Germany.
The SAO audit showed that in the Czech republic are awarded a significantly voluminous public works in the area of road constructions, without being divided into parts or divided they are, but only on the volume of the very significant parts. This method can distort competition and lead to restrictions on only a few large companies.
These limitations on market potential can result in significant cost increases and create the risk of unserious price negotiations and inadmissible conventions.
The legislation in both countries allows authorities, under certain conditions, additionally enter other construction work,if such a need arises only after the conclusion of the contract (section 4.1).
In both countries, the requirements for correctly determining the type of Procurement Procedure are met.
In the Czech republic according to the applicable legislation, contracting authorities can freely determine the one of the open tendering procedures, the open procedure or the restricted procedure.
German rules in the procurement and budgetary law enshrine the preference of open procedures for both European tender and national, known as public calls for competition.
Open tender procedures in both countries allow a larger number of candidates to submit a bid, and also reduce the risk of corruption, because they make it difficult unlawful negotiation of prices between the candidates.
At the same time, the best results in value for money are achieved.
In the case of large contracts, with an estimated total price reaches or exceeds the limits set by the EU, writing controlled entities always european procurement procedure.
In determining the type of Procurement Procedure, the correct determination of the estimated value of the contract plays a very important role.
In Germany, databases are used for objective pricing of Public Works, in which values are based on completed construction projects.
This is a sufficiently objective tool.
In the Czech republic databases are used only in the field of road construction, but not yet an effective tool (section 4.2).
When the award of the contract for construction work according to european public procurement procedures is necessary to publish a prior information and contract notices, and due to the increased competition by the candidates to prepare in time for the submission of tenders.
As a rule, the construction authorities audited complied with this requirement.
In isolated cases, errors in the information released, incorrect application of provisions and/or a lack of controls may have impaired competition (item 4.3).
There is a greater risk of manipulation when choosing candidates to participate in a shortlist.
Under EU law, the number of candidates invited must be high enough to guarantee genuine competition.
The selection criteria shall be objective, non-discriminatory and published well in advance.
In addition to EU requirements, contracting authorities in both countries should as often as possible alternate candidates who call for participation in the procedure when selecting suppliers.
In Germany, there are, in part, very detailed requirements for preventing the risks of manipulation.
In some cases, controlled contracting entities did not comply with these requirements.
In the Czech Republic, selection decisions were not always credible (section 4.4).
In both countries, contracting authorities during the procurement procedure to ensure that all candidates who wish to submit a bid, received the same information.
Any agreements between these candidates and between them and third persons, which participated in the preparation of the specifications, must be to the greatest possible extent prevented, to avoid restriction of competition in the form of illegal agreements.
In Germany, the measures in question are more thorough than in the Czech Republic.
However, the German contracting authorities under scrutiny did not comply with that requirement in several cases (point 4.5).
In both countries, the principle of cross-checking and transparency must be applied when opening envelopes.
The requirements for labelling, documentation, protection and confidentiality of the offers have a limited space for manipulation and in Germany are particularly detailed.
Checks in both countries found only a few cases of irregularities (section 4.6).
The assessment and evaluation of bids is procedurally regulated in both countries.
The relevant German measures are more comprehensive, but have not always been respected by the contracting authorities under scrutiny.
Authorities, for example, transferred their supply to third parties for inspection without their prior assessment, without that we can document any suspicious circumstances.
Thus, tenders were insufficiently protected against subsequent manipulations (point 4.7).
For reasons of legal protection, participants must be informed about the intended contract award before the latter is finalised.
This legal protection rule also is designed to prevent corrupt action.
The law of the Czech Republic provides for judicial review of contract award procedures also for national tenders.
Only in few cases, the notification of the enterprises was not appropriately ensured (item 4.8).
The tender documentation was not always complete or completely credible for the contracting authorities controlled in both countries.
In the case of several procurement procedures were not always in the minutes of proceedings duly complied with the transparency requirements applicable at european level.
In addition, some of the deficiencies identified reduced the preventive anti-corruption function of the dossier.
Contracting entities in both countries have mostly complied with their reporting obligations (clause 4.9).
Summary of the main principles of European tendering law and Prevention of corruption
European Procurement Law
The european parliament and the Council of the European union take to ensure free competition in the EU, inter alia, the directive on the coordination of procedures for the award of public contracts for public works, supplies and services with the aim of ensuring the free movement of goods and services and the directive on the coordination of laws, regulations and administrative provisions relating to review procedures concerning the award of public supply contracts and public works contracts (directive on review procedures), with these two directives should be transposed into national law.
General procurement principles of the EU include in particular: the requirement for a competitive environment; the requirement for equal treatment or prohibition of discrimination; transparency requirement.
the procurement principles of the EU include the Directive on the coordination of procedures for the award of public contracts includes provisions relating to construction projects whose total estimated value equal to or greater than 5 miles. €.
These provisions have an impact on: the content of the tender documentation; the used type of the procurement procedure; the publication of certain information before, during and after the termination of the proceedings; the deadline for the receipt of tenders; the qualification requirements which may be after the applicants are required; the criteria for selecting the most suitable deals.
The legal protection of tenderers is governed by the review directive.
In the event of a potential breach of the tendering law, tenderers may have the decision of the contracting authority reviewed in accordance with the review procedures.
Both countries transposed EU requirements into national legislation.
Prevention of corruption
Importance of preventing corruption
There is no legal definition of what corruption actually means in either country.
In general, corruption is understood as an abuse of a personal (confidential) position for one's own benefit.
As a rule, this means that such abuse is encouraged by those who benefit from it.
Corruption can be a barrier to competition and can cause serious economic losses.
According to estimates, total corruption-related damage accounts for 5% of the world's economic output.
For the EU region, these costs are estimated at 1% of the EU's economic output.
If it is in the contract involved, the contracting authority, of the convention restricting competition, or allowing dishonest conduct may weaken confidence in the integrity, ability and overall work of the public administration.
Therefore, the Prevention of corruption is an essential task of the contracting authorities.
Practice and procedures shall be checked in particular in areas particularly susceptible to corruption, in order to adopt adequate measures for its avoidance.
Taking preventive measures and carrying out effective controls can significantly reduce the susceptibility of the decision-making process to corruption.
As a rule, the award of works contracts is considered an area particularly susceptible to corruption.
Measures to prevent corruption
In Germany corruption is stíhatelná under criminal and labour law, which especially refers to active and passive bribery, accepting and offering significant advantages.
The German federal government issued a manual with recommendations, which relate to the prevention of corruption in the federal administration and according to which they are applied throughout the procurement process outside the risk analysis following principles: priority to the open input; the principle of multiple control and transparent decision-making; separation of planning, award and accounting phase; accurate and complete documentation of the procurement procedure.
In addition, other measures having a preventive effect against corruption have become part of the procurement law.
In 2011, introduced the relevant federal ministry of information technology supporting system for monitoring the award of contracts for the construction of federal roads.
Using this system can be information such as the estimated cost, the total value of the contract and the involvement of the private design offices fully recorded and analysed in order to ascertain eventual irregularities.
In the Czech Republic corruption is prosecuted under criminal law, the level of labour or civil law is also taken into account.
The legal requirement for transparency, equal treatment and the prohibition of any discrimination during the entire procurement process (preparation and implementation) is the most important part of the prevention of corruption.
Anti-corruption measures in this field was established by the government in the "Strategy of the government in the fight against korupcím for the period 2011-2012", which was updated for the years 2013 and 2014.
Part of those measures has been incorporated into the Public Procurement Act and subsequent implementing regulations.
The new legislation contains the following basic provisions: lowering the limits for small-scale contracts; the obligation to provide prior notification of the contracting authority, including the justification of the contract; the prohibition to limit the number of candidates in a restricted procedure and the abolition of the general possibilities to limit the number of candidates by drawing lots; the obligation to publish contracts, including annexes; the obligation to disclose actual and lists of subcontractors.
Results of checks relating to the subsequent stages of the procurement procedure
Tender documentation
The tender documentation must contain all information necessary to enable tenderers to prepare their bids due form.
In particular, the documentation must enable the tender price to be processed.
In order to do so, candidates must not be exposed to risks they could not count on.
Tender documents mainly contains the specifications, then the requirements to demonstrate the qualifications of the candidates and criteria for the selection of the most advantageous tender.
Requirements for European law and Prevention of corruption
In particular, European law contains requirements relating to technical specifications.
Specifications must restrict competition as little as possible and all candidates must have equal access.
The specifications shall be neutral.
Requirements for specific specific products are admissible on a very limited scale in the tender documentation.
The basic principle of preventing corruption is that the tender documents do not contain requirements that could restrict competition.
Documentation should also avoid confusion or inaccurate data, which create a space for speculation and for handling during the evaluation of tenders.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries have transposed EU legal provisions into their national legislation.
The basic principle is that the specifications are given in general without reference to a particular product or brand.
Specifications must precisely define the required supplies and services and detail the number of units of work and supply.
In normal cases, the prices should be quoted according to units of works or supply (e.g. in € /m or € /item).
To define the required works in terms of their functionality is permissible only in exceptional cases.
In principle, as a rule, the specifications need to be drawn up completely and unambiguously.
They must contain precise quantities and must not include works and supplies, the necessity of which is not entirely obvious.
Reimbursement in the form of lump sums or according to time worked should be avoided where possible.
These parts of the tender documents shall exclude speculation and manipulation, based on ambiguous specifications.
The specifications must enable each tenderer to prepare their tender with certainty and without excessive preparatory work.
The invitation to tender shall not be published until the tender documentation is complete.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic there is no obligation for contracting authorities to award construction contracts in parts.
The contracting authority can divide the contract into several separate parts, if it admits the nature of the subject of such contracts.
In Germany it is required the application of the rule to divide the construction work on the section, either quantitatively (partial deliveries), or according to specific criteria (a specialized part of the contract).
This allows participation in the competition even to small and medium-sized entities, increases the number of potential bidders and makes it difficult to fix prices.
This type of award is usually considered the most appropriate in terms of providing value for money.
In the Czech Republic, the tender documents must contain evaluation criteria for national and European procurement procedures.
Thus, the tenderer should be informed comprehensively and exhaustively of the criteria by which his tender will be evaluated.
In Germany, the requirement to include evaluation criteria in the notice apply only to european invitation to tender.
In national procurement procedures, it is necessary to include Evaluation Criteria Only in the contract record, which is an internal administrative document.
If the tender documentation prepared by independent experts, the German regulations require to exclude from it any information which would assist in the identification of specific interested companies, architects or designers.
This is to prevent individual construction companies from obtaining any additional information or other inadmissible competitive advantages without the knowledge of the sponsor through contacts with these independent experts.
It is also why independent experts shall not disclose documents relating to tenders and facilitate their accessibility for examination.
The contracting authority is the only point of contact for construction companies.
The Czech Republic does not currently have a similar provision.
In the case of large construction projects arises after the conclusion of the original contract almost always a need for additional works or modification of existing work.
The legislation of both countries allows the award of a multi-work contract within a certain limit to the same supplier without the need to publish and implement a new procurement procedure.
The volume of multiplication under both European and German legislation shall not exceed 50% of the original value of the contract.
Moreover, multi-work must be necessary and must have the nature of a specific component of the main contract.
In the Czech Republic, a more stringent limit of 20% is applied for the entry of multipractice.
It can bring the risk of greater delays in the implementation of the contract and the possible integration of new entity into the already running project.
Where a multi-work contract is awarded to the supplier of the original contract, German law contains a provision which prevents suppliers from arbitrarily increasing the price of modified works or multi-work.
Calculations must be made taking into account the prices agreed in the original contract.
In addition to more work, fewer work can occur during construction, that is, work that was not needed.
In the Czech Republic, lesswork and morework can not compensate each other.
Main control findings
BHR
Technical specifications and product-neutral invitation to tender
In isolated cases, the specifications referred to national technical requirements or standards, but were replaced by EU standards in the meantime.
In some cases, the specifications include the data requesting a certain brand, e.g. for system resilience of public inscriptions to prevent water penetration or for acoustic tiles, although it wasn't needed.
In some cases, the specifications were so detailed that only one product met the requirements.
Quantitative specifications broken down into items
In no case has the BRH observed a non-compliance with the general requirements for inviting tenders for supplies and services in accordance with the quantitative specifications broken down into items.
Completeness of specifications
In most controlled cases, tender documents were drawn up without a trace before the invitation to tender was announced.
However, in different cases, the documents had to be modified during the procurement procedure when changes in the items or in the timetable had to be taken into account.
In isolated cases, the tender documents contained work and supplies, the need for which was uncertain.
One tender documentation for demolition works contained almost exclusively such items.
Subdivision of the contract and award criteria
In many cases, the desired justification for not dividing supplies into parts has not been demonstrated.
The BRH did not find any deficiencies in the criteria for evaluating tenders prior to the award of the contract.
Inclusion of the names of authorized independent experts
Many of the documents cited interested authorized experts.
The names were indicated on the opening pages of the documents or on the plans or attached opinions.
In one case, the sponsor invited the applicant to its questions to the procurement management contact explicitly appointed by the architect.
For projects of road construction were these cases detected mainly in the tender documentation, where they were processing the specifications of the entrusted self-employed experts.
Authorities said they do not have sufficient staffing capacity for detailed vetting of tender dossiers.
Sao
Technical specifications and product-neutral invitation to tender
In the case of public contracts for the construction of a house with 12 apartments was a link directly to the specific manufacturer and brand products.
The contracting authority did not authorise the use of other similar product types or justify why it requires the supply of specific products.
For the construction of facilities of the University, the tender documentation included references to specific trading firms and specific product designations.
General overview of specifications and sub-specifications
In the construction of some industrial zones of the contracting authority in the tender documentation failed to identify clearly the amount and type of the requested works, supplies or services in the bill of quantities and the set for each building as a unit of measurement only enclosed space in cubic metres.
Completeness of specifications
During the procurement procedure for the construction of the road circuit, the tender documentation for the narrower procedure was amended four times between August and September 2009.
This was due to changes in the project documentation caused by the expansion of the scope of the contract and the change in technical conditions.
In the construction of social objects should tender documentation defects, which necessitated the creation of additional works (missed the exact focus, was not carried out sufficient structural and technical survey, missing drawings).
In the tender documentation for the construction of the great library were listed elements of the interior only descriptively, without specifying the quality requirements on the products.
Supply equipment to the interior of the building provided the subcontractors, who got some extra and very expensive equipment.
Parts and award criteria
In the Czech Republic there is no obligation to award the contract in parts.
From the analysis of the three major road constructions during the construction of the ring road showed that, at the time of their entering in an open procedure in parts (separately for selected objects) it was possible to achieve savings of up to eur 790 million. CZK 15,508 million of the public procurement price achieved. CZK.
For example, a saving of £ 62.5 M could be achieved when six building buildings were awarded as a separate part of the contract.
CZK, i.e. 25% of the contracted price and the award of 20 bridges as a separate part of the contract could have been achieved by saving £ 287.8 m. CZK, i.e. also 25%.
The contracting authority during the construction of the road in the tender documents the qualification criteria, which limited the participation of small suppliers in the procurement process.
In the tender specifications open procedure for suppliers in one construction highway construction contracting entity demanded, inter alia, the practice of a supplier consisting in the implementation of at least three road construction projects on the financial volume of each of more than 700 miles. CZK, completed or operational over the last five years.
In the Czech Republic there are only nine companies that meet the condition of completion of construction above 700 miles. In the last five years.
Public contract for the supply of other highway construction projects in an open procedure included six separate buildings, for which the contracting authority required a minimum annual volume of construction work in last three years 12 billion.
Two thirds of financial volume of road construction works (I.email. € 2.5 billion out of € 3.7 billion) in the period of 2008-2009 were realized would be 5 suppliers or individually either in form of consortium.
There were only two or even one bidder for 46 contracts worth a total of £ 13.2 bn.
The Sao pointed out that limiting market potential can lead to a large increase in costs.
Area of multiplication
In two cases, the contracting authority did not conclude a written contract for the delivery of multi-works during the construction of the road circuit and did not provide for multi-work in any of the procedures specified in the law.
The value of unapproved multiplications in one case was 1,591,4 million. CZK excluding VAT (21% increase) and in the second case 4,135,8 million. CZK excluding VAT (increase of 91 %).
The cause of the multiplication was, first of all, an ambiguous definition of the quantity and type of work required.
For the construction of a higher education institution, the contracting authority did not include in the procurement documents certain works and supplies, the necessity of which he knew when the contract was awarded for the completion and housebuilding of the building.
These labor and delivery making amendments to the contract for work with the construction contractor with an increase in prices, in negotiated procedure without publication, although the volume of extra works exceeded the national limit of 20 % of the value of the original contract.
In connection with the construction of the judicial Palace, the contracting authority reserved the right to award additional works without a procurement procedure.
During construction, the contracting authority increased the scope of the contract by £ 50.5 m. CZK.
Unit prices for additional works established without competition were significantly higher than comparable works performed by the same supplier.
Other findings
SAO on a selected sample of buildings found that the average construction cost for the construction of one mile of four-lane highway in the Czech republic are 355,0 million. CZK.
According to long-term data obtained from the German Ministry of construction, the average cost in Germany per kilometer of a four-lane highway is 260.0 miles. CZK.
This comparison suggests that the acquisition of a motorway in the Czech Republic is more expensive than in Germany.
Summary
The legal provisions relating to the contract documents are in both countries almost identical, and are in accordance with the requirements of european law.
The aim is to ensure complete and equal competition and Prevention of corruption.
The specifications must be sufficiently precise to allow candidates to calculate costs and prepare their tenders.
In addition, this requirement limits the scope for speculation, and the sponsor is protected against the need to enter multiwork.
In Germany, the basic legal provisions about tender documents supplemented by other rules, which have even more reduce the options for limiting the competition and for the implementation of the manipulation.
Although there are no detailed requirements of this kind in the Czech Republic, greater transparency is achieved by publishing the award criteria.
In both countries, the requirements for specifications are mostly met.
However, in some cases, deficiencies have been identified that could lead to a restriction of competition.
At the same time a valid rule in Germany calling for dividing large construction projects into parts seems to be suitable for strengthening the competitive environment and achieving cost-effective results.
The SAO found that the Czech republic may award contracts on the volume large-scale projects without entering in parts, or division on a volume large parts restrict the range of applicants to a small number of large suppliers.
The result of the strict requirement for the reference of candidates, which is implemented in the Czech republic for the selection of applicants for road construction work, is the fact that they are public contracts awarded to only a small circle of candidates, and small and medium-sized companies do not have a chance to compete.
A limited number of bidders also increases the risk of price fixation and other illegal conventions.
As regards the award of additional multi-work or modified work and their reimbursement, regulatory approaches in both countries are different.
If the value of additional works under european and German law does not exceed 50% of the value of the original contract, may be additional works awarded without a procurement procedure and its notification.
In the Czech Republic, a stricter limit of 20% applies.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
This limit is often exceeded by the sponsor.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
If the limit of 20 % is exceeded, morework must be entered on the basis of a new procurement procedure.
By dividing the works into parts, competition can be avoided, as well as the consequent unfortunate consequences.
Determining the type of procurement procedure with regard to EU limits
By determining the type of Procurement Procedure, the sponsor defines the circle of potential suppliers who will be admitted to the competition.
The Sponsor may leave the range of potential suppliers Unlimited or may limit the range according to the criteria specified.
In the case of large-scale project works, the value of which reaches or exceeds the limits set by the EU, a European Procurement Procedure must be conducted.
Requirements for European law and Prevention of corruption
When choosing the type of procedure the contracting authority must in particular meet the requirements of european law concerning the competitive environment and transparency.
If the estimate of the total cost of the contract for the required works reaches or exceeds the current EU threshold of 5.0 million. € (125 million Open or restricted procurement procedures at European level are always required.
In exceptional cases, a negotiated procedure or a competitive dialogue shall be admissible.
If the construction project reaches the EU limit, the contracting authority may deviate to a limited extent from the European Procurement Procedure by issuing a national procedure if the total value of the relevant part is below 1.0 million. € (£25m) And the total value of all parts does not exceed 20% of the value of the entire contract estimate.
Share construction project or intentionally to estimate its cost too low, with the intention to avoid the fundamental obligation to write out a european tender procedure is not permitted.
The choice of the type of management is very important for the Prevention of corruption, since the restriction of competition significantly increases the risk of manipulation.
Therefore, an important part of the procurement documentation is the detailed justification of the type of procedure chosen, in particular in relation to the obligation to apply European tendering law.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries fully implement EU legal requirements for procurement procedures and limits into their national laws.
Different provisions
The Czech Republic has established the principle of equal validity of open and narrower procedures, as well as for procurement procedures at national level.
Open and narrower procedures can be chosen at all times, while other types of proceedings are allowed only when the statutory conditions are met.
In contrast to the Czech regulation, the relevant German regulation of budgetary law and the principles of prevention of corruption prefers open proceedings or a public invitation to participate in proceedings.
Other types of management, including limited management, shall only be admissible exceptionally if permitted by legislation.
Such exceptions shall be justified and documented.
The principle preference of the open procedure has a guarantee, that is, to the maximum extent prevented the restriction of competition and that there is limited opportunity for manipulation (pre-selected specific candidates).
In Germany, this principle of public procurement is central to the Prevention of corruption.
The correct estimation of the expected price of the contract is an important basis for the decision on the corresponding type of Procurement Procedure.
When estimating the cost of projects of road construction authorities in Germany can rely on the budget and cost databases of public administrations and other organizations.
These have been compiled on the basis of the analysis of completed construction projects and include, inter alia, standard cost values for the types of buildings, building units, building parts and sub-construction work.
Based on such standard cost values, it is possible to estimate the value of the contract of the planned project or construction work.
Only a few construction administrations in Germany already have a similar database for road construction.
However, the database is expected to be expanded nationally.
Contracting entities in the Czech Republic do not use any central database or average prices of comparable objects to determine the expected cost of public procurement for construction.
In many cases, the cost determination is based on an estimate of the body financing the project or on the value of the resources available to that body.
Meanwhile, standardization measures are at an early stage.
On the basis of the Anti-Corruption Programme for the period 2011 to 2012, the relevant ministries are to draw up a database of the usual prices for standardised commodities.
The application of the pricing system to determine the expected price of the contract is determined by a new regulation ordering the establishment in detail of the subject-matter of the contract.
The pricing system should serve as a set of information on construction and assembly works, materials and products and other data in order to calculate the necessary costs and to determine unit prices.
The Ministry of Transport issued normative prices for transport structures in order to check them, which are regularly updated.
The database is intended for determining the price of the project (investment) plan and should play a bridging function in other stages of the preparation of the construction work.
Main BRH control findings
Selection of the procurement procedure
Controlled entities generally have not entered the contract in an open procedure or in the form of a public call for participation and were in accordance with the requirements of budgetary and procurement legislation.
In 2011, the share of public competitions in the total volume of federal construction projects in the field of land construction was 59.5 %.
In road construction, this proportion was 94.8%.
The BRH found that in some cases there was insufficient justification for the use of non-public competition.
In the case of printed checks BRH found on the basis of information collected from more than 16 000 management limited management has a clear disadvantage in comparison with the public management and public challenge and the limited control also increase the risk of manipulation and corruption.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
According to the BRH study, tender prices were 6% to 10% higher in restricted procedures and negotiated procedures than in public procedures.
Parallel studies of the Ministry of construction and the provincial control Court confirmed differences in value for money received in public and limited management.
A study by the Ministry of construction even found that prices in limited proceedings were twice as high as those in public proceedings.
Compliance with EU limits
For projects whose total contract value was estimated at more than 5 million. € (125 million As a rule, the contracting authorities under scrutiny have drawn up tender plans indicating which works will be awarded in the European Procurement Procedure and which in the National procedure.
According to the tender plans, the proportion of works awarded under European rules always exceeded 80% of the total work.
There was no case of circumvention of the European Management requirement by way of an exorbitantly low cost estimate.
However, in some cases the minimum share for the pan-European procedure was not achieved as a result of the calculation error.
In the course of carrying out the work, some contracting entities unlawfully changed the allocation plan of contracts.
They did not justify these changes and did not demonstrate that the minimum share of the European procedure would subsequently be respected.
As a rule, the share of European management by project accounts was lower than that provided for in the procurement plan.
Where the expected values of construction project contracts exceeded European limits, contracting entities did not apply the European procedure to all individual sub-parts of a value exceeding 1 million. € (£25m) CZK).
Instead, they awarded the relevant contracts on the basis of a national procedure, without giving any valid reasons for the need to deviate from the requirement.
Sao
Selection of the type of Procurement Procedure
In the case of several large construction projects (e.g. the construction of a road section, the equipment for a big sporting event, and construction of housing) the contracting authority has divided one project into several parts, although these sub-contracts were of the same or of a similar nature.
The division reduced the expected value of the contract, and the contracts were awarded in a less demanding mode or even out of the law mode.
Methods of calculating the estimated price
The price normatives applicable to road construction projects have not yet been an effective tool for determining the expected price.
They were based on the prices indicated in the completed procedures, which were, however, burdened by wastefulness and excessive profits of suppliers.
The Sao found that the actual prices for three parts of the road circuit were about 37% lower than these price normatives.
The ministry of transport has to update directives in relation not only to prices of the past, but also in comparison with other comparable markets and the price developments.
For terrestrial buildings, the estimated price was based on the budget of the project carried out by architects or the investor's estimate.
The actual price then differed significantly from the expected price.
The projected cost of building a large library was twice as high as the contract price, but increased by £ 54m over the course of implementation. CZK, i.e. 27 %.
Similarly, for the construction of the depository of this library, the contractual price was 33% lower than the expected price.
In other cases, the price of the successful applicant was higher than the estimated price and increased even more during the implementation.
For the construction of a large library, it was about 400 miles. CZK, i.e. 22 %. For the construction of the palace of justice, the actual price during the implementation of the construction increased disproportionately (by 139 %) compared with an increase in functional areas (by only 12 %).
Summary
Both countries have implemented the european provisions on the choice of the type of the procurement procedure and the respect for european limits into their national laws, so the relevant national legislation of both countries are almost identical.
The principle of public management in Germany is however stricter than the european regulation and the current national treatment in the Czech republic.
Compared with the strict procurement procedures gives the public tender or public invitation to participate the possibilities of a greater number of competitors to participate in a procurement procedure.
These types of procurement generate a large number of offers that guarantee the best effect of value for money.
Prevention of corruption is significantly strengthened, as the circle of candidates is not limited by the decisions of advance adopted by the contracting authority, which thus gives room for manipulation and fixation of prices between the candidates.
Studies have confirmed the benefits of the German preference clause for open procedures or public calls for participation.
Czech legislation allows contracting authorities to award contracts in open or restricted procedures.
However, the latest legislation in the Public Procurement Act imposes a prohibition on contracting authorities to limit the number of tenderers in shortlisted procedures.
The narrower proceedings have now come very close to open proceedings.
In Germany, the contracting authority is largely complied with the requirement of preference for open proceedings or public calls for competition, while in the Czech Republic some projects were divided in violation of the law, in order to circumvent the requirement for the selection of the relevant type of Procurement Procedure.
However, for some projects implemented in Germany, European limits were not respected, which resulted in a lack of a minimum share in pan-European proceedings.
In the Czech republic has not yet established a satisfactory system to facilitate the correct calculation of the expected costs of construction works and projects.
In cases where this is in place, should the contracting entities through extenzivnějších checks to ensure that the requirements for the selection of the type of the procurement procedure and the volume of contracts awarded in the european proceedings have been met, or should create such conditions which are necessary to enable the correct calculation of expected costs.
Preliminary information and notice of initiation
Where contracts are awarded under the European procedure, the contracting authority shall publish a procurement report.
Preliminary information and award notices are an important basis for European competition.
Requirements for European law and Prevention of corruption
By means of preliminary notifications, the contracting authority must indicate the basic specifications of the projects envisaged.
Pre-notifications are required in the case of projects, which is an estimate of the total cost equal to or greater than the european limit, and if the contracting authority wishes to shorten the deadline for the submission of tenders in individual procurement procedures.
The contracting authority is obliged to publish a procurement notice with detailed information for all public contracts requiring European procedures.
The information shall be binding on the contracting authority after publication.
Among other things, the notification shall include specifications, deadlines for the procedure and for the completion of the contract, specific requirements and selection criteria and their weights.
A common public procurement dictionary must be used to describe the subject-matter of the contract.
Preliminary information and contract notices are published in the EU in the Official Journal of the EU and on the profile of the contracting authority.
In order to prevent discrimination against foreign bidders do not have the notification at the national level contain no additional information and is not to be published before sending the text of the notice to the publications Office of the EU.
Incomplete or inaccurate information in the preliminary notification can violate competition or even facilitate manipulation.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries have fully implemented EU provisions on preliminary information and procurement notices in their national legislation.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic, preliminary information and notifications must also be published in the case of contracts for which a European procedure is not required.
The procurement procedure shall not commence until one month after the submission of the prior notification.
Prior information may be waived only in exceptional cases.
In Germany, preliminary information is not required in cases where European proceedings are not necessary.
In the case of national proceedings, the public call must be published on the federal government's website, and, if appropriate, in the press.
In the case of restricted procedures without competition participants the notice must be published in the case where the estimated contract price is equal to or higher than 25 000 € (625 ths. Czk).
Preliminary notifications must explain all planned parts of the project.
This is an important requirement given the number of small contracts in Germany.
Dividing projects into smaller parts is not in the Czech republic so frequent and this measure is considered less important.
Main control findings
BRH
Prior notification
The contracting authorities published a preliminary notice on the projects, which included the work to be commissioned in the European procedure.
In certain open procedures, shortened time period, although the number of days between sending a pre-notification and sending the notification of the contract was less than 52 days.
In the case of other shortened procedures, the annual time limits applicable to the preliminary information have expired and should be renewed.
In many cases, the preliminary notification did not indicate the expected division of construction works into multiple parts.
Contract notice
Some notifications contained the codes from a common dictionary, which deviate from the content of the advance notification or did not provide specifications of the work to be implemented.
In rare cases, the notification at the national level include more information, e.g. regarding the deadlines, or were published before publication of a notice in the Official journal of the EU.
Ex-ante transparency
One sponsor hired an outside company to publish the national notice.
It posted a notice on its platform, the use of which was charged.
Sponsor but didn't check if this company must comply with the requirement to send a further notification to free online government portal.
The sample found that only a third of the notices were actually published on the government portal.
Sao
Contract notice
In the construction of the sewage treatment plant, the contracting authority did not set out the criteria for the contractor to reduce a large number of tenders for the evaluation procedure in the notice of a shortlist for the contractor.
The method of selection (reduction) of offers for evaluation has not been able to prove by the contracting authority.
The reduction in the number of offers was made possible by previous legislation.
During the construction of the ring road, the sponsor for one of the buildings failed to identify in the notice of initiation of the restricted procedure or in the qualification documentation the value by which it will assess the degree of compliance with the qualification criteria or the number of candidates who will be invited.
The sponsor assessed the compliance with the qualification requirements so that all six candidates under the restricted procedure it come true, but one of them ruled out with the fact that he fulfilled up to the last sixth place.
Procedure the contracting authority has not been transparent, as in advance, disclose information about what data on qualifications will be evaluated and how.
Publication of calls
In the case of construction modifications in the former military ujezdas, the contracting authority, contrary to the law, did not publish a written invitation to tender.
Conclusions and recommendations / summary
A two-stage information process with advance information and the publication of the notice of initiation is an important tool to meet the requirements of the transparency and the strengthening of the competitive environment, applicable in the european proceedings.
By extending the obligation to publish preliminary information in the Czech Republic also for national procurement procedures and by strengthening this obligation in Germany in cases of limited procedures, both countries have increased the transparency of procurement procedures and improved the competitive environment.
Selection of candidates in limited procurement procedures
Compared to the open procedure does not allow restricted tender participation of all potential bidders, who would be interested.
In restricted procedures, the contracting authority shall first select potential suppliers who will be asked to submit a tender.
Requirements for European law and Prevention of corruption
EU provisions allow limiting the number of candidates in European restricted procedures.
The restricted procedure, however, requires at least five candidates who will be invited to submit a tender, and in the case of negotiated procedure with publication must be asked at least three potential candidates.
In any case, the number of tenderers invited must be broad enough to guarantee genuine competition.
The selection criteria must be objective and non-discriminatory and must be published in advance.
Selection of potential candidates who will be invited, it is very prone to manipulation, e.g. the preferences of some of them.
Reducing competition to several bidders may ease their collusion.
This has a negative impact on the outcome of the proceedings.
Therefore, the contracting authority must take measures to prevent manipulation and to make sure that it has effective control, that such a procedure was transparent and credible.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
The provisions for the selection of candidates are similar in both countries.
In addition to the requirements of the European directive, contracting entities should replace the tenderers which are invited to submit tenders.
It is also not permissible to limit competition from a regional point of view.
Contracting entities shall document and justify the selection of tenderers and the selection process.
Different provisions
In Germany, at least three tenderers are required to be invited in the case of a restricted procedure and several suitable tenderers in the case of a negotiated procedure.
Except in two cases, the new Czech rules do not allow limiting the number of contenders addressed in the case of a closer and negotiated procedure.
In Germany, when choosing candidates, it is necessary to respect the"principle of four eyes".
While one worker proposes a list of them, another must substantially modify the proposal, e.g. by deleting the proposed tenderer or placing another.
This is intended to prevent a situation where an individual can definitively determine the circle of candidates who take part in the procedure.
If such a provision is not introduced, a far-reaching unlawful agreement between the participants is allowed.
The list of tenderers to be invited to submit a tender shall be confidential and shall not be divulged.
Authorized independent experts are also obliged to do so.
There is no similar or confidential treatment of the list of candidates in the Czech Republic.
According to German provisions, they may not designate candidates from outside companies, but may make proposals to the contracting authority.
There is no similar requirement in the Czech Republic.
Main control findings
BRH
Number of candidates
Except in a few cases, the requirement to reach a minimum number of candidates has been met.
Analysis of nearly 7 000 enter the building with a value to the national limit showed that in the case of restricted procedures, the contracting authorities have called on an average of 6.6 potential candidates and in the case of direct negotiated procedure in an average of 4.4 candidates.
Change of suppliers and regional restrictions
In particular, contracting entities did not change the scope of the contenders addressed in the area of building construction because they had good experience with those with whom they had worked so far.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Authorities argued that in case of non-public proceedings have the guarantee that the appeal applicant, the suitability of which is already pre-assured.
Although there was no evidence of unlawful regional restrictions, the number of candidates in non-public proceedings included a greater proportion of regional candidates than in the case of public proceedings.
Contracting entities explained this by the low contract amount compared to public procurement and the high cost of travel for potential bidders.
Principle of cross-checking and proposals of self-employed professionals
Contracting entities mostly ignored the obligation to change the list of candidates proposed by self-employed professionals.
They argued, in particular, lack of staff, time pressure or inadequate knowledge of a suitable candidate.
In many cases, the records did not reveal who proposed the candidate who was asked to participate in the proceedings.
Check some of the samples showed that the list of potential candidates was created by self-employed experts and the contracting entity was adopted without changes.
Thus, contracting entities did not protect themselves sufficiently from potential manipulation.
Confidentiality of treatment of lists of potential tenderers
In one sponsor was guided by a list of candidates for invitation to tender in the database, which should all employees anytime access.
It allowed the manipulation or unauthorized disclosure of the names of envisaged or adopted candidates, who could then agree on a price.
Documentation
The dossier cited the reasons for the selection of candidates in only a few cases.
Sao
Criteria for selection of candidates
During the construction of the ring road shouldn't the candidates information about what the data about their qualifications will be evaluated and how.
For actions related to the development and modernisation of waterways and ports, the award procedure notice for participation in the shortlist did not set criteria for limiting the number of tenderers.
All eight bidders met the qualification requirements, but this exceeded the number to which the contracting authority restricted participation in the procurement procedure.
The commission then conducted the selection of candidates by random selection – by drawing lots, which was at that time legal.
This procedure should have been mentioned as a criterion already in the contract notice.
Summary
With regard to the high risk of manipulation in the selection of the winning bidder in the restricted procurement procedures to introduce both countries, special measures for preventing the illicit restriction of competition.
