The German rules restrict such opportunities to the manipulations using the so-called cross-checking (principle of four eyes) by respecting the confidentiality of the list of candidates and using prohibition to make proposals for the selection of candidates to external companies.
The Czech rules aim to prevent potential restrictions with the aim of manipulation mainly by an unlimited number of applicants.
Control however found that part of the said rules has not been sufficiently applied and that undue restriction of the set of candidates was in some cases prevented.
Contracting entities are obliged to completely eliminate the deficiencies mentioned.
Submission of tenders
Phase of the procurement procedure, in which potential bidders to develop a bid based on the tender documentation received, starts with the publication of information about the procurement procedure and/or challenge applicants.
By the date of opening of the envelopes, prospective tenderers may submit their tenders to the contracting authority in order to apply for the award of the contract.
Requirements for European law and Prevention of corruption
EU law does not prescribe specific requirements at this stage of the procurement procedure.
The sponsor must follow the national rules governing this stage of the procedure and prevent potential manipulation.
Those provisions shall apply in particular to the organisation and control.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
The principle applies that tender documents on the basis of which potential suppliers make their offers must always be sent by the contracting authority.
Design offices that are interested in management should not perform this role.
The contracting authority shall ensure that all candidates have received the same information during this stage of the procurement procedure.
In the case of ambiguities in the specification or raises further questions, information tenderers may add only the sponsor.
The design offices responsible for drawing up the procurement documents may not provide any information.
Any contact between the design office and the tenderers must be avoided throughout this phase.
They must remain anonymous throughout the course because allowing contact with them can adversely affect the competition.
Tenders sent by post or submitted directly must be submitted in a closed envelope.
Electronically submitted offers must be encoded.
Different provisions
In Germany, the sponsor may instruct the insured to a supplier of external services print and distribution documentation, and their employees shall be bound to comply with the confidentiality agreement.
In Germany it must be received tenders marked with an indication of the date of receipt and directly and immediately handed over in original condition (sealed) official, who is entrusted with their safekeeping.
This worker may not be involved in the procurement procedure.
The received offers must be locked until the date of opening of the envelopes.
In the Czech Republic, the offers received are marked with a serial number.
The sponsor exposes a message with details about the competition including numbers, deals and information on developing bids and receipt.
There are no special regulations on the safekeeping of offers.
Main control findings
BRH
BRH controlled the assignment of the administrative building.
Sending of procurement documents
Controlled entities building management sent the tender documentation, either directly or commissioned the printing and distribution of the external company.
Self-employed persons did not send any documentation.
Information provided to tenderers
For the part of the procurement documents relating to questioning and obtaining information, the contracting authority did not follow the rule of separate planning from the procurement procedure.
In violation of relevant regulations often in the documentation did it state the names of their contact workers, but rather employees of the department of project management.
Some of the tender notices even included the names of the companies or self-employed persons involved in the preparation of the tender documentation.
In isolated cases, candidates who asked questions during the procurement procedure did not receive identical information.
Labelling of tenders
For contracting entities, all received tenders have been stamped and confirmation of receipt.
However, in some cases, the negotiated procedure tenders were accepted by self-employed professionals, in violation of rule one of the construction prevention of corruption.
Custody of the tenders
Once marked, not all tenders were passed on directly and without delay to the official assigned to keep them in custody locked the tenders in a steel cabinet.
For one contracting authority, bids were temporarily placed in the open glove compartment of the mailroom, to which all employees had access.
Another sponsor placed the mailbox in the hallway without constant supervision, and part of the offers thrown into the mailbox remained there overnight.
The opening of the box was wide and unsecured, so it was accessible not only to employees.
Sao
The SAO has not identified deficiencies in this area.
Summary
In both countries there are established rules to prevent the contacts, in particular between the interested companies and design offices, which collaborate in the procurement process, and throughout the process.
Equal treatment is ensured by sending the same information to all tenderers.
For the receipt, storage and confidentiality of offers, rules are suitable for preventing manipulation and corruption.
In Germany, the relevant requirements are somewhat more developed than in the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the accumulated control records showed violations of the rules in some areas.
These irregularities can be easily corrected.
Opening envelopes
Opening envelopes
During the opening of envelopes, bids that have not yet been closed are opened, their content is read and published.
The period for which the applicant is his bound, starting at the moment of the expiry of the deadline for the submission of the envelopes or their opening and ends with the date designated by the sponsor.
Requirements for European law and Prevention of corruption
European legislation does not contain any specific provisions concerning the opening of envelopes.
However, national laws and regulations contain extensive requirements for the protection of tenders and competition during this sensitive phase of the entire procurement procedure.
The principles of" more eyes", transparency and credibility of the envelope opening process are intended to prevent manipulations and modifications of already submitted offers.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
The opening of envelopes must be carried out by several persons appointed by the sponsor.
Compliance with the principle of "more eyes" is intended to prevent individuals from hidden manipulation of offers.
Candidates may be present when opening envelopes.
When opening, all envelopes must be placed before the president of the commission and opened one by one.
Late bids received must not be taken into account.
In order to ensure transparency in the opening of envelopes, this stage, including the conclusions (results), must be recorded in writing. The record shall include, inter alia, the names of the tenderers and the prizes offered.
The minutes must be read and signed by the head of the group.
Registration may also be signed by the candidates present.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic, a commission is established for the opening of envelopes.
The participation of independent experts shall be permitted.
Members of the commission may also be entrusted with deliberations at subsequent stages of the procedure, i.e. evaluation of tenders.
In Germany, the opening of envelopes takes place in the presence of the head and the writer.
The manager must be an employee of the sponsor.
The head and in the case of civil engineering and registrar shall not be participants in the preparatory phase (creation of the tender documentation), shall decide on the award of the contract and shall not be members in the subsequent processing (procedure) of the contract.
German regulations require that the minutes of the opening of the envelopes contained not only bid prices, but also any information about discounts and special (unusual) symptoms, e.g., damaged envelope, upon receipt of or late received bids.
In the Czech Republic, in addition to the tender prices, the registration must include an indication of the language of the tender and the tenderer's signature.
German regulations require that all parts of the opened envelopes were marked so as to avoid subsequent changes.
Deals, as a rule, marked in the form of a perforation indicating the date, must be held after the end of the opening of the envelopes as confidential (secret) and may be disclosed only to persons, which is further processed.
Similar measures do not exist in the Czech Republic.
If a single offer is received in the Czech Republic, the envelope must not be opened and the tenderer must be notified immediately.
In Germany, they do not have this adjustment, and if a single offer is accepted, it is opened and evaluated.
Main control findings
BRH
Principle of cross-checking
During the opening of envelopes, the sponsors adhered to the principle of four eyes.
Always there was a leader and a writer, to whom no other role was assigned.
However, in isolated cases, for small proceedings, natural persons opened tenders sent to them, without the participation of the contracting authority.
The course of opening envelopes
opening envelopes has not always documented progress.
In some cases, bids filed late were not marked, and in some cases signatures were missing.
Labelling of tenders received
Contracting entities marked offers of perforations with a date, which was in accordance with the requirements.
Some have flagged bids incorrectly in the past,but have changed practice after the BRH warning.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Sao
Time limit for receipt of tenders
At one event, the bidder's offer was handed over to the contracting authority with a monthly delay, and he nevertheless accepted it.
Summary
The essential parts of the envelope opening provisions are identical in both countries with regard to the principle of "more eyes" and the principle of transparency, and thus allow to substantially reduce the risk of corruption and manipulation.
The German rules are more complex compared to the Czech Republic, especially the requirements for accurate documentation of the procedure.
Marking, safe storage and respect for the confidentiality of tenders significantly limit the possibility of subsequent changes in the tenders submitted.
In addition, the workers responsible for opening envelopes may not carry out any other activities related to the contract to be awarded.
The findings, despite the detection of some irregularities, confirm that the rules for opening envelopes are largely applied.
Assessment and evaluation of tenders
The contracting authority must review and evaluate the tenders received within the specified time limit.
At the same time, they must award the contract to the tenderer who best meets the award criteria in the tender.
Requirements for European law and Prevention of corruption
EU law sets out the process of assessing and evaluating bids in several steps:
The first step is to check the suitability of candidates.
They must have a good economic and financial position and the required professional and technical knowledge and skills.
Tenderers who have sometimes been convicted of bribery or defraud must always be excluded from the procurement procedures.
Deals nevyloučených candidates must be evaluated in terms of numerical accuracy, technical suitability and value for money on the basis of previously published award criteria.
The contracting authority must determine the most economically favourable offer and, in particular, examine all significantly low price offers.
Review and evaluation is particularly sensitive and prone to manipulation.
For example, candidates may be excluded without a legitimate reason, or bids that do not meet the requirements may be left in the competition.
The outcome of the evaluation may be improperly influenced by the prioritisation or disadvantage of a tenderer, thereby preventing the selection of the most economically advantageous tender.
The contracting authority must therefore adopt special measures in choosing the persons included in the process and must make sure that they meet the requirements for integrity and technical knowledge.
They also need to make sure that the whole process and decisions taken are transparent and credible.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
In line with EU requirements, the relevant provisions in both countries require the review and evaluation of tenders in step-by-step.
During the evaluation must not be changed the requirements for proof of suitability of tenderers, evaluation criteria and their weights specified in the notice or in the tender documentation.
The criteria laid down for assessing the suitability of tenderers may not be further applied.
Further evaluation can be carried out only on the basis of evaluation criteria.
The tenders submitted shall first be investigated from a formal point of view, whether they are complete or do not include if the suspicious elements that could encourage the manipulation.
If there are candidates from further review and evaluation by them of the submitted tenders excluded, must be informed without delay.
If it is the result of the evaluation of tenders, the findings of abnormally low tender prices, must be given to the candidates the opportunity to comment on the situation before the eventual decommissioning of its menu.
The reasons for the decision must be documented in a transparent manner.
Different provisions
In Germany, candidates must maintain confidentiality and only authorised persons may participate in the evaluation of tenders.
The mathematical accuracy of bids can only be reviewed by the sponsor.
A rating may be assigned only to employees who are not integrated into the decision-making phase of choosing a supplier or the implementation phase of the project.
There are no precise provisions on who can carry out further reviews and evaluations.
If external companies are entrusted with reviewing and evaluating bids, they must be aware that the bids are confidential and respectfully respect this fact.
They may only make proposals for decisions to the sponsor.
In the Czech republic tenders must be reviewed and evaluated by the commission, appointed by the contracting authority, which shall draw up a report with a proposal for the conclusion of the contract.
However, in both countries, the final decision depends on the sponsor.
If you are in Germany, the documents and statements required in connection with the submission of the tenders incomplete, the applicants concerned must then submit the required documents within six days.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
If the tenderers fail to fulfil this obligation, their tenders shall be excluded.
In the Czech Republic, the contracting authority may decide whether to give the tenderer the opportunity to supplement the missing documents.
If the candidate does not submit them, he must be expelled.
In Germany, it is necessary to review not only the total price, but also the unit price.
If the pricing structure of the menu shows that prices for a part of the overall project were estimated to disproportionately high or low, applicants must be asked for an explanation.
If they do not provide an explanation and if the contracting authority can demonstrate that the tender contains compensatory prices, such tenders must be excluded.
It is intended to prevent bidders submission of price calculations based on the assumption that for each part of the overall project will be made in substantial quantitative changes, which can lead to a significant increase in the cost of the project.
In the Czech Republic, the total price of the work is evaluated, and the prices of individual parts are not examined in detail.
Valuation compensation is not a reason to exclude the offer.
In Germany, a contract cannot be awarded to a tenderer who offers a disproportionately high or low price.
If one or several offers budget differ by 10 % or more compared to the price estimated by the contracting entity, or compared to other bids, the tenderers must demonstrate that their offer was plausible and convincing zkalkulována.
If they are unable to do so, the sponsor should exclude them.
In the Czech republic may be tender after the price review is revoked, unless they have been received only bids with unreasonably low prices and bidders, these prices nezdůvodnili.
If the tender price is substantially higher than the estimate of the contracting authority, is not a reason for refusing to specify to the tenderers the contract (unlike the German procurement law).
If there is a suspicion in Germany of conduct intended to restrict competition, the Sponsor shall report this to the competent superior authority without delay.
The latter must decide on the next procedure and if it is appropriate to inform the antitrust office or law enforcement authorities.
Furthermore, it must approve (e.g., when a contract exceeds 50 000 € and the contract has been awarded to the bidder with the lowest bid), whether the contract will be awarded during the discussion of the contract or whether the tender procedure shall be cancelled.
The Czech rules do not regulate this area.
Main control findings
BRH
Verification of suitability and award criteria
Most of the procurement procedures examined were in compliance with the relevant requirements.
In the case of certain recommendations of potential suppliers, made by self-employed persons, not themselves contracting authorities the suitability of the applicants.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
In some cases, the procurement procedures has not been submitted sufficient documentation about it, whether in the choice of taking the sponsor shall consider all of the published assessment criteria or whether the selection decision was based only on the criterion of price.
Selection of stakeholders and confidentiality of offers
Some contracting authorities use the services of unauthorised persons, for example, self-employed workers or employees of construction authorities.
You have been included in the planning or implementation process of construction projects, to perform the functions which should be held exclusively by the sponsor.
Authorities tried to justify this fact, your lack of human resources in the sector.
In some cases, the use of self-employed professionals to review offers the services of persons who were not formally bound to respect the confidentiality of tenders and to perform with due care the performance of its obligations resulting from the contract.
As for the contracting authorities, as a rule, the absence of conclusive evidence on whether the menu in the custody of self-employed experts were available only to the designated persons.
Review and mathematical check of tenders
Some contracting authorities handed the open envelope to further examination of self-employed professionals, without having first conducted the prescribed examination of the tenders and math review and without documented results of these checks.
In the event of any intent to manipulate, third parties may have made changes to tenders which could not have been identified by the contracting authority.
The examination of documents revealed a number of cases where unusual elements in the tenders were not adequately marked or where price and product data were missing.
Performance audits
Model checking one sponsor revealed that in 75 % of cases of procurement procedures is advantageous tender deviated by more than 10 % from the pre-estimated cost.
One of the twenty tendering procedures was cancelled due to inadequate tender prices.
In many cases, there was a lack of evidence or sufficient documentation to verify bids or negotiate with bidders for further clarification.
In many cases, detailed information such as unit prices of the most important invoiced items was also missing.
Changes in market prices or increases in material costs were often cited as the reason for the derogations.
Contracting entities have argued that identifying and demonstrating countervailing prices is difficult.
In the case of one invitation to tender made by an entity outside the scope of normal contracting authorities, a 66% lower price was offered compared to the original cost estimate.
No data were recorded on the closer examination of the cost or on the identification of the reasons for the deviations.
When clarifying this question, find sponsor no hint of price-dumping by the applicant, which contract was eventually awarded.
It was therefore not clarified whether the initial cost estimate was exorbitant or whether the price offered was too low.
Later, the sponsor classified this bidder as a" low-cost company " that was unable to meet either qualitative requirements or terms.
In another procurement procedure, the contracting authority awarded the contract to a tenderer whose price was 35% higher than the original cost estimate.
The sponsor did not cancel the tender procedure and featured the unfounded argument that the said candidate would be expected that the determination of their prices set at a disproportionately high cost.
Suspected irregularities
Two cases of irregularities were found with one contracting authority and they were reported to the firm responsible for technical supervision.
In one Procurement Procedure, two bidders submitted bids containing an identical price calculation, which prompted the contracting authority to exclude both bids.
The checks have not shown any significant deficiencies in the application of other provisions.
Sao
Verification of suitability
In many construction events, such as university buildings, roads and railways, contracting entities shall exclude the tenderer from participation in a procurement procedure, although they did not meet the requirements of the contracting entity indicated in tender conditions, or they did not substantiate qualifications to the extent required, or, conversely, one submitter failed to substantiate or explain the reason for delisting candidate, which requirements it meets.
Evaluation
For the construction of the wastewater treatment plant, the individual award criteria for the contractor were established, but the contracting authority did not respect them during the procedure.
For the action in the field of railway infrastructure development, the weighting of the award criteria was not established at the start of the procedure, but only at the beginning of the evaluation.
For the road repair project, the evaluation of the "shortening of construction time" criterion was not done correctly.
Bidders in second and third place were incorrectly assessed for a greater reduction in the construction time than indicated in their bids.
Documentation of the reasons for choosing a candidate
The contracting authority did not establish, on the basis of what criteria it assessed the tenders received and how it selected the most suitable of them.
Correctness of selection of contractors of small-scale contracts associated with the construction of a road circuit with an estimated price of up to 500 thousand.
Czk was not possible to verify, as the suppliers were selected only on the basis of telephone consultation about the price and date of performance, evidence of these negotiations, however, were not provided.
Summary
In both countries, the rules for validating and evaluating offers correspond to EU requirements.
However, they differ with regard to the specific steps of management and the selection of individuals in the management included.
Unlike the Czech republic, in Germany, these steps of the procurement process governed by stricter and more detailed requirements, especially with regard to the application of the universal principle and the protection of the tenders.
The same applies to the rules for verifying the appropriateness of the prices offered.
In both countries, in some cases, the inspections found that the essential process steps in the verification and evaluation of tenders were not at all documented, and if yes, then only partially.
The Absence of control instruments and transparency in decision-making during the examination and evaluation of tenders allows manipulation.
Checks have shown serious defects, such as the transmission of tenders to third parties without prior due verification and documenting of tenders by the contracting authority.
If the authorities delegated to a third party the performance of functions associated with the screening and evaluation of tenders, are necessary corresponding measures and enhanced control measures against the increased possibility of manipulation.
In checking the validity of prices, the German contracting authorities controlled did not use in all cases a complete set of available instruments and did not deal with their own pricing structure.
In the Czech Republic, deficiencies were identified in the assessment of the suitability of tenders and the application of evaluation criteria.
Completion of the procurement procedure
After examination and evaluation of tenders, the procurement process is completed by award of the contract or cancellation of the procedure.
Requirements for European law and Prevention of corruption
In the case of the European procedure, all tenderers must be informed in advance of the award decision.
Suppliers shall have the opportunity to review the decision taken within a limited period of 10 or 15 days and to request its review, where appropriate.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The period of 10 days shall apply to electronic submissions and 15 days to other submissions.
The contract shall not be concluded before the expiry of that period or before the decision of the review procedure.
If the review body rejects the complaint and confirms the decision, candidates and tenderers must be given the opportunity to have the application of the tendering law reviewed by an independent court.
This measure ensures that no contracting authority will be able to circumvent the legal protection of suppliers by promptly implementing the decision of the procurement procedure.
The procuring entity shall duly document the conduct of the procedure.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries have implemented information obligations management.
In both countries, the final decision on the outcome of the procurement procedure rests with the contracting authority.
However, the latter cannot arbitrarily deviate from the results of a properly conducted examination and evaluation.
The contracting authority is to conclude a contract within the specified time.
This is due to the fact that the tenderer is not bound by his tender after the expiry of this period.
The content of the contract must not deviate from the winning offer.
Unsuccessful bidders should be informed of the outcome in a timely manner, stating the reason why their bid was not accepted.
Cancellation of the procurement procedure is permissible only if certain conditions are met, e.g. if the prices in the bids do not meet specifications.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic, the mandatory waiting period before the conclusion of the contract 10 or 15 days applies to both European and national procedures.
In Germany, the equivalent provision applies only to European procedures.
In all other procedures in Germany, tenderers may not be informed of the award of the contract before deciding on its EU provisions and the Review Award.
In the Czech republic shall be the procurement procedure shall be cancelled in the case that received only one bid or only one offer meets the requirements for consideration and evaluation.
In Germany shall be awarded the contract, even if it was received only one bid, and provided that the offer meets the conditions set out in the tender documentation and is cost effective.
Main control findings
BRH
The inspections found few irregularities in the completion of the audited procurement processes.
In some cases, companies have received letters of authorisation before the notification period expires, which may invalidate the contract.
In several open procedures, authorising letters also contained modifications incompatible with the content of the tender, such as new deadlines.
In some cases, contracting authorities did not meet the deadlines for awarding the contract.
In one open procedure chosen by the contracting entity a second most advantageous bid, because the bidder offers a price of more than 50 % lower already declined to fulfil the contract for the originally offered price.
Sao
In the reconstruction of and construction of a high school sponsor in one case has not concluded with the contractor of the contract in accordance with the draft agreement contained in the offer to the selected candidate.
For some actions the repair and maintenance of roads, construction of motorways and the ring road contracts have been concluded later than provided by law.
The construction work in the former military újezdech the contracting authority has sent notification about the selection of the most suitable tenders to all tenderers after expiry of the statutory period.
Summary
Both countries have implemented EU rules on the termination of the procurement procedure.
Legal protection of unsuccessful candidates contributes to the reduction of corruption.
The Czech Public Procurement Act includes the Institute of legal protection even in cases of contracts below EU limits.
In both countries, it was found that a limited time limit for the conclusion of the contract was exceeded.
This can cause adverse economic consequences and increase the risk of manipulation.
In the future, contracting entities should eliminate such shortcomings in the conclusion of the procurement procedure.
Documentation, notifications, information obligations
Tender process with all its individual phases, relevant findings and decisions, including the appropriate justification must be transparently documented.
The completion of the procurement procedure at European level must be published.
Data on procurement procedures are summarised in EU statistics.
Requirements for European law and Prevention of corruption
The obligation to document the procurement procedure is in line with the fundamental requirement of the principle of transparency, applied at EU-wide level.
Only the good and time-relevant documentation of choices and reasoning gives a guarantee of transparency in the process of the procurement procedure, and, above all, guarantees an effective legal protection of the interests of each applicant in cases where the value of the contract exceeds the european thresholds.
Appropriate documentation is also an essential part of anti-corruption measures, because the obligation of the detailed justification of individual decisions and their justification significantly reduces the scope for manipulation.
In the case of European procurement procedures, the contracting authority must notify their completion of the EU's Office of Official Publications within 48 days of the date of award of the contract.
The authority publishes the notification in the Official Journal of the EU and thus fulfils the transparency requirement.
The sponsor must summarize the essential information about their procurement procedures and communicate them to the European commission via the competent national ministries.
On this basis, the European Commission publishes annual statistics, which allow to get an overview of the development of the single market in the field of construction.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries fully transpose into their national laws the provisions of european law on the documentation and notification obligations.
The provisions relating to documentation and notification for the purposes of European statistics are almost identical in both countries.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic, the obligation to notify the award of the contract applies not only to European procedures, but also to national procurement procedures.
The deadline for notification is only 15 days from the conclusion of the contract.
In Germany, the obligation of notification of procurement management, in addition to those which are compulsory under european law, applies only to the limited management in excess of the limit of 25 thousand. € (625 ths. Czk) and direct management in excess of the limit of 15 thousand € (375 thous. Rubles) including VAT.
Only interested parties shall be informed below this limit.
Main control findings
BRH
Documentation
A large number of assignments have not been fully documented.
The notification did not contain all the necessary information, such as the reasons for the supply specifications and national rules.
In the case of one management sponsor did not explain why he closed a contract with the bidder whose offer did not contain the mandatory particulars.
In several cases, some of the required records were also missing.
Publication of the award of the contract
In the case of certain European procedures, the contracting authority erred in the publication of the notice.
In the case of several assignments, there was no evidence of publication of the notice.
Notification obligation
Statistically verified files included the required minimum of information and were created and sent on time.
Preliminary transparency
In most cases, the sponsor disclosed information about the outcome of the contract.
In the case of one contracting authority, contract information was not disclosed due to a communication error.
It took the sponsor six months to notice the error.
As a result, the outcome of the proceeding was not disclosed during this time.
Sao
Documentation
For actions relating to the organisation of large sports events have been identified considerable shortcomings in documentation during the procurement procedure, such as incorrect information about the bid prices in the protocols of the meetings of the evaluation commission.
In addition, some documents on the opening of envelopes were not signed.
Publication of the award of the contract
In the preparation of the repair and maintenance of roads, construction of motorways and the ring road was the notice of contract award sent after the deadline, or has not been published.
Summary
The provisions on documentation and reporting and notification obligations include the european requirements and are in both countries almost identical.
This generally ensures transparency of procurement procedures and final selection.
Czech notification obligations are somewhat stricter compared to German ones.
The inspections revealed weaknesses substantially reducing the value of documentation as a means of preventing corruption.

Authorities should continue to strengthen the transparency of its procurement procedures and to fully meet reporting and notification requirements.
Summary evaluation and recommendations
Parallel control of the SAO and BRH were focused on two areas, which are for the procurement process, substantial as in the Czech republic and in Germany, and that the application of the procurement law of the EU and the prevention of corruption.
EU legislation gives an opportunity to international competition within the EU with a view to creating a single European market.
The aim of measures to prevent corruption is not only to avoid it or at least limit it, but also to prevent financial damage and possible losses of confidence in the integrity of government.
Held control of the findings of the two audit institutions – SAO and BRH – having regard to the application of the procurement law of both countries and the comparison of its relevant provisions give an inside look at the common and different elements that can be both countries to assist in the further development and application of the law.
Application of EU procurement law
Both countries transposed EU public procurement law into their national legislation.
In both countries there are important common base for public procurement and fulfillment of fundamental requirements in the areas of: competition; equal treatment of candidates; transparency of procurement procedures.
Contracting entities reinforce these requirements in part by very large measures.
The Czech Republic has laid down provisions on public procurement requiring European procedures as well as those which are below EU limits and are therefore governed by national legislation.
However, checks have shown that contracting entities are not always fully compliant with all relevant provisions of EU requirements.
The German authorities should continue to improve the quality of its procurement procedures, to eliminate the mentioned discrepancies with regard to the implementation of EU requirements.
In the Czech Republic, the checks identified risks affecting economy and achieving value for money.
In particular, the incomplete definition of the object of public procurement, which resulted in additional work, which were often awarded in violation of the law, inadequate definition of the expected prices and further about the required qualifications of narrowing the possible range of applicants and thus decreasing competition, in particular in the field of traffic engineering.
Prevention of corruption
Joint controls were not intended to detect corruption cases.
The reason was that both the BRH and the Sao did not have sufficient tools to do so.
May, however, review whether the competent authorities of both countries shall take measures to limit corruption and manipulation in public procurement and how are these measures applied.
As for the Prevention of corruption, both countries focused on different aspects.
In particular, German provisions give scope for wide and unlimited competition, transparency and controls as a central element of preventing corruption.
In particular, Czech regulations aim at strengthening the transparency of procurement procedures.
BRH
In Germany, there are general principles of prevention of corruption that apply to the entire federal administration.
These principles have also been integrated into public procurement requirements and have been adopted to meet the specific needs of such procurement.
The relevant provisions specify, at times and very accurately, ways to comply with the requirements for the Prevention of corruption during the procurement procedure and the choice of persons incorporated therein.
In the opinion of the BRH is the principle preference of open procurement procedures and calls for the participation of a particularly suitable instrument significantly reducing the risk of corruption in public procurement, while the reduction in competition increases the risk of manipulation.
Analysis of risks and adequate controls (in particular the principle of cross-checks), transparency requirements, documentation of the procurement procedure and various organizational measures are also an effective mechanism for prevention of corruption and manipulation.
Therefore, the BRH does not feel the need for substantial changes to the current provisions that public institutions must comply with in public procurement.
Anti-corruption measures are widely applied in practice.
The irregularities found in some areas highlighted weaknesses in compliance with some requirements.
Therefore, contracting entities should provide their employees with further education, and the relaying is so with anti-corruption requirements and further increase their awareness in this area.
A significant part of the exposed weaknesses relate to activities that the construction administration has delegated to private entrepreneurs.
However, the Absence of adequate controls in delegating powers increases the risk of abuse.
Activities prone to manipulation and corruption should therefore be transmitted to third parties only if the administration has to guarantee a sufficient degree of protection against tampering.
Sao
In the Czech Republic, anti-corruption strategies have been adopted at the government level, which also significantly affect public procurement.
Audit SAO take place in the period, when there was a realisation of one of the most important parts of this strategy, and that significant amendments to the law on public procurement and the adoption of subsequent implementing legislation.
The strategy adopted and the new legislation can be effective steps to improve the state.
Under the new regulations, the sponsor, for example, must justify the effectiveness of the public procurement, determination of the expected value of the contract, the adequacy of the requirements on the qualifications, the determination of the basic evaluation criteria and method of evaluation of tenders and all duly zdokladovat and publish.
Recommendation
Overall, both the SAO and the BRH have favourable views on the ways in which EU requirements are implemented.
Their wide application in practice has confirmed that the EU requirements on competition, equal treatment and transparency form an appropriate basis for public procurement within the EU.
The transnational model, established in the EU, can also serve as a base for similar projects aimed at facilitating and promoting international competition.
Taking into account the large potential of material and intangible damages incurred as a result of manipulation and corruption in connection to public procurement insist BRH and NKU on the fact that it is the duty of contracting authorities to continue the measures against corruption and manipulation and improve them where possible.
Particularly the organizational structure and processes, procurement procedures should be continuously monitored in terms of weaknesses and risks, in order to identify the need for corrective actions and respond appropriately to the.
In comparison with the practice in Germany showed that in the Czech republic should increase the share of open procurement procedures that give the space competition and substantially reduce the possibility of corrupt behaviour.
Procurement may also have a positive impact on the price achieved in parts where it is permissible and appropriate for the contracting authority. A higher number of applicants puts pressure on the price achieved.
The provision of its organisation also affects the procurement process.
In Germany her provide a special state organization, while in the Czech republic it with the exception of the transport structures, organised by the central authorities themselves or through contracting organizations.
Both the SAO and the BRH want to further develop knowledge in their work where it is appropriate and address it with their parliament and government beyond their joint project.
In addition, they are convinced that the principles of the procurement law and their implementation, as described in this report, will be subject to interest even at the level of the International organisation of supreme audit institutions (INTOSAI), as the mentioned principles and findings are of general importance for effective fight against corruption and to guarantee that public contracts are awarded in the mode of a well-functioning and fair competition and that it achieved value for money.

Joint final report on the results of parallel inspections of the excise administration in the SR and the Czech Republic
Joint final report

Introductory word
Presented to the joint report informs of the progress and outcome of international cooperation in the parallel controls, which implement the Supreme audit office of the Slovak republic and the Supreme audit office of the Czech republic, focusing on the administration of excise taxes in the years 2012-2015.
Cooperation between the supreme audit institutions of the two countries was implemented on the basis of the treaty on cooperation among the SAO SR and SAO of the CZECH republic in the performance of parallel audits on the management of excise duties, which was concluded in August 2015.
The theme of the parallel controls were selected on the basis of the fact that both the member states of the EU are based on common european legislation with the aim to find out how it is applied at the national level, how the system is set up the administration of excise duties and what are systems in SLOVAKIA and in the CZECH republic different.
The greatest benefit of the control actions carried out was the exchange of experience, the identification of differences and the detection of good practice.
Last but not least, the benefit was the finding that the international comparability of data on the performance and efficiency of Excise Management is very limited without the implementation of parallel controls.
Miloslav Kala,
Karol Mitrík,

President
Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
on the results of parallel controls of the SPD administration in the SR and the Czech Republic
Summary and evaluation
The legislation on excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic and their administration is in line with EU legislation and significantly exceeds EU requirements.
Between the adjustment of excise taxes in the SR and CR differences were found in the CZECH republic contributes to the effective administration of excise taxes verification of the economic stability of applicants for the issue of permits and the mandatory marking and coloring selected mineral oils and some other oils; IN the SR is the distribution of control marks easier than in the CZECH republic and less burden on the tax administrator.
In the fight against the evasion of excise taxes as a good practice in both countries proved supervision over the movement of raw tobacco or tobacco raw materials, the implementation of the institute's distributor of motor fuel and registration of dealers of consumer packaging of alcohol.
Excise income in the SR and the Czech Republic is growing more slowly than other tax revenues.
The EU's objectives of reducing labour taxation, introducing eco-austerity measures and reducing dependence on tobacco and alcohol have not yet been met in the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic, including because there is no indexation of excise rates in both countries.
This has resulted in reducing the significance of excise taxes in total tax revenues and as a result of the growing purchasing power of the real reduction of the tax burden on consumption taxes.
The introduction of environmental measures become long-term financially supports, however, these measures have a negative impact on revenue from excise taxes, which in the future will need to be replaced by other revenues or by reducing expenditure of the state.
Administrative expenses incurred for the administration of excise taxes in the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA in the long term grow, in particular due to wage growth, and their efficiency decreases.
In SR this efficiency negatively affecting also expenditure on the computerisation of the administration of excise duties (IT expenditure) and the expenditure incurred on wage of employees performing the permanent tax supervision of tax warehouses for alcohol.
The electronisation of excise duty management in the SR did not significantly reduce the number of tax managers.
The Czech Sao and Sao SR recommend that the Sao SR reconsider the merits of the exercise of permanent tax supervision in alcohol tax warehouses.
In the CZECH republic the efficiency of administrative expenditure influenced by the fact that the Customs administration of the CZECH republic has not applied in the audited period, the procedures which would lead to a reduction in personnel performance management excise taxes.
The number of comparable administrative tasks of tax administrators was in the SR and the CZECH republic in the individual years of the period audited similar, yet the number of comparable tax entities is in SR by about one-third lower than in the CZECH republic.
Tax administrators in the Czech Republic perform administrative tasks mainly in the form of physical exercise of tax supervision, while tax administrators in the Czech Republic emphasise remote supervision and risk analysis.
The administration of excise duties in the SR is more administratively demanding than in the Czech Republic and, given the ratio of the number of tax acts to the number of entities, more costly.
The electronization of excise tax administration in the SR and the Czech Republic took place in different areas.
In the SR is fully elektronizována administration of tax declarations for excise taxes, in the CZECH republic are electronically transmitted documents proving the taxation of selected products in free tax circulation.
Both methods of electronization promote effective management of excise taxes, and therefore the Czech Sao and Sao SR recommend applying them not only in both countries.
The total expenditure on the implementation of the EMCS could not be compared, since the FDC provided data on expenditure only for the upgrade of the system in the period 2011-2015, but expenditure was also spent before that period.
Expenditure incurred in that period only for the upgrade EMCS have been in SR for about 20 % higher than the expenditure incurred in the CZECH republic as on the introduction of EMCS, so to upgrade this system for more than ten years.
Excise managers in the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic did not achieve comparable values of qualitative indicators when spending comparable expenses.
The level of supervision is comparable in both countries, but in SR excise management is significantly more resource intensive.
The introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the movement of excisable products (EMCS) occurred to streamline the administration of excise taxes, however, in the SR in a lower extent, since the introduction of the system and its modernization have been incurred significantly higher expenses than in the CZECH republic.
Basic information
Cooperation between the two audit institutions took place on the basis of the Agreement on cooperation in the implementation of parallel checks aimed at the administration of the excise tax of 18. 8. 2015.
The Czech Sao and Sao SR agreed to carry out parallel checks, which will primarily focus on the issue of Excise Management and the results of which will allow analysis, comparison and evaluation of the facts identified.
Common audit issues were agreed on which parallel controls were based.
Characteristics of the subject and objectives of parallel control:
The aim of the parallel controls was to compare the performance of excise managers, taking into account qualitative and quantitative indicators, and to identify weaknesses in the Excise Management Process.
In particular, the following main audit questions should have been answered:
Did the excise administrators in the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic achieve comparable qualitative indicators when spending comparable expenses?
Has the introduction of the excise Movement and Control System (EMCS) made excise management more efficient and the expenditure incurred in implementing it effectively?
Carried out parallel controls should be identified the causes of the significant differences affecting the efficiency and effectiveness of tax administration in the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA, in particular in the field of legislation and in the adjustment of the organizational structure.

Legislation for excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic
Excise legislation is divided into the level of EU legislation (see annex 1) and the level of national legislation (see Annex 2).
Council directive 2008/118/EC concerning the general arrangements for excise duty and repealing directive 92/12/EEC, defines the excise tax and determines the basic rules for the management of taxes and management of energy products and electricity, tobacco products, alcohol and alcoholic beverages.
This directive makes it possible to impose taxes on consumption on other products.
The EU legislation regulates in particular the minimum conditions for: the amount of tax rates for individual types of the selected products, the production, storage, processing and holding of products subject to the tax, chargeability, exemption from tax and refund of taxes, the supervision of the transport of selected products between the EU member states, international cooperation and maintenance of the register of economic operators and tax warehouses.
EU legislation allows to introduce control procedures and institutes at the national level provided that they do not distort competition.
Excise tax legislation in the Czech Republic
Definition of legislation in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic excise tax legislation is concentrated in the excise tax Act (Act No. 353/2003 Coll.) which regulates the administration of mineral oil tax, alcohol tax, tobacco product tax, beer tax, wine and intermediate tax and raw tobacco tax.
This law defines the forms of dealing with products subject to excise taxes, tax payer, approval procedures, conditions for the transportation of the products, tax returns and penalties for violation of the legislation.
The law and subsequent decree also regulate some other conditions for dealing with mineral oils (tagging mineral oils), restrictions on the sale of spirits and tobacco products, monitoring the management of special mineral oils and the storage of raw tobacco for any purpose other than for the manufacture of tobacco products.
Taxes on other energy products (i.e. natural gas and certain other gases, solid fuels and electricity) are regulated in sections 45 to 47 of act no. 261/2007 Coll., on the stabilization of public budgets.
In addition, in the Czech Republic, a number of provisions related to the administration of excise duties are contained in special legislation. Fuel Act No. 311/2006 Coll. and the implementing regulation governs the conditions for the sale, dispensing, distribution of fuel and keeping records of fuel put into free tax circulation.
In Law No. 61/1997 Coll. the conditions for the production, storage, registration and control of the production and circulation of alcohol are defined in its Implementing Rules.
Act No. 307/2013 Coll. concerning the compulsory marking of ethyl alcohol, and the relevant implementing regulations establish the compulsory labelling of alcohol in consumer packaging, the conditions for dealing with the control tapes and the conditions for the management of alcohol (i.e. for the production, processing, sale or other transfer, transport, transportation, storage, taking, use, possession, import or export of alcohol).
Procedures for tax proceedings, not specified in special regulations, are regulated by Law No. 280/2009 Coll. the tax code.
Penalties are imposed by procedures under Act No. 500/2004 Coll. administrative order.
Conditions for issuing business license (concession) to operate the trade "production and processing of fuels and lubricants and fuel distribution" and "manufacture, presentation and sale of ethyl alcohol fermentation, alcohol drinking and spirits" are regulated by act no. 455/1991 Coll., about business (Trade Act).
The Czech republic took advantage of the permission to implement control procedures and institutes for the control of the transport of selected products in free tax circulation, and for the supervision over compliance with legislation in the handling of selected products, which has not been paid the excise tax, even when dealing with selected products, for which no tax is paid.
This is the monitoring of the management of special mineral oils and unmanufactured tobacco, marking certain other mineral oils, marking tobacco products and alcohol in consumer packaging.
Czech republic permission to apply excise tax to other products availed and as one of the measures against tax fraud introduced the excise tax on raw tobacco.
Structure of changes in legislation for individual types of excise duties in relation to the subject of control in the Czech Republic
On the basis of the resolution of the government of the Czech Republic of 3. October 2012, no. 735, to the implementation of "the plan of zero tolerance to the black market liquor", occurred in the years 2012-2015 in the Czech republic to major legislative changes, which were introduced a number of measures against tax fraud on the excise duty on ethyl alcohol.
In the same period, there have also been major changes in legislation in the tax on mineral oils, tax on tobacco products and the criminalisation of the preparation of tax evasion.
Criminal protection of tax revenues
Effective from 1. 7. 2016 is introduced the criminality of the preparation of the crime "reduction of tax, fee and similar mandatory payments". The adjustment made should enable police authorities more efficient and more timely adoption of measures to reduce tax fraud, such as the use of operative means of detection.
General provisions of excise duty management
The issue of permits for the management of products subject to excise duty under the law on excise duties is effective from 1. 1. 2015 subject: reliability; bezdlužností; economic stability; authorized to operate the business, allowing performance of activities related to the permit; a situation where the claimant is not in liquidation or in bankruptcy.
The aim of the legislation was in particular addressing the issue of the emergence of tax arrears and reduction of the entities authorised to deal with products subject to tax excise taxes.
The condition of economic stability newly allows the tax administrator to take into account the financial situation of tax entities both in the framework of the authorisation procedure and after the issue of the permit.
The purpose of this measure is to prevent entities which do not have sufficient financial income to properly fulfil their tax obligations from discharging selected products.
To assess the economic stability of the applicant have been established indicators (profitability, liquidity, financial stability, activity, productivity), on the basis of which performed the financial analysis.
In addition to these indicators, the administrative discretion of the tax administrator depends on the individual conditions of the procedure.
In the law it is established the periodicity of the verification of the compliance of the conditions of economic stability because of the timeliness of the data – screening takes place once a year following the deadline for submission of income tax return.
The tax administrator has the opportunity to establish other conditions necessary for the administration of the tax.
If the holder of the authorisation conditions do not fulfill, is the tax administrator is entitled to a permit to cancel, or cancel suspended.
Of the total 2 609 subjects for which the Customs administration of the CZECH republic examined the condition of economic stability, was 18.6% of found to be economically fragile with a high risk of the emergence of arrears in the event that the tax obligation exceeds the amount of the tax (e.g., a repeated recipient).
License was revoked ten entities, other applicants have increased the reinsurance tax, kapitalizovali your stake in the company or provide the actual data from the accounting, according to which already meets all the conditions for issuance of the permit.
The conditions of reliability and completeness shall, in addition to the petitioner to fulfil the natural person who is the statutory body or its member, or natural person, which, while not a statutory body of the applicant or its member, but performing this activity (chaining of legal persons in the position of the statutory body or its member, the so-called related entities).
By the end of 2016, more than 30,000 linked entities had been vetted.
Records kept under the excise duty Act (§ 37 to § 40 and § 60 of Act No. 353/2003 Coll.) contain data on:
type, name, code and quantity of goods produced, received, issued or dispatched, broken down by type of tax regime management (the regime of conditional exemption from tax, imports, reverse the entry into the regime of conditional exemption from tax, export, free tax circulation, own consumption, loss of);
identifier (SEED ID) of the recipient or supplier of the selected goods, the declarant, the date of the occurrence of events and registration;
transport of selected products (e.g. means of transport, carriers, transport number);
registration numbers of related documents;
notification concerning the placing of alcohol in consumer packaging marked with control tape into free tax circulation and data on its distribution.
A post-transport takeover record shall be made immediately after its termination.
In the case of electronic records, the records must be kept or allow output in the format xls, xlsx, ods.
Alcohol
Czech republic after the year 2012 introduced a complex of measures, whose purpose was to provide a detailed overview of the activities of the operators (see annex 3, scheme A) from production of raw ethyl alcohol through the marking of the control tape until after its distribution to the final retailer or authorized user of alcohol, exempt from tax.
In the Czech Republic it is subject to the supervision of customs authorities and production facilities for the production of alcohol that is not in operation.
The aim of the new legislation was to increase the visibility over the processing of ethyl alcohol and production of spirits and identify the persons dealing with alcohol in consumer packaging, reduce waste with rubbing alcohol on a financially stable and reliable people and ensure constant supervision over the production and labeling of spirit drinks.
The most important measures are: Records of production, income, stocks, and release of ethyl alcohol they contain information about the amount of alcohol according to individual stages of production and handling of ethyl alcohol, with the numbers of the documents.
Restriction the volume of consumer packaging, material packaging, and limiting the number of packages with broken control tape in the place of ultimate sale or issue to the consumer.
Consumer packaging means a container or other container with a capacity of max. one liter, or three liters, if it is a container made of glass.
Spirits in larger packages are seen as Unmarked, which are forbidden to be handled.
At the place of final sale to a natural person for his personal consumption can be located max. one consumer pack with broken control tape, or three if fitted with a one-way valve.
Mandatory registration of a person who places alcohol in products in consumer packaging with at least 15 % by volume of alcohol into free tax circulation and is: importer of ethyl alcohol, the manufacturer of ethyl alcohol in the CZECH republic or by the operator of the tax warehouse in the regime of conditional exemption from tax, provided that the personal and technical conditions.
Personal conditions – the reliability, integrity and nevyslovení ban on activities – must comply with the applicant and the person in the position of the statutory body or responsible representative.
The applicant must grant bail of CZK 100,000 to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. approximately € 3,700 to €185,000), depending on the estimated amount of control straps collected.
The technical conditions for registration are a convenient place for marking of alcohol and amenities of the place marking or tax warehouse of the camera tracking device with continuous operation and remote access of the tax administrator.
Registration markings of control tapes are introduced for the marking of spirits with a volume of more than 0.06 liters.
When transporting control belts, the registration marking of the control belts must be indicated in the documents of transportation or customs declaration at export.
Control tape up to 30. 11. 2013 contained a digit registration code, which included the four-digit registration sample number, the code allocation request control of the tapes and code the classification according to the level of the volumetric concentration of ethanol.
Control tape from 1. 12. 2013 newly contains two types of identifiers and the quantities of alcohol in a consumer packaging, expressed in milliliters of ethanol at 20 °C, and that the nearest millilitres downward.
The register control tapes for the marking of spirits contains daily entries about the various ways of dealing with the control tapes according to the filing codes and also the documents on the basis of which the entry is made.
In the destruction, loss or theft of specific control strip is the holder bound to the following working day after the relevant facts electronically notify the tax registration code of the concerned control strip and their number.
The introduction of a new factual substance of the offences and the adjustment of the amount of penalties imposed for violations in the handling of control tapes.
Sanctions may be imposed up to the amount of excise duty or her up to ten times exceed (e.g., in the destruction of, or loss of control of tapes in a number exceeding 0.1% of the total amount of individual underlying orders of the control belt when the failure to return control of the tape within the statutory time limit).
Restrictions on dealing with the control tapes only to the registered holder, who is not allowed to refer to another person, with the exception of providing it to a foreign supplier for the purpose of designations for spirit drinks in consumer packaging produced outside of the Czech republic.
The exported control tapes shall be placed on consumer packaging and returned no later than nine months after receipt from the tax administrator.
Compulsory registration distributor of ethyl alcohol in a consumer packaging, provided that similar personal conditions as for persons required to mark the spirit and with the obligation to deposit bail in the amount of 5 000 000 Czk (i.e. circa 185 000 €).
Definition of persons for the sale or purchase of alcohol in a consumer package.
Authorized persons are required to sell alcohol in consumer packaging other registered persons or to the ultimate retailers, or it may sell as the ultimate seller.
Alcohol may be acquired from other registered persons, insolvency administrators, administrative bodies, organizational departments of the state or unregistered persons in the execution of tax enforcement.
Notification concerning the placing of alcohol or the sale of the consumer packaging in tax free circulation of the holders and distributors of ethyl alcohol required to send immediately the following day after the relevant facts to the tax authorities through the information system maintained by the tax administrator (ORO web client) or in compliance with the content in xml format.
The notification contains the number of the used control tapes, the volume and type of consumer packaging, the volume percentage of ethyl alcohol, european commodity code (EAN), the identification of the distributor or final seller and also the product name and batch production.
Tax entities sent about £ 10.5 m in 2014 and 2015. notice.
Mandatory concessions (a specific form of a trade licence) not only for the production and editing of ethyl alcohol, but also for the sale of alcohol in consumer packaging an entrepreneur natural person for his personal use or any other legal or business natural person for its own internal use.
Conceded trades may be exercised only after a decision has been made by the trade authority, subject to professional competence and other conditions.
No prescribed professional competence is required for the sale of alcohol.
The benefit to the tax administrator is an overview of the sellers and their establishments and restrictions
trading on reliable entities.
In the Czech Republic, about 94 thousand were registered in 2014 and about 104 thousand were sold in 2015.
The checking of legal compliance in the areas of dealing with products subject to excise taxes in the Czech republic shall ensure in their activities outside of the tax administrator also: business offices, the State agricultural and food inspection, the authorities of the Financial administration of the CZECH republic, the authorities of the Czech trade inspection.
If it finds that there has been a breach of the obligation or breach of the prohibition, it shall notify the excise duty administrator without delay.
Mineral oils
The Czech republic has introduced a comprehensive system of supervision (see appendix 3, diagram B), which are subject to the mineral oils burdened by excise taxes, but also to the selected mineral oil excise taxes unencumbered, which have been abused for tax evasion.
The system includes supervision from production of mineral oil over the storage, transport, tagging and coloring selected mineral oils, marking certain other mineral oils up to delivery to the final consumer or user and, in some cases even the consumption of mineral oils.
The supervision of customs authorities shall include the production and management of marking agents for the marking of mineral oils.
Tagging and coloring selected mineral oils are subject to the mineral oils listed under combined nomenclature codes 2710 19 25 (kerosene others), 2710 19 29 (other n. e. s medium oil) and heavy gas oil 2710 19 41, 2710 19 45 and 2710 19 49, where the tagging is prohibited.
Marking certain other mineral oils subject such as benzene, toluene, xylene and lubricating oils and other oils intended for other purposes than the propulsion engines.
It is possible to mark and paint selected mineral oils and some other mineral oils with a marking agent only on the permission of the tax administrator.

The most significant new measures since 2012:
Monitoring the management of special mineral oils, which is a group of mineral oil under the combined nomenclature codes 2710 19 71 to 2710 19 99 (i.e., lubricating oils and other oils intended for other purposes than the propulsion of the engines), whose kinematic viscosity at 40 °C is lower than 12 mm2. with-1 inclusive and having at least one of the following: the flash point is less than 150 °C, at least 20% by volume distilled during the distillation test, including losses up to 350 °C.
These mineral oils have been used as an admixture to the ready-made fuel, it was particularly diesel fuel, or were directly used or sold for the propulsion of the engines, because the physical properties are very similar.
Entities handling monitored mineral oils in bulk or in packages exceeding 220 litres shall be registered with the tax administrator.
For the issue of registration must be met for the personal conditions of the applicant, a statutory body and the responsible representative, which is valid for the whole period 2, With the exception of beer, fruit wines, other wines and mead and fruit distillates obtained tan.
