For the checked period the volume of expenditure related to upgrading the EMCS system in the SR in terms of one carriage 2.3 times exceeds the expenses of the same type in the CZECH republic.
Conclusion
Cooperation between the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic has achieved its objectives.
Both audit institutions have acquired a deeper knowledge of the excise tax management system in the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic.
It was found that, despite a common basic legal framework exist in both tax systems, significant differences, which affect the efficiency of the administration of excise taxes.
During the parallel controls have been identified examples of good practice, which could contribute to curbing tax fraud, their meaning with the rising rates of taxes will grow.
Procedures reducing the cost of Excise Management have also been identified.
Mutual cooperation revealed differences, which significantly affect the efficiency of the tax administration and limit the international comparison, if they are not carried out mutually coordinated due diligence for the tax administrator.
In this, the role of the Supreme Audit Institutions is irreplaceable.
Report on the results of the parallel control of the administration of Value Added Tax carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introductory word
The Lima Declaration of 1977 stresses that the Supreme Audit Institutions (Sai) have the power to audit all public financial operations.
The declaration calls for tax revenues to be checked as far as possible.
The Organisation considers the European Organisation of supreme audit institutions (EUROSAI) to be one of the most important components of Public income tax.
GOI. the EUROSAI Congress, organized in Bonn in 2005, was engaged in auditing public revenues carried out by the SAI.
An important step on the way to optimizing the SAI control activity is the development of a specific strategy for auditing public revenues.
This applies in particular to taxes as the most expensive source of Public income, which is most susceptible to large losses.
Due to the fact that national economies are becoming more interconnected and dependent, may be SAI to some extent unable to perform inspection activities without the cooperation with the SAI of another state.
An example is the audit of internationally organized fraud, which causes substantial losses in the income of many countries.
In order to combat this crime, responsible authorities need to cooperate with each other.
SAI, which carry out inspections in this area, must be willing to establish closer cooperation with each other.
Just on VI. EUROSAI congress in Bonn, the idea arose to perform control of the administration of value added tax (hereinafter "VAT") and VIES in the framework of cooperation of the Supreme audit office and of the Federal court of auditors Bundesrechnungshof.
Careful preparation followed, with both parties first having to familiarise themselves with the legal environment and VAT management procedures in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany.
On the basis of the analysis of this information, a selection of control topics was made, which was included in the control program.
Achieving effective and efficient VAT management is a long-term problem and individual states (in particular member states of the European Union) are looking for solutions to improve, simplify and make the collection of this tax more transparent.
We believe that the results of our review may serve not only for improving the work of the controllers of taxes, but also as a basis for a proposal to improve the system of international exchange of information.
Report on the results of parallel controls of the administration of Value Added Tax carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 06/27 (d) VIII 2 – 2005 – 1215
Subject of inspection:
(CZ) administration of Value Added Tax after the Czech Republic joins the European Union
(D) Examination of administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax under Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003 and the Commission Regulation (EC) no 1925/2004
Objective of control:
(CZ) the Aim of the control action in the Czech republic was to examine the procedure of the financial authorities in the administration of value added tax after the integration of the Czech republic to the single internal market of the European union (hereinafter "EU") united with the free movement of goods and services, and explore the use of VIES, in particular in monitoring the application of the right to exemption from value added tax in intrakomunitárního delivery.
(D) the Objective of the audit was to review the system of control of intracommunity value-added tax with a particular focus on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax according to the above-mentioned regulation.
The result should be a report on weaknesses and recommendations for their elimination.
System of exchange of information on value added tax Control actions implement the Supreme audit office, Czech republic (hereinafter the "SAO") and the German Bundesrechnungshof (hereinafter referred to as "BRH"), in mutual cooperation on the basis of the contract concluded between the two audit institutions on 8. June 2006.
Cooperation focused mainly on the examination of selected commercial transactions between payers from the Czech republic (hereinafter "CR") and the Federal republic of Germany (hereinafter "GERMANY"), the use of information obtained in the form of international cooperation between tax administrations and comparison of the systems of VAT administration in both countries.
The joint final report on the results of the control actions was prepared within the meaning of European Directive No 31 for the implementation of INTOSAI audit standards.
The period under review was from 1. 5. 2004 to 31. 12. 2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
Parallel control in the area of VAT management in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of a contract between the two SAI.
Outside of the main point – the exchange of information on the basis of Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003 and the Commission Regulation (EC) no 1925/2004 – cover inspection of other topics, such as, for example, registration of payers, VAT returns and recapitulative statements, which are the main point of the closely associated.
In addition, the control included the legal situation in the area of international bus passenger transport and the comparison of certain statistical data.
Comparing the VAT management systems of both countries, differences were found in the following areas:
1) registration for VAT.
While in GERMANY entrepreneurs are registered regardless of their turnover, in the CZECH republic is the primary criterion (among others) for registration of exceeding the limit laid down in the law on VAT.
In the Czech Republic, payers are assigned only one tax identification number, which they also use in intracommunitary transactions.
In SRN, payers are assigned a tax number when registering for VAT, serving only for commercial transactions in the territory of SRN.
If a German payer intends to carry out intracommunity transactions, must request the allocation of a specific identification number, the so-called VAT ID.
As different registration methods cause problems, conditions should be balanced across the EU (see. 4.1).
2) international passenger bus service.
In the Czech Republic, international passenger bus service is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct VAT.
In Germany, part of the transport carried out on German territory is subject to VAT.
At EU level, efforts should be made to harmonise the situation within the meaning of article 393 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of VAT (see. 4.2)
3) VAT returns.
While in the CZECH republic, payers submitted VAT returns, only a single tax period (month or quarter), in GERMANY they have the payer the obligation to file so-called preliminary VAT returns (monthly or quarterly) and after the end of the calendar year must file an annual tax return to the VAT.
In contrast to the Czech Republic payers in Germany are required to file preliminary tax returns electronically.
The introduction of the obligation to file VAT returns electronically in the Czech Republic would increase the efficiency of the Czech Tax Administration (see. 4.3).
4) summary reports.
While in the Czech Republic payers file aggregated reports at the tax authorities, in Germany payers file aggregated reports on customs duties.
Therefore, the tax authorities in the Czech Republic have data from the aggregate reports available immediately after filing them.
The German tax authorities have information from the aggregate reports only after processing them into customs duties.
Combating VAT fraud requires that updated information on intracommunity transactions be made available as soon as possible.
A monthly summary reporting would shorten the time shift between the transaction date and the update of the VIES data.
This would subsequently allow for a timely examination of taxation in the member state of the acquirer (see. 4.4).
Which would, but would require all member states to adopt the same deadline for submitting a summary report.
5) international exchange of information in the field of VAT.
The Czech duty monitors compliance with the three-month period for requests for information received.
German tariffs do not follow.
As a result, the German tax administration handled a significantly lower percentage of applications received within the deadline.
Because of these problems, BRH recommended a permanent warning to the German customs (see. 4.6).
6) Risk Management System.
Each of the two member states is developing its own risk management system (risk management system, hereinafter referred to as "RMS"), which has its strengths and weaknesses.
The SAO and the BRH point out that an effective RMS cannot be developed by just one member state.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in each EU member state, otherwise fraudsters will choose the member state with the weakest RMS (see 5.).
As part of the cooperation, both SAI examined selected cases of intracommunitary transactions between tax entities from the Czech Republic and Germany.
Together with the use of the legislation for CUSTOMS examined thirty-one cases of commercial transactions, for which there were doubts as to their realization or suspicion of tax evasion on VAT.
It was found that:
In some cases, the tax authorities used information obtained in the form of international cooperation and imposed VAT on payers.
In these cases, the payers either unjustifiably claimed the exemption from VAT or did not admit the acquisition of the goods in the VAT return.
In some cases, the tax authorities could not use the information obtained because the information was either incomplete or incomprehensible.
In other cases, could not be used because of the different legal provisions in both member states.
In some cases, the tax administration of another member state refused to respond to a request for information.
There have been cases where payers erroneously reported business transactions in aggregate reports.
As a result, the data in VIES were incorrect and the tax authorities had to examine these cases (see. 6.).
Course of control action
The course of the control action in the Czech Republic
The inspection was carried out in the period from June 2006 to march 2007 by the Department II – department of revenue of the state budget and territorial departments of central Bohemia, north-west Bohemia, south Bohemia, south Moravia, central Moravia and north Moravia.
Controlled entities were: the Ministry of finance (hereinafter "MF") and 10 of the financial authorities – the Financial authority in Humpolec, the tax office in Jihlava, the Financial office in Kadaň, the Financial office in Liberec, the Finance office in Nymburk Financial office in Otrokovice, the Financial authority for Prague 1, the Financial authority for Prague 4 tax office in Sokolov and Financial authority in Třinec.
The audit conclusion of this audit action was approved by the Sao College on 23. April 2007.
Course of control action in Germany
The inspection was carried out in the period from June 2006 to February 2007, the control group for indirect taxes and staff designated regional audit offices in Berlin, Frankfurt and Munich.
The control was part of the control plan for 2006 and was therefore notified to the Federal MF in 2006.
After the testing phase, the inspection was started in the fourth quarter of 2006.
According to the cases selected by the BRH and later elected by the SAO, the BRH had to notify the control of a number of federal states.
In addition to interviews on the Federal MF and on tariffs, the inspection was carried out in the following federal states:
Baden-Württemberg, Bavaria, Hamburg, Lower Saxony, North Rhine -Westphalia, Rhineland-Palatinate and Saxony.
The tax files of the following tax authorities were included:
Bruchsal, Ettlingen, Freudenstadt, Karlsruhe-Stadt, Leonberg, Mühlacker, Singen, Tuttlingen, Cham, Fürstenfeldbruck, Munich tax office for corporations/ legal persons (München-Körperschaften), Munich II, IV and Munich, Starnberg, Hamburg-Altona, Hamburg-Hansa, Hamburg-center (Hamburg-Mitte), Hamburg-nord (Hamburg-Nord), and Hamburg for large enterprises (Hamburg für Großunternehmen), Hannover-Nord (Hannover north), Winsen-Luhe, Bonn center (Bonn-Innenstadt), Cologne center (Köln-Mitte), Cologne-Porz (Köln-Porz), Cologne south (Köln-Süd), Sankt Augustin, Pirmasens, Budyšín (Bautzen), Chemnitz south (Chemnitz-Süd), Neustadt II (Dresden II), Freiberg, Leipzig, I (Leipzig I) and Zschopau.

The report on the control findings was submitted to the MF in May 2007.
Cooperation between the two control institutions
In the preparation of parallel control actions in the period prior to their commencement took place several meetings of the representatives of the two audit institutions.
The participants in these meetings became acquainted with the organization of tax administrations, with the legislative regulation of the issue of VAT and with the system of VAT management in both countries.
At the meeting, which took place in May 2006, the topics of the test phase were agreed.
The results of the test phase were evaluated at the next joint meeting in August 2006.
In the framework of this negotiation, a timetable for the further progress of the work was agreed and the following themes of parallel checks were established:
1. Registration of VAT payers.
2.
International bus transport of persons-legislation in the Czech Republic and Germany.
3. The international exchange of information, in particular, the procedure of tax administrators in dealing with requests for information and examination of selected problem cases referred to in requests for information and spontaneous information, transferred between the CZECH republic and GERMANY.
4. VAT returns.
5.
Summary reports.
6.
Statistics on the delivery and acquisition of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany.
7. VAT risk management.
On a common inspection day, the SAO and BRH, which took place in December 2006, the two sides mutually acquainted with the course of the inspection in the CZECH republic and GERMANY and to discuss the existing results of parallel control actions.
The report on the results of parallel checks of the VAT administration between the Czech Republic and Germany was prepared at a working meeting in July 2007.
4. Administration of Value Added Tax in the Czech Republic and Germany
Registration of payers in the Czech Republic
(A) payers having their registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic
The tax entity shall Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the administration of taxes and fees (hereinafter referred to as "Act No. 337/1992 Coll.“ ) means the taxpayer, the taxpayer and the legal successor of a natural or legal person, which as a tax entity is defined by law.
31. 12. 2004 a total of 421 865 tax entities were registered for VAT in the Czech Republic.
1. 12. 2005 there was an increase in the number of tax entities registered for VAT to 457 590.
Taxable person, which has its registered office, place of business or establishment in the CZECH republic whose turnover exceeds for at least 12 preceding consecutive calendar months the sum of 1 000 000 Czk (33 575 EUR), becomes the payer of 1. on the third month following the month in which it exceeded the registration limit (§ 94 para. 1 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., on value added tax; hereinafter referred to as "Act No. 235/2004 Coll.“).
The application for registration the person shall submit, within 15 days after the end of the month in which exceeded the registration limit.
The current legislation does not allow to register a taxable person the so-called backward, in cases when the reason for registration is exceeding the legal limit for registration.
A taxable person with registered office, place of business or establishment in the CZECH republic, which carries out taxable transactions or of transactions exempt from VAT with a right to deduct can become a tax payer, even though do not exceed a turnover of 1 000 000 Czk (33 575 EUR), if they meet any of the other conditions referred to in act no. 235/2004 Coll.
A taxable person with registered office, place of business or establishment in the CZECH republic, which fails to comply with any of the conditions provided for by law, may apply for VAT registration voluntarily.
The registration procedure under Act No. 337/1992 Coll is initiated by the application for registration to the local tax administrator.
The voluntary VAT payer shall also indicate on the VAT registration application the date on which he applies for registration as a VAT payer.
The Tax Administrator shall verify the information communicated by the tax entity, i.e. the completed application for registration with all annexes.
If it has doubts about the data, it shall invite the tax entity to explain, supplement or document the data.
After the tax administrator has verified that the taxpayer meets the conditions for registration, it shall issue a decision in the form of a certificate stating that it is a tax entity registered and was assigned a tax identification number (hereinafter "TIN").
On the certificate, the Tax Administrator shall indicate the effective date of the VAT registration and the periodicity of the VAT tax period.
The tax period is a calendar quarter, if the turnover of the payer for the previous calendar year did not reach 10 000 000 CZK (335 750 euros).
If the turnover of the payer for the previous calendar year amounted to CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335,750), the tax period is the calendar month.
The payer whose turnover in the previous calendar year reached 2 000 000 Czk (67 EUR 150), is entitled to elect for the tax period of the calendar month and such change shall notify the tax administrator.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The allocation of the VAT number in the registration certificate always has a constitutive character and the tax body is obliged to indicate in all cases of communication (including payments) with the tax administrator and in the cases stipulated by a special law (e.g. act no. 235/2004 Coll. when issuing tax documents).
The tin contains the code " CZ " and the tribal part forming the general identifier.
The general identifier is for natural persons the birth number, or other general identifier, if provided for by special law, and in legal person identification number (the provisions of § 33 paragraph. 12 of Act No. 337/1992 Coll.).
If the tax entity has not fulfilled their registration obligation or to challenge the tax administrator, register it locally competent tax administrator from official duties without delay.
The result of the registration procedure is the issuance of an ex officio Registration Certificate, which is served on the tax entity.
In the CZECH republic is the tax entity that received permission to business activity, allocated a TIN at the time of his first registration to any tax.
The same tin is used by the tax entity even if it is registered as a VAT payer.
According to the text of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. which is effective from 1. 1. 2005, can the tax administrator in case of failure to fulfil the registration obligations for VAT, save to the taxable person a refund of up to 10% of total revenues or income for taxable transactions, which this person was held illegally without tax, for the period from the date on which should be legally registered by the payer, the date on which the basis of the decision of the tax administrator to the registered payer has become a (the provisions of § 98 paragraph. 1 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.).
The payment of the amount thus determined shall be considered as a levy (§ 98 para. 3 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.), that is, it is not a sanction.
Cancellation of the registration of the VAT payer when the conditions laid down by law are met is possible for two reasons:
1)
Cancellation of registration on request of the payer, mainly arising from the above turnover is below the registration limit (§ 106 par. 1 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.).
The payer shall be entitled to apply for the cancellation of the registration no earlier than 1 year after the effective date indicated on the registration certificate.
2) cancellation of the registration "ex officio" (§ 106 Para. 7 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.) if: (a) the payer has not carried out without notice the tax administrator for 12 consecutive months of performance, (b) the payer does not fulfil its obligations under Act No. 235/2004 Coll.(C) the payer shall cease to be a taxable person.
B) Payers who do not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the CZECH republic, a Person registered for tax in another member state, which has no seat, place of business or establishment in the CZECH republic, or a foreign taxable person, which will take place performance with place of performance in the territory of the country and is the person liable to pay tax from this performance pursuant to § 108 of the act no 235/2004 Sb. (the so-called "non-established payer") becomes the payer on the date of implementation of this performance.
This person is obliged to submit an application for registration to the IRS for Threshold 1 no later than the date of implementation of the transaction.
In the application for registration, it is obliged to indicate all the tin assigned to it in other member states or in a third country.
If "non-established" a payer submits an application for registration later than the date of first taxable supply in the CZECH republic, the Financial authority for Prague 1, it registers retroactively, because according to act no. 235/2004 Coll. the tax entity became a VAT payer on the date of first taxable supply in the CZECH republic.
When registering retroactively, the Tax Office for Threshold 1 requires proof from tax entities that the fulfillment was carried out (invoices, or explanatory letters).
If "non-established" tax entity applies for registration in the CZECH republic before the first taxable supply, then the Financial office for Prague 1 calls for the submission of agreements, that the performance take place.
The Tax Office for Threshold 1 was at 31. 12. 2004 registered 473" non-established " payers, of which 124 payers from Germany, and at 31. 12. In 2005, 951" non-established " payers were registered, of which 233 were from Germany.
According to the provisions of § 106 Para. 9 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. the tax administrator is entitled to cancel the registration of the "non-established" payer at 31. January of the following calendar year, provided that the payer has no obligation to grant and pay the tax during the current calendar year.
The Sao's inspection found that if the" non-established " payer submits a tax return abroad for postal transport 25. January, i.e., in accordance with the statutory adjustment in the deadline for filing tax returns, doesn't have it the irs is still 31. January available.
In cases where the facts applicable to the possibility of revocation of the registration are known to the IRS at a later date than 31. in January, in the Czech Republic it is no longer possible to cancel VAT registration for an "unoccupied" payer in a given calendar year.
Registration of payers in Germany
Due to the legal provisions of the German tax code (§§ 137, 138 Abgabenordnung, hereinafter referred to as "AO"), anyone who develops a business activity, is obliged to inform the city/municipal authority or the competent financial authority.
The deadline for submitting information is one month after the start of the business.
This information is processed by the municipal/municipal authority for the tax office.
If the IRS detects an undertaking that has started but has not registered, the competent IRS may register that payer ex officio-even retroactively.
Taxpayers who are in the federal republic of GERMANY tax residents and tax non-residents, are required by law to register for VAT if they meet the criteria set out in § 2 of the German VAT law ('the UStG').
This obligation does not depend on the volume of turnover that they implement.
In Germany there is no voluntary registration for VAT.
For entrepreneurs permanently living abroad, there are special tax authorities.
For example, for those who are based in the Czech Republic, the competent tax office is Chemnitz-Süd.
30. in April 2004, a total of 295 Czech entrepreneurs were registered at the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office; at 1. a total of 1050 Czech entrepreneurs were registered in March 2006.
BRH found that these specific financial authorities often refuse to register so-called polozávislých independent workers established in the new eastern member states of the EU.
Because of the work permit of employees from the ten new EU member states after their accession into the EU is limited, they tried to these independent workers to avoid these limitations, business start-ups.
These businesses do not meet the criteria for the entrepreneur provided for in section 2 of the UStG, because they are usually dependent on a single employer, which determines their working hours and the way they work.
For the purpose of registration, the entrepreneur must fill out a questionnaire of the competent financial authority, which must submit information about the company and about the activities that are carried out.
The questionnaire constitutes a standard form that is binding on all tax authorities in Germany.
It is processed either by special departments of the tax authorities or by general-purpose departments responsible for assessing taxpayers.
Through this form is the risk assessment on individual taxpayers before the irs issues a tax number.
The structure of the tax number for domestic transactions is governed by certain rules:
The first three digits provide information about the relevant financial office, the following three (or four) provide information about the appropriate department at the tax office, the other five (or four) are to the resolution of the payers, while the last is always a check digit.
If an entrepreneur intends to participate in the intrakomunitárním trade, he needs a VAT registration number (VAT ID), to receive the intracommunity delivery to the tax-exempt.
The duty allocates a VAT ID at the request of the entrepreneur, if the entrepreneur is registered in the German federation and if he has a tax number for VAT purposes.
Customs allocates VAT ID to entrepreneurs automatically when payers indicate intracommunitary delivery in their VAT return.
The VAT ID structure is the country code (DE) followed by a series of nine digits.
Registration of an entrepreneur can be canceled: 1. at his request (for example, if ceased its business activities), after the execution of all administrative work (assessment of all the economic years) and 2. in the event that the tax administration realizes that it is no longer engaged in business activity.
The validity of the VAT identification number is usually linked to the validity of the VAT tax number.
The financial authorities are in such cases obliged to inform the CUSTOMS about the cancellation of the tax number, that the DUTY may terminate the validity of identification numbers for VAT purposes.
According to the German VAT Act (§19 (1) UStG) tax residents in Germany are not obliged to pay VAT in case 1. that the turnover plus the relevant VAT of the previous calendar year does not exceed EUR 17 500 and 2. the following year is unlikely to exceed EUR 50 000.
So-called small entrepreneurs ("Kleinunternehmer") are not entitled to invoice other entrepreneurs VAT and are not entitled to deduct input tax.
Although they are not obliged to pay VAT, small entrepreneurs must be registered with the tax office and must file an annual VAT return.
A small entrepreneur may declare that there will be no provision of § 19 para. 1 ustg apply.
This confession is binding on him for the next five years.
The entrepreneur can then invoice VAT and deduct the input tax.
For tax non-residents there is an opportunity to appoint a tax representative (§22a UStG).
A prerequisite is to undertake exclusively the business operations of tax-exempt and not entitled to deduct input tax.
Functions of a tax agent is to fulfill the tax obligations of the foreign entrepreneur, who thus need not register for VAT.
Invoices must contain information about representation for tax purposes.
Comparison and evaluation
The situation is different in both countries.
While in GERMANY entrepreneurs are registered regardless of their turnover, in the CZECH republic is the primary criterion (among others) for registration of exceeding the limit laid down in the law on VAT.
If the tax entity in the Czech Republic does not exceed the established limit, it has the opportunity to apply for VAT registration on a voluntary basis.
The registration procedure is standardized in Germany, but differences may arise as a result of different organizational models in federal states.
In the Czech Republic, the payer is assigned a tin at the time of his first registration for any tax.
In the event that the payer registers for VAT, he uses the same tin even in intracommunitary transactions.
In SRN, the payer is assigned a tax number when registering for VAT, serving only for commercial transactions in the territory of SRN.
If a German payer intends to carry out intracommunity transactions, must request the allocation of a specific identification number, the so-called VAT ID.
As the SAO and the BRH found, can the German two-tier registration system causing many misunderstandings in other member states, such as in the CZECH republic, which allocates a single id number for national registration for VAT and registration for intrakomunitárním transactions.
On the other hand, a two-tiered system allows retroactive (national) registration in cases where the payer to refuse to inform the municipalitu or the competent financial authority of their business.
This retroactive registration allows for the correct assessment of VAT for the previous tax period, especially an accurate estimate of the VAT tax liability.
As different registration methods cause problems, conditions should be balanced across the EU.
The German parliament recently decided to introduce a tax identification number (Tin).
The Federal Tax Office will allocate the tax code at the birth of a natural person.
This tin will be valid throughout the life of a natural person who is a German resident.
If a natural person starts a business, the competent tax authority will apply for an economic tin that will be used as a VAT ID.
In the future, there should be no delay between the National Registration of the payer and the allocation of VAT ID.
Work on the introduction of an IT resource to manage the tin has not yet been completed.
International passenger bus service
Legislation in the Czech Republic
According to the provisions of Section 70 of Law No. 235/2004 Coll. it is valid from 1. 5. 2004 transport of persons between member states and between member states and third countries in the Czech Republic exempted from VAT with a right to deduct tax.
This transport is exempt from VAT, even if it is implemented by entrepreneurs, who are registered for tax in other member states, or a foreign taxable person.
Return transport shall be considered as a separate transport.
If "not established" tax entities in the CZECH republic do not operate in addition to the international bus passenger transport other economic activity, have no obligation in the CZECH republic to register as VAT payers.
International passenger transport in the Czech Republic was exempt from VAT by virtue of the act of accession of the Czech Republic, annex in kap. Article 5 (5) Point 1 (b) where it is indicated:
"For the purposes of art. Article 28 (2) Article 3 (3) b) of directive 77/388/EEC, the Czech republic can continue to exempt from value added tax on international transport of passengers referred to in point 17 of annex F to the directive, until the condition set out in article. Article 28 (2) 4 the directive or, whichever is the earlier, when the same exemption is applied by an existing member state.“
Description of the legislation in Germany
Pursuant to Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC of 28. November 2006, implemented by § 3b para. 1 of the German law on VAT the place of supply of passenger transport services (i.e. transportation services) route (i.e., location), where transport takes place.
Therefore, the German tax system does not distinguish between national and international cross-border passenger transport.
Only that part of the route which takes place in Germany constitutes the taxable provision of transport in Germany.
The German tax system also does not distinguish between tax residents and non-residents.
If a tax non-resident carries passengers through GERMANY, then that part of the route, which takes place in GERMANY, also represents a taxable supply of transport.
Tax non-resident shall, before he carries out his services in GERMANY, announce their intention to provide transport of passengers to the competent tax office.
The tax office registers this tax a non-resident taxable persons (see 4.1.2) and issue a special certificate for any bus or coach which is referred to in the notice of the taxpayer.
The taxpayer is obliged to declare its taxable provision of transport in the German VAT return.
1. in March 2006, the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office registered 741 Czech payers who were engaged in passenger transport.
If passenger transport is provided to a tax resident who is a VAT-liable person, the tax non-resident does not have to pay VAT to the tax office himself.
Instead, an entity that is obliged to VAT to take to the tax office and the invoiced net amount of the tax non-resident is the tax resident who is a recipient of the services; this process is known under the name of "reverse charge" (reverse charge) and is in accordance with article 196 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC.
In addition, the announcement of the tax non-resident and its tax returns for VAT, the German tax authorities have several means to assess the correctness of the conferred on the taxable provision of passenger transport.
Mobile control groups of the customs office shall carry out audit certification of buses with permits (licenses) for foreign shipments, which are used to carry passengers over GERMANY.
After each audit, mobile control groups shall send a control report to the competent IRS.
If the bus driver does not have a valid certificate, the mobile control group is entitled to require the bus driver to pay VAT before continuing further transport.
A tax non-resident may deduct the VAT thus paid on the tax calculated in his VAT return.
If the irs doubts about the accuracy of the tax returns for VAT, it may notify the intention to carry out an audit, which must take place in the office of the finance office, or they can use the means of administrative cooperation referred to in Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003 (see 4.6).
Even if the tax non-resident refuses to pay the amount of VAT calculated in accordance with its statutory rate, the tax office may apply for administrative cooperation under Council Directive 76/308/EEC.
If it is to be conducted a review of tax return for VAT or performing the duties of the tax of a nonresident, the BRH considers all these means of administrative cooperation as too demanding from the point of view of the labour force in comparison with the small amounts of VAT that have been paid for the taxable provision of passenger transport.
In particular, the audit of the accounting of a tax non-resident provokes disproportionate costs for both the taxpayer and the tax administration.
The tax administration shall carry out the audit of foreign accounts, which doesn't just mean need for a knowledge of a foreign language, but also familiarity with international accounting standards.
The audit of this type is also likely to require more time than an audit of a tax resident, this audit is, however, limited to the provision of passenger transport, which are made in GERMANY.
On the other hand, the tax non-resident does not have to just accept the law on inspection, that his or her national tax administration, but also the right to perform the audit by the other member states, which transports passengers.
Moreover, in each member state, in which it is carried out only one provision of the carriage of passengers, is the taxpayer obliged to fulfill any tax obligations that apply to it in these member states, and in all languages and on all tax forms these member states.
The actual taxation of cross-border passenger transport therefore creates disproportionate bureaucratic costs.
Comparison and evaluation
The legal situation in both countries is different.
In the CZECH republic is the transportation of persons between member states of the EU or between member states and third countries, on the basis of the Act of accession of the CZECH republic exempt from VAT with the entitlement to a tax deduction.
In Germany, part of the transport carried out in the German territory constitutes a taxable transaction.
If this transport provides the FRG an unsettled payer for the first time, is obliged to provide transport to pre-notify the competent tax office.
The financial office of this payer registers and the payer is obliged to admit in FEDERAL taxable the provision of transportation in a tax return.
The implementation of the law is very time-consuming in Germany.
At least three of the four Czech payers registered with the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office are engaged in passenger transport.
In comparison with the given effort, the tax return, if implemented, is rather low.
Member states collecting VAT in accordance with Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC of 28. November 2006, on a common VAT system, is burdened with time-consuming obligations without a financially sensitive outcome.
To prevent undue costs to the assessment of VAT would provide cross-border passenger transport should be taxed in one member state only.
This could be the state where the transport starts or where the provider resides.
Such taxation would require adaptation of Council Directive 2006/112/EC.
VAT returns
Filing and processing of VAT tax returns in the Czech Republic
The payer is obliged within 25 days after the end of the tax period to file a tax return for VAT on a form prescribed by the MOF, even in the case that he incurred the tax liability, unless the law provides otherwise.
Your own tax liability is payable within the deadline for filing tax returns for VAT, with the exception of the tax vyměřované in connection with the importation of goods according to § 20 of act no. 235/2004 Coll. for which the maturity of the tax is determined by customs legislation.
If a repayable overpayment is incurred as a result of the excess deduction, the payer shall be returned without an application within 30 days of the excess deduction being calculated.
The period is not applied in cases where the tax administrator initiates a tax procedure relating to the payer's tax liability.
In accordance with the provisions of § 73 para. 11 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. can be entitled to a tax deduction to apply in ordinary tax return for VAT no later than the last tax period of the calendar year in which he could be entitled to a deduction.
After this period, it is possible to claim a tax deduction on apply within 3 years from the end of the tax period, in which he could be entitled to a deduction as soon as possible.
However, this is only possible by filing an additional VAT return.
Amendment to Act No. 235/2004 Coll. effective from 1. 1. 2005 allows the filing of an additional VAT return only for the period when the right to deduct tax could be applied for the first time.
The payer is required to submit additional tax returns for VAT, if a) a summary of the corrections increases the tax liability, b) performs the correction, while they do not change the last known tax liability, but only the data from the tax entity previously hardened, c) performs the repair rates and the amount of tax according to § 49 of act no. 235/2004 Coll.
The payer may submit an additional VAT return if the aggregate of Corrections reduces the tax liability.
An additional VAT return shall be submitted by the payer by the end of the month following the finding of these facts.
Submission of the VAT return in electronic form can be effected both through the Internet network or on a technical data medium.
Filing over the Internet can be done such as filing with a data message bearing an advanced electronic signature or of the filing with the data message neopatřenou advanced electronic signature.
In the case of filing with a data report not covered by a guaranteed electronic signature, submission in writing is still required, t.J. delivery of a computer report to the tax administrator (e-form).
The VAT return contains separate lines concerning the values of intracommunitary supplies / acquisitions of goods.
The values of the acquisition of services are reported on special lines of the VAT return.
Some lines are used for the purpose of initial automated control within the ADIS system.
The value of supplies of goods to other member states persons registered for tax in other member states shall be compared with the data given in the recapitulative statements submitted by the Czech payer.
The value of acquisitions of goods from other member states from persons registered for tax in other member states shall be compared with the values that are obtained through a system of VIES of the summary report of payers from other EU member states.
The tax office is undergoing an ADIS credibility test for VAT returns.
This test is carried out automatically, since VAT returns cannot be measured without the test.
The credibility Test involves calculating the credibility criteria and evaluating the risk types of VAT returns.
According to the provisions of § 37 para. 1 of Act No. 337/1992 Coll. can a financial authority who fails to comply within the prescribed period the obligation of non-pecuniary nature, resulting from this or the special tax act, or imposed in a decision under this act, to repeatedly impose a fine of up to $ 2 000 000 Czk (67 EUR 150).
An automated tax information system used by mergers to support tax administration.
The audit of the Sao found that the tax authorities did not usually use the possibility to impose a fine on payers for not filing a VAT return.
Filing and processing of VAT returns in Germany
In Germany, we distinguish between a preliminary monthly or quarterly VAT return and an annual VAT return.
Those taxpayers who are required to submit preliminary VAT returns must still submit an annual VAT return.
Even small entrepreneurs who are not obliged to pay VAT must file an annual tax return.
In general, taxpayers are required to submit quarterly VAT returns up to 10. on the month following the quarter in which the VAT is generated (§18 para. 2 UStG).
However, if the tax obligation of VAT exceeds in the preceding calendar year 6 136 EUROS or, in the case that it is a newly founded enterprise, the entrepreneur shall be obliged to submit monthly VAT returns to 10. the next month.
The taxpayer may also decide to file a monthly VAT return if there was a refund last year which exceeded EUR 6 136 (§18 para. 2a UStG).
VAT returns need not be made if the amount of the annual VAT does not exceed EUR 512.
The relevant amount of VAT duty must be paid within 10. on the month following the tax period in which VAT was incurred.
A refund can lead to an even more detailed investigation by the Fu.
Deadlines (according to the law) for the processing of tax returns and the refund of excess VAT deduction do not exist.
In order to timely refund, it is possible to offer collateral for the amount to be returned.
The basic principle is to process VAT returns and return the tax quickly.
The German VAT Act provides for the possibility to extend this period (§ 18 para. 6 UStG).
Such an extension should be applied for separately.
Allows you to to submit VAT returns and pay the relevant tax liability VAT a month later, provided that in the case of monthly returns is paid by the special advance.
This advance payment will be offset against the December VAT tax liability.
Whenever an error is detected, the entrepreneur must file a corrective VAT return.
There is no additional VAT return.
Once the annual VAT return, which must be filed by 31. may of the following calendar year, registered at the tax office, the entrepreneur can not fix the erroneous prior tax returns, but only the annual tax returns for VAT.
Correction of the annual VAT return to the benefit or disadvantage of the payer is possible during the next 4 years after the year in which the first annual VAT return was filed.
After these four years, the annual VAT return can normally be corrected only in cases of tax fraud or evasion.
Payers are obliged to file preliminary VAT returns electronically.
The tax authorities may apply exceptions to this rule to avoid excessive hardness.
Filing an annual VAT return is possible in paper form or via the internet, either with or without certification.
If it is carried out without certification, the payer must file a return once more on paper with personal signatures.
In the event that the payer does not file a VAT return, the tax administration is entitled to make a rough estimate of the taxpayer's turnover.
In case of late filing, the payer may be charged a penalty payment (maximum of 10% of the tax to be paid, or EUR 25 000).
During a previous inspection, the BRH found that tax authorities often do not impose this standard fine.
In other cases where the tax authorities imposed a fine, the amount was calculated inconsistently and arbitrarily.
Therefore, the standard fine does not meet its goal of reducing the average delay, especially when filing an annual VAT return.
The VAT return contains separate lines relating to the values of intracommunitary supplies/acquisitions of goods.
The values of the acquisition of services are reported on special lines of the VAT return.
Non-taxable transactions must be reported on a separate line of tax return/ VAT.
In the case of VAT returns which are submitted in paper form, must be taken by a copy either through the scanner or employees who are specially authorised.
Data from VAT returns submitted electronically shall be immediately available to the IRS staff.
Once all the data is entered into the system, the RMS staff pass them and make a selection of cases that correspond to certain criteria.
The selected VAT returns must be rechecked by the IRS staff on the basis of a control report drawn up by the system.
(see Section 5.2).
Although the tax administration has to roughly estimate the amount of VAT that the taxpayer must pay the estimated tax must be as accurate as possible.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, payers file VAT returns within 25 days after the end of the tax period.
The tax period, depending on the amount of turnover of the payer, is either the calendar quarter or the calendar month.
In GERMANY served to the payer preliminary VAT returns, depending on the tax liability in the previous year, either within 10 days after the end of the calendar quarter, or month.
Until 31. in May of the following year, payers are required to file an annual tax return.
The obligation to file an annual VAT return has its pros and cons:
+ about the end of the calendar year, the payer is able to correct errors in (monthly preliminary) tax returns by filing a single annual VAT return;
– if the payer corrects the awarded intracommunitary transactions, the correction may not be related to the period for which the summary report is submitted;
– the federal states usually do not compare the VIEs data on intracommunitary acquisitions of German payers before processing the annual VAT return.
In accordance with the marketing authorisation (see. 4.1.3) German payers are obliged to file an annual VAT return irrespective of the amount of their turnover.
This obligation allows the German financial authority to check the maximum turnover limit for small entrepreneurs.
In addition, the Responsible Tax Office is able to compare the annual VAT returns with the direct tax returns and the final accounts.
In the Czech Republic, tax administrators are able to determine the amount of the payer's turnover only from the filed income tax returns.
Unlike the Czech Republic, payers in Germany are obliged to file VAT returns in electronic form.
The introduction of the obligation to file tax returns electronically in the Czech Republic would help to increase the efficiency of the Czech tax administration.
Summary reports
Reporting and processing of summary reports in the Czech Republic
The summary report (hereinafter referred to as "SH") shall be submitted in accordance with the provisions of § 102 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. the payer who made the delivery of the goods to another member state to a tax-registered person in another member state.
Data on the value of the delivered goods shall be always in the Czech currency in breakdown by individual tax entities, indicating their VAT ID under which they are registered in their country.
Data on services provided are not included in the SH.
SH shall be filed by payers with both monthly and quarterly tax periods for each calendar quarter within 25 days of its termination to the local tax office.
Correction of erroneous data is carried out in the subsequent SH within 15 days from the date of detection of errors.
The erroneous data in SH shall always be replaced by the data in the subsequent sh.
Like tax returns, payers can also file sh in electronic form.
In the event that the payer does not submit SH or subsequent sh and had them under Act No. 235/2004 Coll. file, prompts by the administrator of the tax to his administration and at the same time to learn about the consequences in the event of non-SH or subsequent SH, so that the tax administrator pursuant to section 37 of the act no. 337/1992 Sb. authorized for failure to fulfil obligations non-cash nature repeatedly impose a fine of up to $ 2 000 000 Czk (67 EUR 150).
The audit of the Sao found that the tax authorities did not usually use the possibility of imposing a fine on payers for non-compliance with their legal obligations.
In particular, in the case of SH are not tax entities sufficiently motivated to perform their duties, because no SH has no effect on the tax liability of VAT.
The tax administrator is obliged according to § 102 para. 5 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. the data in SH, or subsequent sh, shall be examined, any uncertainties removed and the data used for the determination of the tax liability.
In case of discrepancy of data in the SH and the data in the relevant (payers with a monthly tax period) or relevant (payers with a quarterly tax period) VAT return should the tax administrator to verify the accuracy of declared tax obligations referred to in the VAT return.
Erroneous data in SH the tax entity removes by submitting the subsequent SH itself, or may be prompted to do so.
The Tax Administrator shall correct the data on the supply of goods to other member states in the ADIS system in the event that::
– the payer shall not prove the information specified in SH (or subsequent SH), correcting it by submitting a subsequent SH,
- the tax administrator has shown that the information given by the payer in SH or subsequent sh is not true.
The tax administrator by inserting the repairs without filing a subsequent SH payer does not replace the filing of a tax entity, it only adjusts the information in the database VIES to keep it current, complete and accurate.
Sh data shall be sent to the member states concerned.
Can it send and receive only the national authority of the financial administration, designed to cooperate with other member states in the field of VAT; it is a DUTY (in the CZECH republic to perform this function, the MOF, the department of International cooperation in the administration of VAT (DUTY).
O_MCTL is an automatic message that customs duties receive from other member states.
Contains all faulty VAT ID specified in sent sh rows.
If an erroneous VAT ID is used in one of the transferred normal rows of SH or subsequent SH, an entry is made to the erroneous VAT ID table.
The table contains the so-called "notice of doubt on VAT ID".
The Tax Administrator shall verify the data and record the result of the verification in the system.
When acquiring goods from another member state, the payer is obliged to declare VAT and indicate the values of the acquisition on separate lines of the VAT return.
Selected cases of irregularities in the value of the procured goods declared by the Czech payer in his VAT return and in the value of the goods delivered, as stated by the payer from other member states in their SH, they are sent from DUTY on the irs to investigate.
Tax administrators have an obligation to investigate irregularities.
Three situations may occur:
(a) the value declared by the Czech payer in the relevant lines of VAT returns is lower than the value of the delivery declared by the EU payers.
In this case, the tax administrator will check the correctness of the data.
(B) the amount of the difference is 0.
This situation may occur either by changing the data in the EU (the foreign supplier will repair your SH) or by changing the data in the VAT return (the Czech tax entity itself in the meantime submits an additional tax return to VAT).
In this case, it is at the discretion of the tax administrator, whether despite this fact will verify the accuracy of the data in the VAT return.
(C) the value of the acquisition of goods from other member states indicated by the Czech taxpayer in the relevant lines of the VAT return is higher than the value of the goods delivered declared by the EU payers.
It is also at the discretion of the controller to verify the accuracy of the data.
After checking the difference and clarifying the causes of its occurrence, the tax administrator will put the result of the verification in the ADIS.
The screening results are transferred back to customs.
The number of cases sent from customs duties to the tax authorities for examination for each quarter of 2005 is shown in Chart No. 1 (note source: MF).
The above graph 1 shows that the number of cases transferred from DUTY to the fiscal authorities for each quarter of 2005 declined.
A significant decrease in the number occurred in 4. quarter 2005. The duty has increased the minimum threshold, including in view of the possibility of sending requests for information to other EU member states.
The discrepancy between VAT returns and EU data may not always be due to an error on the part of the domestic payer.
It may also be an error on the part of EU payers or an error arising from the fact that in individual EU member states certain types of transactions may be placed in a different way.

Reporting and processing of summary reports in Germany
Entrepreneurs, who carry out intracommunity supplies from GERMANY to other EU member states or are involved in the tripartite transactions, are obliged to submit every quarter of a year SH, in which are listed intracommunity supplies according to the beneficiaries (§ 18a para. 1 UStG).
SH must be administered within 10. on the month following the relevant calendar quarter.
If an extension of this period is allowed in the case of preliminary VAT returns, this also applies to SH.
Shinzo Abe: Shinzo Abe has been given the all-clear.
From 1. January 2007 must be submitted electronically.
Exceptions may be granted by the competent tax authorities certain tax payers, in order to avoid undue hardship.
In cases where taxpayers realise that the sh contains incorrect data, they are required to submit a corrective report within one month.
In the event that taxpayers do not file an SH, the duty shall initiate proceedings to enforce the submission of this report.
Part of this procedure is: – first reminder – second reminder associated with the threat of fines/periodic penalty payments, and – the assessment of a penalty.
Although the German tax code allows a fine of up to EUR 25 000 (§ 329 AO), it measures the fine in three steps, amounting to EUR 125, 250 and 500.
Furthermore, § 26a para. 1 no. 5 UStG stipulates that the payers are acting illegally if they deliberately or negligently do not submit a properly SH, shake it is incomplete, do not submit them in a timely manner or if at all they fix or repair late SH.
This offence can be punished with a fine of up to 5 000 euros.
Data on intracommunitary deliveries can not be entered in the VIEs by the tax authority, since the processing of SH is the sole task of customs duties.
Sh data is stored only in the duty system.
Therefore, sh data are visually available to the IRS only after processing them into customs duties.
The deadlines for processing SH are set out in Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003.
SH data must be stored within three months following the relevant calendar quarter.
In the event of incorrect VAT ID in the SH German payers receive the duty from another member state with the o_mctl codes.
Customs contacts a particular entrepreneur and asks him for the correct data.
If the duty fails to obtain the right information, the case is transmitted to the relevant tax authorities.
It is then up to these tax authorities to request the correct data.
During the inspection, BRH found that most entrepreneurs VAT ID at the request of Customs corrected.
However, the challenge, the threat and the assessment of three additional fines occupies in cases where the payer may be involved in cross-border carousel fraud, too much time.
These cases, which were ultimately reported to the competent financial authorities, were usually completed within one or two months.
The IRS denied exemptions for reported intracommunity deliveries in 73% of those cases.
When the payer provided the correct VAT ID, the IRS asked him to file for the duty corrected SH, since the IRS can not fix the data in VIES on its own.
The BRH found that neither the tax authorities nor Customs had checked the filing of the corrected SH, so payers often did not comply with the requests.
Due to the fact that the DUTY does not have access to the data from the VAT returns, the comparison of the data about the delivery of goods declared in VAT return and in the SH is not carried out prior to the submission of these data the DUTY of the other member states.
This control can only be carried out by the tax authorities and is usually applied in the preparation of VAT control.
Data obtained from other member states shall be processed into customs duties.
Incorrect VAT ID is selected and then submitted to the member states concerned.
These data are used for the purposes of the control of acquisitions carried out by the tax authorities.
Once they are entered into the system, the duty will recheck them based on comparisons with data from previous calendar quarters.
Where they meet certain criteria (see 5.2), control information shall be generated and sent to the relevant tax authorities.
This procedure is applied steadily, while the compilation of data on the acquisition of goods or services for all VAT payer is created later and submitted to the tax authorities.
The RMS installed for the purposes of the assessment procedure shall subsequently double-check these data with intracommunitary acquisition data.
This system completely covers those entrepreneurs who do not have a full right to deduct VAT.
Comparison and evaluation
In the CZECH republic submitted to the payer who made the delivery of goods to another member state to a person registered for tax in another member state, SH within 25 days after the end of the calendar quarter, the locally competent tax office.
The tax authorities will process the SH and transfer the data to the duty.
The value of the supply of goods to another member state, referred to the payer in the SH, are in the financial offices compared with the values of supplies of goods to another member state, set out by these payers in the VAT returns.
The results of the comparison are used in the measurement procedure.
In Germany, payers who have made intracommunitary delivery are required to submit quarterly SH, up to 10. on the following calendar quarter.
SH payers serve on duty, from 1. 1. 2007 in electronic form.
The tax authorities have information from SH only available after processing them for customs duties.
Payers from the Czech Republic and Germany State in SH only the supply of goods, the supply of services is not specified in SH.
Unlike the Czech tax authorities, the German tax authorities are not able to correct the erroneous lines filed by SH on their own.
As a result of this limited access to data of the German VIES wasn't wrong VAT ID fixed, even if the payer gave the tax office the correct VAT ID.
The German tax administration does not compare the data on intracommunitary deliveries, which are indicated in the VAT return of the German payer and his sh.
Differences between the data of these two statements are usually not detected before the German duty provides data from VIES to other member states.
Given the BRH findings, it is clear that the comparison would increase the reliability of the data transmitted in VIES.
Data about the delivery of goods to the Czech tax payers, received from other member states, in the CZECH republic are compared with data on acquisition of goods from other member states declared by Czech payers in their tax returns for VAT.
Comparisons carry out duties separately for each calendar quarter.
The most significant cases of irregularities are forwarded to the financial authorities such as alerts for possible errors in the tax returns of payers.
Unlike the Czech tax administration, the German tax administration does not usually control the taxation of intracommunitary acquisitions.
Such a general check is processed only for payers who do not have a full right to deduct VAT.
In addition, the German tax administration controls the tax intrakomunitárních acquisition of other payers only, if RMS produce a control notice, or if the tax payer is designed for control anyway.
This procedure relieves the tax authorities from the need to clarify the reasons for each difference.
On the other hand, the detection of VAT fraud depends on the quality of the RMS.
Combating carousel fraud requires continuously updated information on intracommunitary acquisitions as soon as possible.
The current sh system, specially VIES, provides financial authorities with information that can be up to six months old.
This delay may be shortened by up to four months if payers serve Sherlock monthly.
Monthly filing would not be a significant increase in bureaucratic costs, since most payers in the Czech Republic and Germany are required to file monthly VAT returns – and SH does not require any additional information compared to the tax return.
In order to avoid bureaucratic costs, filing SH may be associated with filing a VAT return.
However, the obligation to submit SH monthly would cause more time disagreements between the reporting of intracommunity delivery and intracommunity acquisition, and could increase the flow of data between individual duties.
In 2006, the German federal government considered the general provisions of the monthly SH.
Its implementation failed because of the doubts of federal states.
They feared that the monthly submission of vies data to customs by other member states could lead to misunderstandings and confusion.
In fact, if the obligation of monthly submission of SH and monthly data transfer should be efficient, the monthly update of the VIES would require a european standard monthly SH.
