Level 3 International Information Exchange
Implementation of the international exchange of information in the Czech Republic
The international exchange of information allows tax authorities to obtain from other member states information regarding intrakomunitárních commercial transactions and taxpayers that these transactions happen.
Council regulation (EC) no 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing regulation (EEC) no 218/92, distinguishes between two basic categories of information exchange, and the exchange of information on request and exchange of information without prior request.
The international exchange of information on request is carried out in the form of so-called requests for information (hereinafter referred to as "Joi"), using standardised SCAC forms.
The tax authorities of the CZECH republic is sending its RFIS, or answers to the RFIS through the financial directorate, customs DUTY, which ensures the translation of the information provided on standardized forms SCAC into a foreign language and their dispatch to other member states.
The DUTY also ensures the intake of RFIS from other member states and the replies to the sent RFIS, their translation into Russian and distribution of the locally competent tax authorities for execution.
In art. 8 Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003 provides for a maximum period of 3 months from the date of receipt of the application.
The Sao scrutiny was carried out by all Sao, transmitted during the controlled period between the Czech Republic and Germany.
Of the total number of 94 RFIS, taken in the CZECH republic from GERMANY, was 70 cases (i.e. 74,5 %) settled within the prescribed three-month period, the other 23 cases (i.e. 24,5 %) were settled after this period and the remaining 1 case was not to the time of the SAO audit, the answer to GERMANY sent.
More detailed information on the deadlines during which responses to the Czech Republic received from the Czech Republic were sent from the Czech Republic contains graph 2.
Of the total number of 335 RFIS sent from the CZECH republic to GERMANY was on 136 cases (i.e., 40.6% of) the answer delivered within the stipulated three-month period, other 179 (i.e. 53,4 %) requests were answered after the deadline and for 19 cases (i.e., 5.7 %) is not to the time of the SAO audit, the reply of the federal republic of GERMANY received (in the remaining 1 case was of the transmitted data can determine when the response from GERMANY delivered).
For more detailed information on the deadlines which have been to the CZECH republic delivered responses to RFIS sent to GERMANY, includes graph no.3.
The percentage expression of the values of intracommunitary transactions, indicated in the ŽOI transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany, includes graph 4.
As can be seen from the chart above, the value of commercial transactions, verified through the Joi, most often ranged in the band above 60 000 euros.
The international exchange of information without prior request shall take place either by automatic or structured automatic exchange of information, or in the form of spontaneous exchange of information.
Tax authorities from other member states are often provided with information that may be relevant to them in the management of VAT without prior request.
In the Czech Republic, All information is collected on customs duties.
Information shall be transmitted electronically between member states.
"Automatic exchange" according to the Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003, means the systematic communication of predefined information to other member states without prior request, at pre-established regular intervals.
"Structured automatic exchange", then, means the systematic communication of predefined information to other member states without prior request and as soon as that information becomes available.
The Czech Republic provides other member states with information on the delivery of new means of transport in the form of automatic exchange.
This information is available to the tax authorities from the form of the report on the delivery of a new means of transport pursuant to § 19 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. and a copy of the tax document issued.
The tax administrator fills in the processing of the above-mentioned form data into a specially created template and forward them promptly to the liaison worker in the financial directorate, where these data are collected in a timely fashion, i.e. at the latest within two months from the end of the quarter in which such information is available, forwarded to the DUTY for subsequent processing and transmission to other member states.
Further provided by the CZECH republic to other member states information on distance selling, which is exempt from VAT in the member state of origin, information about the operations within the EU, which appear to be unjustified and the information on potential "missing traders".
That information shall be sent to other member states in the form of spontaneous exchange using the SCAC form.
Implementation of international information exchange in Germany
In Germany, both requests for information and the processing of spontaneous information are initiated by the local tax office.
The tax authorities send the completed SCAC 2004 form by email directly to the German customs office, which transmits the SCAC forms to foreign customs.
The financial authorities were instructed to write their requests for information or its own spontaneous information only in German; even the used form SCAC is not multilingual.
Half of the German requests for information, controlled BRH has been sent with the aim of ensuring the taxation of intrakomunitárního acquisition in another member state, where appropriate, to demonstrate the liberation of intrakomunitárního delivery from GERMANY to another member state from the tax.
If the German CUSTOMS receives a request for information from another member state shall check the value of the supply of goods or the provision of services referred to in the application for a minimum limit of 15 000 EUROS.
If for this application there is no reasonable reason, German CUSTOMS will reject any request containing an amount lower than this limit.
In addition, the German DUTY translates free texts form SCAC [(B1-17) or (E)], if these texts are not in German nor in English.
To answer the request for information, the duty sends the request to the relevant tax office, pointing out a three-month period.
There are no additional deadlines for processing applications at specific organizational levels of tax administration.
Although the German duty has technical conditions for monitoring the elapsed time limits, it lacks sufficient staffing capacity to notify the tax authorities of the answer to unfilled requests for information.
The tax authorities get the necessary information by sending a letter to the taxpayer or carrying out an audit.
Auditors usually choose between two distinct types of audits: the special audit of VAT, which applies to any taxable process over a period of several months or the so-called inspection of the VAT, which may be for only one trading operation, which was carried out recently.
This short and flexible type of audit does not require any notification to the taxpayer and has demonstrated its usefulness in the investigation of the individual's taxable business operations.
In the framework of the automatic exchange, without prior request, provides the federal republic of GERMANY to other member states information about the VAT ID assigned payers who are resident in other member states, – the repayment of input tax the tax payers who are resident in other member states.
In addition, the German authorities undertook to provide other member states with the following information through structured automatic exchange:
and. Delivery of new means of transport to entrepreneurs without the use of their VAT ID, B. forwarding or catalogue sales in other member states not taxable in Germany, C. significant differences between intracommunitary purchases declared by the payer and VIES data provided by other member states, D. intracommunitary delivery of goods, which the German payer did not report in SH, because he treated the deliveries as domestic transactions, e. the potential "missing trader", which made intracommunity transactions independently of the validity of their VAT ID, f. entrepreneurs who supplied goods to potential "missing traders" or those recipients who have abused their VAT ID.
Comparison and evaluation
The dispatch of Joi or spontaneous information is initiated both in the Czech Republic and in Germany by the local competent tax authorities, which send the completed SCAC form for customs duties.
While the Czech CLO uses a bilingual form to SCAC (English – English) and sent the information translates into the English or the German language, the German financial authorities are governed by instructions according to which they have write RFIS or spontaneous information only in German at the jednojazyčném form.
German customs does not guarantee the translation of German texts.
Vetting of the Joi submitted in the period from 1. 5. 2004 to 31. 12. 2005 between CZECH republic and GERMANY found the SAO, the Czech tax administration settled the matter within the prescribed three-month time limit for 74.5% of the received requests, while the RFIS sent to GERMANY were the German tax administration are dealt with in the prescribed period only in 40.6% of cases.
Although the German duty warns the tax authorities of a three-month period, it does not monitor the elapsed time limits.
The result of the missing alerts is a large number of delayed responses to the Joi.
Because of these problems, the BRH recommended regular alerts on tariffs.
The situation has already improved.
According to the latest information, the German duty now alerts the tax authorities to answer unfinished answers to the Joi.
VAT risk management
Risk management in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, VAT risk management deals with several departments at different organizational levels of tax administration.
Within the framework of the MF, the following departments deal with the issues of risk management and combating VAT fraud:
The Department of VAT methodology and enforcement and within it a VAT risk management report which, inter alia, manages the selection of risks of possible tax evasion and evaluates the trends of these risks at domestic and community level.
It coordinates nationwide the functioning of the role of the credibility of VAT returns and the use of VIES data in terms of the risks of tax evasion in intracommunitary transactions.
Based on data from the Czech trade balance, the Czech Republic evaluates risk commodities, processes conceptually VAT risk management and cooperates in this area with the relevant EU institutions and with other member states.
Department of International cooperation in the administration of VAT, which, inter alia, provides for the exchange of information in the field of VAT, involved in the creation and maintenance of information databases, analyzes the data from other member states contained in the VIES, ensures public awareness and provides other forms of international cooperation within the meaning of Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003.
Both SAI requested data on the number of wrong tin or VAT IDs contained in the o_mctl reports transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany for each quarter of the audited period.
These data are contained in the following tables.
The data show substantial differences.
The cause of these differences may be a different basis for determining the number of o_mctl messages.
While the Czech CLO relates their numbers to the calendar quarter in which it was filed SH, German the DUTY relates their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the report was O_MCTL taken.
Department of Methodology of tax inspection and search, which, inter alia, conducted a risk analysis in the framework of methodical management of tax inspections and in accordance with the risk analysis sets the priorities for the focus of tax inspections in the plans of the financial directorate, processes risk analysis in the context of reducing tax evasion, including the collection of knowledge obtained in the administration of taxes and from other sources and suggests measures to reduce tax evasion.
The financial directorates are set up the search department, which shall carry out, inter alia, a search of tax subjects and areas, which are risky from the point of view of the occurrence of tax fraud (e.g. internet shops, the gold, the pharmaceutical industry), search of unregistered tax agents in terms of risk of tax evasion (e.g. from the field of internet services, mediation of work, radio, and print services, etc.), the analysis links the string of fraud and transmission of information to the territorial financial authorities.
On the selected 12 tax authorities, specialized control departments are established.
They have regional competence, tax inspections outside the territorial competence of the tax authorities are carried out on the basis of mandates.
Need to set up a department specialized tax inspections resulted on the basis of the increasing detection of new and improved forms of tax evasion, that occur especially in subjects linked to the chains.
This department focus on the control of tax bodies according to the requirements of the search department, tax entities with specific activities and multinational companies and tax bodies of a large range of activities in terms of size of turnover.
The system of the ADIS have been integrated following the mechanisms used to limit risks in the field of VAT: – the role of Credibility of the tax returns of VAT, used to evaluate the riskiness of filed tax returns, – the role of Selection of taxpayers for inspection, allowing you to choose from based on the selection criteria of the payer to control – the role of the VIES, through which they have to the tax authorities access to data provided from other member states of the EU.
The role of the VIES allows, inter alia: – examine the validity of the VAT ID of the payers of other member states, – to obtain from other member states of the value of the goods delivered to the Czech payer, declared in the SH all his suppliers from other member states, – generate a report of payers who have not lodged SH, – to carry out a formal check of the data, that payers of the CZECH republic stated in the SH, before sending these data to other member states, – generate a report of payers, for which data on the supply of goods to other member states referred to in the VAT returns do not coincide with the data in the SH, – generate a report of payers, for which the value of acquisition of goods from other member states referred to in the VAT returns does not coincide with the data declared in the SH all his suppliers from other member states.
In the framework of the activities to mitigate risk of tax evasion are the tax administrator access to the registers of public authorities such as commercial register, land register, register of motor vehicles the registry of business trade etc.
More detailed information is provided in Chapter 4.4.1 submission and processing of summary reports in the Czech Republic.
Risk management in Germany
Due to the federative (federal) structure of GERMANY the federal tax administration (especially CUSTOMS) and the tax administration of the 16 federal states involved in the development and operation of the RMS.
Although there are joint development working groups, neither customs nor tax administrations of federal states share a completely consistent database.
At the level of the DUTY, collects department ST I 2 (hereinafter referred to as "PIECES" – coordination unit for special audits, VAT and tax investigation) the findings of the audit relating to tax fraud in a special database called OPUS.
KUSS, in collaboration with the tax authorities, introduced a new database called ZAUBER designed to transmit the names of tax fraudsters "missing traders".
KUSS coordinates related cases of national and cross-border tax fraud.
The experience of KUSS is reflected in the development of RMS in working groups.
In addition, the specialists of several other departments of Customs and MF are entrusted with the duties and powers associated with the RMS.
At the level of customs duties, a formal control of the composition of VAT ID of other member states in the SH submitted by German payers is established.
This formal inspection is performed prior to providing the data from the SH to the other member states, to improve the clarity and use of the data provided VIES (see 4.4.2).
Verification of the validity of the VAT ID mentioned in the SH is done on the basis of codes O_MCTL provided by other member states (for the procedure for correcting an invalid VAT ID, see. also 4.4.2).
In addition, it is the RMS DUTY is based on data from VIES to be transmitted by other member states and creates several types of control messages based on several characteristics, which usually figure in the so-called revolving business operations, in order to identify potential "missing traders".
The federal tax authorities are instructed to process these Control reports and, in some cases, report on the results of their duties findings.
The findings of the audit of the BRH has confirmed that it is necessary to take into account all available characteristics, it has to be with sufficient probability implied the existence of a case of tax fraud (instead of an exclusive focus on the company's turnover).
Therefore, the BRH suggested to the MF that different characteristics should be taken into account when processing reports.
RMS should also be affected by other factors, such as payment behaviour (morale) of the taxpayer, discipline (economic activities) or shareholder structure.
The second level of RMS is processed in the tax administrations of the federal states and is aimed at processing VAT returns.
For example, RMS generates a list of those payers who have reported intracommunitary delivery in tax returns.
This list is sent to customs to monitor the full filing of SH.
In addition, this type of RMS compares the intracommunitary acquisition, reported in the payer'S annual VAT return, with data from the VIES system.
The tax administration of the federal states is trying to avoid comparisons to quarterly data because this comparison would reveal too many discordant data, which are attributed to other reasons than tax evasion or tax fraud; for example,:
- different period of implementation of the intracommunitary transaction in the opinion of the supplier, on the one hand, and the recipient, on the other;
– different accounting treatment of sales discounts and sales promotions (incentives) and their different reporting in the tax return.
In addition to comparing data from tax returns to VAT and system VIES many federal states have introduced elements of the RMS, which are based on the data of tax returns for VAT and some other facts (such as, for example, the structure of the title company, the age of the shareholders, number of employees and payment behaviour/ morality of the taxpayer).
Bavaria introduced the RMS based on the rules, which allow the team of specialists on tax fraud (hereinafter referred to as risk managers) to program your own rules for the exclusion of potential perpetrators of tax fraud.
This RMS is applied at the moment when the tax authorities process the monthly VAT return.
Therefore, the competent tax authority will receive a recommendation made by the RMS before the VAT is fixed.
Since this RMS is unable to reflect current findings in its activities, risk managers must adjust the relevant rules based on feedback from the tax authorities.
Administrative district Mecklenburg-Western Pomerania programmed adaptive artificial neural network with the data of tax files in which the check revealed the tax evasion.
Based on these data, the RMS is able to determine the characteristics of tax evasion.
RMS creates a monthly list of tax files suspected of tax evasion.
The relevant tax authorities use this list as a basis for deciding on the audit of proposed taxpayers.
After the audit has been carried out, auditors must report on their findings so that the results of the list can be reflected in the RMS.
The administrative area of North Rhine-Westphalia uses adaptive artificial neural network, which is combined with a system of fuzzy-based rules.
On the basis of a large number of data assessed tax returns for VAT and some other facts this neural-fuzzy system or a system of selection of potentially useful information (the so-called data-mining system) calculates the probability that a taxpayer committed tax fraud.
After that, he compiles a monthly list of potential perpetrators of fraud.
Local financial authorities use this list as a basis for the selection of taxpayers for review and reported the findings of the control centre for data processing.
The introduction of one of these three RMS in the other Länder is ongoing.
Since none of these three RMS are based on the same approach, a combination of all systems seems useful for dealing with tax fraud.
The question remains whether this system will lead to the expected results.
Comparison and evaluation
Although in this report cannot be discussed specific criteria RMS in the CZECH republic and GERMANY, the SAO and the BRH found that each member state has developed its own RMS.
As well as the different approaches in the three federal states of Germany, the RMS of each EU state has its strengths and weaknesses.
The tax authorities of EU member states are currently discussing new trends and new models of cross-border VAT fraud.
VAT fraud - especially carousel fraud-does not turn out to be a national but rather a European problem.
Payers in fraudulent activities act simultaneously not only in one member state, but in several states.
An effective RMS cannot be developed by only one member state.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in each EU member state, otherwise fraudsters will choose the member state with the weakest RMS.
The loss of VAT due to fraud in the EU may not affect the member state of the initiator of the fraud.
Any member state involved in fraudulent activities may be affected.
Therefore, there should be a European Exchange and discussion of the RMS.
Selected control findings in the verification of business transactions
In the framework of cooperation in realization of parallel control actions, check the SAO and BRH quality and use of information about the selected business transactions that were the subject of international exchange of information between the tax administrations of the CZECH republic and GERMANY.
Furthermore, the two audit institutions jointly check the implementation of several business transactions, for which there were doubts about their implementation, or inconsistencies in the way the payers of both countries, these business transactions had reported in its tax returns for VAT, or SH.
At the request of BRH, the Sao examined a total of 8 cases relating to commercial transactions between 8 Czech and 8 German tax entities.
In 43 cases, the Sao examined the values of INTRACOMMUNITARY transactions with SRN reported by Czech payers in their tax returns and SH.
At the request of the Sao, BRH examined a total of 23 cases relating to commercial transactions between 23 German and 21 Czech tax entities.
Important information has been exchanged under Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003 through official communication with customs duties.
The examination of selected cases found, inter alia, that a different method of registration in EU member states leads to the problems mentioned in Chapter 4.1:
1.
According to data in VIES, the Czech payer should have acquired in III. quarter 2004 from the German payer of goods worth EUR 60 500.
Since the Czech payer only reported the acquisition of the goods worth EUR 29 869, the Czech tax administrator sent a request to Germany to verify the value of the goods delivered.
In response to a letter delivered from Germany, the German side stated that in II. quarter 2004, the German payer supplied the Czech payer with goods worth EUR 27 381, in III. quarter of EUR 31 997 and IV. quarter 2004 worth EUR 10 276.
The reply further indicated that the VAT ID of the German payer was valid only from 28. 9. 2004, but the German duty in 2006 at the additional request of the German payer for a certificate of validity of VAT ID retroactively issued a certificate of validity of VAT ID from 1. 5. 2004.
The German payer made a correction SH.
On the basis of this information, the Czech payer was the acquisition of the goods.
SAO by asking the local tax authority in the CZECH republic found that the Czech payer on the basis of the investigation, the tax administrator filed for each tax period of the year 2004, additional tax returns for VAT, in which the increased value of the goods acquired from other member states and at the same time claim to deduct VAT on acquisitions of goods from other member states.
Of these additional tax returns to VAT, however, the Czech tax administrator could not clearly determine whether they also included the value of the supply from the above German supplier.
On the basis of a request from the SAO, the BRH found that the German supplier was registered for VAT in September 2003.
However, since he did not apply for a VAT ID at the time of registration, he was assigned only an identification number for transactions within the SRN.
Although in Germany it is not normally possible to allocate a VAT ID to a payer retroactively, in this case the German tax officer assigned the above-mentioned German VAT ID payer retroactively to 1.5.2004 in 2006.
The German CUSTOMS allocates a VAT ID retroactively, if a German businessman did not cause a delay in the allocation; for example, if the delay caused DUTY after plátcově application for a VAT ID.
In this case, the duty allocates VAT ID retroactively, since the entrepreneur does not need his own valid VAT ID for intracommunitary delivery under Section 6 of the German VAT Act.
On the contrary, the German recipient does not need a valid VAT ID of his supplier in order to declare an intracommunitary acquisition.
Due to these different practices among member states, the German duty was retroactively allocated in this particular case to the VAT ID.
2.
As part of the international exchange of information on the examination of the registration of the German VAT payer, the Czech tax administrator asked for VAT.
VIES reported a registration date of 5. 3. 2005, whereby the date 1 was indicated on the registration certificate of the German payer issued locally by the competent German tax authority. 10. 2004.
In the reply received from Germany, the German party stated that the German tax entity had been registered since 1. 10. 2004, but VAT ID was provided to him in Germany for organizational reasons up to 16. 2. 2005.
By asking the local tax administrator, the Sao found that the Czech tax administrator had carried out a VAT check on the Czech tax payer during tax period III. quarters 2004 to II. quarter 2005.
This control of the financial bureau found that the Czech payer has included in the VAT tax return services worth 9 897 Czk (314 EUROS), granted by the German payer in the period before his registration for VAT (i.e. before 1. 10. 2004).
For tax period III. quarter 2004, the tax office paid VAT to the tax entity amounting to CZK 1 880 (EUR 60).
According to the request of the SAO, the BRH found that the German payer was assigned a VAT ID of up to 16. 2. 2005, when he informed the Tax Office of his business, which he started in 2004.
In addition, the Tax Office registered it for VAT retrospectively on 1. October 200415 to monitor the filing of the annual VAT return for 2004.
In this tax return the payer reported intracommunitary acquisition from the Czech Republic worth 160 euros (about 5000 CZK).
3. The Czech payer declared in the VAT return for September 2004 and SH for III. quarter 2004 delivery of goods worth CZK 114,615 (EUR 3,642) to the German payer.
The Czech tax administrator, when verifying the registration of the German payer in the VIES system, found that his registration was valid from 11. 11. 2004, i.e. only after delivery of the goods by the Czech payer to Germany.
The Czech payer submitted an additional VAT DAP in which he declared the tax base on transactions made in the Czech Republic worth CZK 114 615 (EUR 3 642) and VAT of CZK 21 777 (EUR 692), which he paid.
NKU query with the relevant tax authority in the CZECH republic found that the Czech payer subsequently filed an application for retrial in the matter of additional tax returns for VAT and as a means of evidence submitted confirming the German tax administration that the German payer was tax led from 1. 1. 2000.
Therefore, the Czech tax administrator verified the validity of the registration of the German payer in the framework of the international exchange of information.
The reply received from Germany indicated that up to 11 were allocated to the German payer. 11. 2004, i.e. after the date of delivery of the goods.
For this reason, the tax administrator in the Czech Republic rejected the request for retrial.
BRH found that, in the present case was not an intracommunity acquisition of goods, because the German payer received a VAT ID to 11.11.2004.
However, the German recipient has reported the acquisition as an intracommunity acquisition and showed a VAT on this purchase, he demanded the refund of input tax in the same amount.
However, there were no changes in the value of the VAT, which had a German payer's obligation to pay, didn't fix the tax administrator in GERMANY data in his VAT return.
The BRH also found that the name of the German payer referred to in the ŽOI was changed during the processing of the reply in Germany, resulting in the confusion of two German tax entities.
This change in the name of the German payer also confused the Czech tax administrator.
4.
As part of the international exchange of information, the German tax administrator verified the acquisition of goods by the Czech payer in I. quarter 2005 worth EUR 22 686 from the German payer.
NKU asking at the locally competent tax administrator in the CR, found out that this manager has performed in the Czech payer of the local investigation, which verified that the delivery of the goods took place and the Czech payer of the invoice for the goods in question were booked and paid.
The Czech payer admitted the acquisition of goods in the VAT return, because the German supplier on the invoice did not indicate their VAT ID, but only the tax number intended for domestic transactions in GERMANY.
In the application of VIES, the Czech tax administrator found that the German payer was registered for VAT for intracommunity transactions 21. 4. 2005, i.e. after delivery to the Czech payer.
The Czech tax administrator also asked the German tax administration by sending a copy of the certificate of registration of the German tax payer, if necessary, could take steps to tax assessment.
The Czech Tax Authority assessed the transaction in question as acquisition of goods from the non-payer from Germany and therefore did not charge the Czech tax on that transaction.
BRH found that the German legislation does not have a payer who supplies the goods to other member states, allocated a VAT ID, in order to intracommunity supplies of goods exempt from VAT.
The supplier must only have at his disposal a VAT ID of the purchaser from another member state and be able to demonstrate the transport of the goods in question to another member state.
Thus, according to the German VAT Act, it was an intracommunitary transaction, and VAT should be charged in the Czech Republic.
In any case, it is important that the Czech tax administrator noticed this transaction, since the delivery of the machine at that value was not the basic object of the German supplier's business.
As described in chapter 4.6.2, the German DUTY to refuse to answer RFIS that relate to intrakomunitárních transactions worth less than EUR 15 000: 5.
The Czech payer had, according to data from VIES in III. quarter 2004 acquire from the German payer goods worth 12 561 euros.
The Czech tax administrator carried out a tax inspection with the tax entity for this tax period.
In the framework of international administrative cooperation, the German tax administration requested through the SCAC form to verify the delivery of these goods.
The Czech payer of the acquisition of goods denied, claiming that with the German company never traded and in his accounts was the acquisition of the goods posted.
The German tax authorities the requirement to provide evidence – contracts, orders, invoices and shipping documents rejected on the grounds that the turnover does not exceed a value of 15 000 EUR and was listed no further explanatory justification.
Because the Czech tax administrator did not obtain evidence for additional tax assessment from the captured goods, he ended a tax audit without a finding, and the tax liability remained charged the original amount.
On the basis of a request from the SAO, the BRH found that the German payer acted as a so – called "fiscal representative" (§ 22 A-e UStG).
The German payer reported these deliveries in its annual VAT return and in SH.
The right to an exemption of delivery was recognized to him.
On the basis of the notice BRH, the German tax office will send to the Czech Republic the documents necessary for the tax on purchased goods in the Czech Republic.
As stated in Chapter 4.6.1, the replies to the CR sent from Germany to the CR exceeded the three-month deadline more frequently than the replies from the CR to Germany: 6.
The Sao audit found that the Czech Tax Administration sent on 5. 10. 2005 to Germany a request for information concerning the verification of the value of the goods delivered for 4. quarter 2004.
The German payer declared in SH for this period the delivery of goods to the Czech payer worth EUR 86 307, but the Czech payer stated in the same period in the VAT return the acquisition of goods only worth EUR 35 314.
In reply to ŽOI, delivered to the Czech Republic 9. 5. 2006, that is, after the expiry of the settlement period laid down in art. 8 Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003, the German party stated that the request could not be processed, since the operation of the German company was at the end of 2005 terminated.
Since the German tax administration failed to meet the deadline for the settlement of the ŽOI, the Czech tax administration did not have the documents necessary for the tax procedure in the Czech Republic.
7. In 2005, the Czech tax administrator requested, through the SCAC form, a verification of the delivery of cars worth EUR 1,265,554 to the German payer, carried out in III. and IV. quarter 2004, which showed signs of carousel fraud.
The Sao found that no response had been received from the Sao pending the inspection.
In addition, the Sao, by asking the local tax administrator, found that the Czech payer did not include in the VAT return the supply of new means of Transport for that German payer worth CZK 11 816 103 (EUR 375 472).
The Czech tax administrator corrected the data in the tax return and the Czech tax entity filed a subsequent SH.
On the basis of a request from the SAO, the BRH found that the German duty had not, for technical reasons, been forwarded by the aforementioned Joi to the local tax authority for examination.
After notice to BRH was in GERMANY conducted by the German maker of the check, in which it was found that the acquisition of all the car was properly taxed and that the cars were sold next to the payer in GERMANY.

The acquisition of these goods was not acknowledged by the Czech payer.
By asking the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the Sao found that the Czech payer had not filed VAT returns since August 2004.
Tax returns were not filed by the Czech payer even after calls from the tax administrator, the Tax Office therefore gave him 23. 5. 2005 levied VAT of CZK 0 for the period October to December 2004.
2. 6. 2005 the duty drew attention to the aforementioned delivery from the German payer.
Since the Czech payer did not cooperate with the tax administrator, he sent the tax administrator Zoi to Germany regarding the aforementioned delivery.
Because the answer to the Zoi was delivered to the Czech Republic up to 7. 2. 2007, until the end of the Sao audit, it was not known how the Czech tax administrator used the information obtained by the international exchange.
The Tax Office cancelled the Czech payer on 23. 8. 2005 VAT registration.

12.
In the framework of the international exchange of information, the German tax authority requested, through the SCAC form, to verify the supply of goods and services carried out in III. quarter 2005.
According to this ŽOI, the Czech payer should have delivered goods totalling EUR 396 126 to the German payer during this period and provided services worth EUR 11 885.
The Sao found that the Czech tax administrator had carried out a local investigation with the Czech taxpayer in order to verify this delivery.
In response to the ŽOI, the Czech tax administrator stated that the Czech payer had supplied the German payer with a production line including Assembly.
The individual parts of the production line were delivered by the Czech payer before the Czech entry into the EU and after 1. 5. 2004 the line was assembled on the basis of the order.
The German payer did not take the assembled line because it claimed to have defects.
In III. quarter 2005 the Czech payer issued invoices to the German payer for amounts of EUR 107 100 per assembly and EUR 11 885 for services.
The German payer took over the issued invoices, but did not recognize them and did not pay.
The Sao also found, by asking the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic, that all invoices are duly registered in the accounting of the Czech payer.
In VAT returns for III. quarter 2005 only amounts documented by the Czech payer relating to invoicing after 1 are listed. 5. 2004.
BRH found that based on a reply from the Czech tax administration, the local tax authority in Germany concluded that the transaction involved the delivery of goods from the Czech payer to the German payer, including assembly services.
In this special case, the place of so-called work filling is where the assembly of the production line occurred.
According to the German VAT Act, the German recipient of the delivered service is obliged to pay VAT.
At the same time, the recipient can claim a deduction of VAT from the same amount.
Since there would be no changes in the value of VAT which the German payer was obliged to pay, the corrections in the VAT return were neglected by the German tax office.
13. The Czech payer A was to acquire a machine worth EUR 58 000 from the German payer C in February 2005, according to data from VIES.
The Czech tax administrator sent a request to Germany to verify this delivery.
In response to the RFIS, the German party claimed that this machine already in 2004 the German payer C added Czech payer B, which, however, should this machine to the German payer C in October 2004 to return.
According to information of the German tax administration was the machine shipped back to GERMANY, but transported to the organizational units of the German payer C in the CZECH republic.
Furthermore, the reply to the request for information indicated that the German payer C sold the machine to the Czech payer A. in February 2005.
This payer machine took over at the headquarters of the organizational branch of the German payer C in the Czech Republic.
Since the delivery took place only within the Czech Republic, it was not an intracommunitary delivery of goods.
By asking the tax administrator locally responsible payer B, the Sao found that according to VIES data, the German payer C delivered in III. quarter 2004 Czech payer B goods (another machine) worth EUR 88 027.
Payer B denied this acquisition of the goods, therefore the local tax administrator of the Czech Republic sent the ŽOI to Germany.
According to the response to this request, the delivery of the machine took place.
Further investigation by the payer B found the Czech tax administrator that the machine in the value of the 88 027 EUROS in the accounts of the payer B did not find, and that this could be a machine of the same type was delivered to the organizational component of the German payer C the Czech payer And in February 2005.
The Sao also found that the Czech tax administrator was the local taxpayer and carried out a local investigation with that taxpayer.
The tax administrator had at his disposal an invoice from the German payer C of 7. 2. 2005, to which payer A. was listed as a customer of the machine.
The Czech tax administrator found that the payer A does not have this invoice included in the accounting.
The payer and had a lease agreement with another Czech company, where the object of the lease was a machine of the same type.
The handover of the machine from the leasing company took place 9. 2. 2005, the carriage of the machine was provided by the leasing company.
The information contained in the reply to the request for information was not used by the Czech tax authority to determine the tax liability for payer A.
BRH found that the German payer C machine worth EUR 88 027 did not deliver to the Czech Republic but to another German payer D.
Thus, it was not an intracommunitary supply of goods, but a taxable transaction in Germany.
For these reasons, the German tax administrator did not recognize the German taxpayer C exemption and corrected the data in his tax return.
German payer D supplied the machine to Czech payer B.
According to German legislation, this supply was not taxable in Germany, but was subject to VAT in the Czech Republic.
In addition, BRH found that the German payer C listed in its SH for I. quarter 2005 delivery of the machine worth EUR 58 000 to Czech payer A.
This delivery was not examined during the tax inspection carried out by the German tax authority.

20. According to the VIES data, the German payer acquired goods worth EUR 4 251 196 from the Czech Republic in 2005 after acquiring goods worth EUR 43 274 in the previous year.

As evidenced by the materials provided to the Sao by the competent tax authority, on 30. 3. 2006 a protocol was drawn up with the Czech payer's manager on the initiation of VAT control for IV. quarter 2004 and January to December 2005.
Payer was at the same time the tax administrator is prompted to submit all the accounting and tax documents for the above-mentioned period, but no documents submitted.
The sole executive of the Czech payer, according to the commercial register, was terminated on 16. 5. 2006, a new executive has not been appointed.
Since April 2006, the Czech payer has stopped filing VAT returns.
Under the control of the SAO in cooperation with the BRH, inter alia, examined several cases of intrakomunitárních delivery, carried out between the CZECH republic and GERMANY, which have not been subject to prior exchange of information between the tax administrations of both countries.
Information on the investigated cases was transmitted by the two Supreme Audit Institutions through the customs duties of both countries.
21. The Czech company (eCR), which is not resident in Germany, has informed the relevant tax office (Chemnitz-Süd) that it intends to carry out taxable transactions in Germany.
Due to this information, the company has been registered since June 2005, but has not received a German VAT ID.
(ECR) received an order from the Danish entrepreneur (eDK) on the production of several wind power plants and on delivery of such wind power plants on behalf of, at the risk and for the account of Danish customer in Austria.
Due to the lack of its own capacities, the Czech company handed over part of the order to the German payer (eD), which is based in Germany.
The following scheme shows contractual relationships and the way wind farms are transported:
According to the German legal situation, the place of execution of such transactions must be determined according to the following:
- Danish entrepreneur (eDK) sent wind farms for assembly under his name, at his risk and his account to Austria.
Since the installation of this supply took place in Austria, the supply of wind farms is taxable in Austria.
– Because the carrier was instructed by the Danish entrepreneur (eDK), and transport took place under his name, at his own risk and on his own account, the supply of the German subcontractor (eD) took place there, where transport began – in GERMANY.
Although wind power plants have been dispatched to another member state and the recipient is a registered payer of another member state, the supply of the German subcontractor (eD) could not obtain an exemption from the tax because a different member state of destination differs from another member state of the Czech society.
This delivery is therefore properly taxed in GERMANY and the Czech company (eCZ) deducted input tax in their tax returns.
The place of delivery of the Czech company (eCR) is also determined by the beginning of the shipment.
Transport of some wind farms was started in the Czech Republic and others in Germany.
- The supply of those wind farms that are produced in the Czech Republic took place in the Czech Republic.
- The supply of other wind farms which are produced in Germany took place in Germany.
So the Czech company (eCR) carried out both intracommunitary delivery from the Czech Republic to Austria and intracommunitary delivery from Germany to Austria.
BRH found that the Czech company (eCR) did not report in his tax returns for VAT in GERMANY no intracommunity acquisition hasn't even HKE the German DUTY.
So it is possible that the Czech company has declared all intracommunitary deliveries uniformly as intracommunitary deliveries from the Czech Republic.
The Sao found that (eCR) reported no intracommunitary delivery to Austria but intracommunitary delivery to Denmark.
Examination of the taxation of intrakomunitárního acquisition in Austria would require the cooperation of at least four tax administrations (the austrian, the Czech, Danish and German), although this case does not show any sign of tax fraud or evasion.
Further, the SAO and BRH examine the transactions in order to highlight the differences between declaring in a tax return and data from the VIES, which were caused by the different legal treatment of VAT in 2004.
Controlled cases also demonstrate that changes in the legislation need time to apply the new legislation into practice by both payers and tax authorities:
22. In SH for II. until IV. quarter 2004 the Czech payer reported an intracommunitary delivery to the German payer totalling CZK 792 977 452 (EUR 25 197 885).
Over the same period, another Czech payer reported an intracommunity delivery to another German payer totalling CZK 18,157,265 (EUR 576,970).
According to the information provided by the Sao from the BRH, in both cases it was the supply of electricity.
Both Czech payers indicated the above-mentioned supply in SH in accordance with the text of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., valid in 2004.
Further examination of the aforementioned transactions, the Sao group found that in 2004 there were differences between the Czech Republic and Germany in the statutory regulation of supply or acquisition of electricity.
While in the Czech Republic the payers reported electricity supply in accordance with the applicable text of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. as the intracommunity supply of goods, from the point of view of the German legal regulations valid in 2004, this was not an intracommunity acquisition, but a taxable supply with the place of implementation implementation on the territory of the federal republic of GERMANY.
The difference in legal regulations was eliminated in the Czech Republic by the adoption of Act No. 635/2004 Coll. amending certain laws in connection with the adoption of the law on administrative fees, effective from 1. 1. 2005.
23. In addition, when examining selected intracommunitary transactions in cooperation with BRH, it was found that the Czech payer reported in SH for 1. up to 4. quarter 2005 intracommunity delivery to the German payer totalling CZK 240 411 163 (EUR 8 071 823) and other Czech payer reported in SH for the same period intracommunity delivery to the German payer totalling CZK 263 470 776 (EUR 8 846 050).
According to the information provided by the Sao from the BRH, in both cases it was the supply of electricity.
According to the text of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. effective from 1. 1. 2005 is in the case of the supply of electricity to the place of performance the place where the customer has its seat, place of business or has an establishment for which the goods are delivered.
Therefore, Czech payers should not have provided electricity to SH in 2005.
By reporting intracommunitary electricity supply in SH, the two above-mentioned payers distorted the VIES data by a total of CZK 503 881 939 (EUR 16 917 873).
Conclusion
Cooperation has met the objectives of the BRH and the Sao.
Both SAI have acquired a deeper knowledge of VAT management systems in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The cooperation revealed the differences between the two systems and showed that VAT governance legislation differs.
During parallel checks, suspicious cases of intracommunitary transactions were detected.
Some of them make sense to check subsequently.
Based on the audit findings, both SAI made recommendations on VAT management.
Monitoring these recommendations should also be part of the follow-up.
New experience and knowledge through cooperation between the two audit institutions are the basis for the successful implementation of the following controls the administration of VAT.
Communique
Report has been drawn up in Czech, English and German language and signed by the president of the Supreme audit office, Czech republic and the president of the Bundesrechnungshofu, the Federal republic of Germany.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in excise control checks between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in 2006
Introductory word
Presented to the joint report informs of the progress and outcome of international cooperation in the parallel controls, which implement the Supreme audit office, Czech republic Najvyšší kontrolný úrad Slovenskej republiky, focused on the administration of excise taxes in the period after the entry of both countries into the European union.
The cooperation was implemented on the basis of a cooperation agreement in control activities concluded in February 2006.
The theme of the parallel controls were selected with respect to a fundamental change in the system of collection of excise taxes that occurred in connection with the inclusion of the Czech republic and the Slovak republic into the internal market of the European union from 1. May 2004.
The functioning of the internal market of the European Union requires the free movement of goods, including excise goods.
The basic principle is to allow the circulation of goods unburdened by tax up to the date of delivery for final consumption.
In accordance with this principle, the new legislation adopted in both countries allows the movement of goods under tax supervision under the conditional exemption regime.
The system places great demands on tax authorities and presupposes a close interaction between the competent administrations of the member states in the fight against tax fraud in this area.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in excise control checks for the period from 1. May 2004 to 31. December 2005 1.
Introduction
Control number: (ČR) 05/34 (SR) 48/11
Subject of inspection: (CR) Excise Tax Administration (SR) procedure of cobrné bodies in the management of consumption taxes
The supreme audit office, Czech republic (hereinafter the "NKU-CZ") and the Najvyšší kontrolný úrad Slovenskej republiky (hereinafter referred to as "SAO SR") has concluded on the 8th. February 2006 "contract of cooperation in control activities".
The subject of the contract was cooperation in parallel checks carried out "Excise Management", included in the Sao-CR's 2005 audit plan under no 05/34, and "control of the Cobra procedure in the management of consumption taxes", included in the Sao SR's 2006 audit plan under no 48/11.
Parallel controls had the character of a coordinated control.
The cooperation consisted in the exchange of information, which the contracting parties could not get in control of the administration of excise taxes on the territory of its state, and in the development of a common final report on the results of the checks within the meaning of the european implementing guidelines for implementation of the audit standards INTOSAI - directive no 31.
On the territory of the Czech republic's control (hereinafter referred to as "CR") implement the group controlling department of the state budget and from territorial departments of the central Bohemia, south bohemia, west Bohemia, north-west Bohemia north-east Bohemia, south Moravia, central Moravia and north Moravia in the period from 7. February to 2. June 2006.
27 inspectors were involved in the inspection.
The audited persons were the Directorate-General of Customs (hereinafter referred to as DGC) and 11 tax authorities.
Within the DG, 12 selected customs offices were inspected out of a total of 54.
Control on the territory of the Slovak republic (hereinafter "SR") conducted by the section of financial and tax the SAO SR, in cooperation with the expoziturami the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice on the 5 customs offices from a total of 9 in the period from 13. February to 2. June 2006.
8 inspectors were involved in the inspection.
The aim of the parallel checks was to examine the customs procedure for the administration of excise duties and compliance with the relevant legislation in force in both countries and the European Union.
The international cooperation was focused on the procedure of the administrators of taxes in the exercise of supervision of the transport of the goods subject to consumption taxes, in particular on the registration of launched and completed transport in the regime of conditional exemption from tax, and the exchange of information within the framework of mutual administrative assistance between the administrators of the excise taxes the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA.
2. Excise tax administration
Excise duties were administered in the Czech Republic until 31. December 2003 financial authorities.
From 1. in January 2004, this agenda was taken over by the customs authorities, which have so far levied excise duty only on imports.
Excise duty is subject to mineral oils, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products and tobacco products in the Czech Republic.
The income of the state budget from excise taxes in the Czech Republic was CZK 82.8 billion in 2004 and the revenue of the state budget from taxes and fees of CZK 424.7 billion was 19.5 %.
In 2005, the income of the state budget from excise taxes 103,6 billion Czk and the share on the revenue of the state budget from taxes and fees in the amount of $ 460.4 billion Czk was of 22.5 %.
In 2004, the revenue from excise duty on mineral oils to the state budget 80% of the total revenue from this tax, and in 2005 accounted for 90.9 %.
The difference against 100% of CZK 13 billion in 2004 and CZK 6.9 billion in 2005 was the income of the state fund for transport infrastructure.
The administration of all excise duties in the SR shall be carried out by the customs authorities from 1. May 2004, with the exception of the excise duty on mineral oil which they have been administering since 1. 1, 2002.
Until then, the excise administration was carried out by the tax authorities.
Excise duty in SR is subject to mineral oil, alcohol, beer, wine and tobacco products.
The state budget's revenue from excise duties in the SR was a total of Sk 43.4 billion in 2004 and the total tax revenue of Sk 209.5 billion was 20.7 %.
In 2005, the state budget revenue from excise taxes was Sk. 50 billion, and in total tax revenues of Sk. 222.6 billion, excise taxes accounted for 22.5 %.
Chart No. 1-Comparison of revenues of the state budget of the Czech Republic from taxes and fees and tax revenues of the state budget of the SR with excise income
The legislation in both countries is based on European union regulations governing this area, in particular: - Council directive 92/12/EEC on the general arrangements, holding, movement and monitoring of products subject to excise duty (hereinafter "the directive 92/12/EEC"), - Council regulation (EC) no 2073/2004 on administrative cooperation in the field of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as "regulation no 2073/2004"), - Commission regulation (EEC) no 2719/92 on the accompanying administrative document for the movement of excisable products under a duty suspension arrangement from the excise tax (hereinafter referred to as "regulation no 2719/92"), - Commission regulation (EEC) no 3649/92 on a simplified accompanying document for the movement of products subject to excise duty which have been released for consumption in the member state of dispatch, within the Community (hereinafter "regulation no 3649/92").
The basic legislation regulating excise duties in the Czech Republic is Act No. 353/2003 Coll. on excise duties, as amended ,( hereinafter referred to as " Act no 353/2003 Coll.“ ) effective from 1. January 2004.
In the administration of excise duties in the SR, the customs authorities are bound, inter alia, by the following generally binding legislation: - law no 98/2004 Z. z. about the consumption tax on mineral oil in the neskorí predpisov act (hereinafter referred to as " law no 98/2004 Z. z."),- law no 104/2004 Z. z. on the consumption tax on wine in the name of neskorí predpisov (hereinafter referred to as "law no 104/2004 Z. z."),- law no 105/2004 Z. z. on the consumption tax of Lieh in the neskorí predpisov act (hereinafter referred to as "law no 105/2004 Z. z."),- law no 106/2004 Z. z. on the consumption tax on Tabak products in the name of neskorší predpisov (hereinafter referred to as "law no 106/2004 Z. z."),- law no 107/2004 Z. z. about the consumption tax on beer in the neskorší predpisov act (hereinafter referred to as "law no 107/2004 Z. z.“).
2.1. movement of excise goods under a conditional exemption scheme between member states of the European Union
Directive 92/12/EEC of Title III provides for the movement of goods subject to excise duty under the conditional exemption scheme. 15 to 20.
According to these provisions may transport such goods to implement only the authorised warehouse keeper, which means the natural or legal person authorized by the competent authorities of a member state to produce, process, hold, receive and dispatch products subject to excise duty.
The recipient in another member state may be authorised warehouse keeper or trader without authorized warehousekeeper status, who must not, however, these products in the regime of conditional exemption to store or further transmit.
The authorized warehousekeeper of dispatch in the CZECH republic and in SLOVAKIA means the operator of the tax warehouse, the operator is the authorized recipient for repeated or one-off acceptance of products subject to excise duty.
The transport of excise products under the conditional exemption scheme is only possible under Directive 92/12/EEC with an accompanying document.
The accompanying document shall be issued by the sender before starting the transport in quadruplicate, if the competent authorities of the member state of dispatch shall not require another copy.
2.2. procedure for commencing and terminating the transport of goods under the conditional exemption scheme between the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic
Transport from the Czech Republic
The procedure for commencing transport is governed by the provisions of § 25 para. 3 of Act no 353/2003 Coll. where, inter alia, is indicated:
"The operator of a tax warehouse is obliged before the start of transport of selected products to notify the customs office which is the digit the competent tax warehouse from which the service started;
the transport of selected products may be initiated only with the consent of this customs office.
The customs office shall issue a consent with transport of selected products without delay after the condition is met, the reinsurance tax...“
The consignor in the Czech Republic may start the transport of all types of excise products only with the consent of the local customs office.
The customs authority shall issue the consent to the commencement of transportation only in case, if a collateral tax in the amount of tax attributable to the conveyed products.
The consignor is obliged to make an accompanying document in five copies before the commencement of transport.
The customs office shall indicate the consent to the commencement of transport on the accompanying document.
Copy no 1 shall be kept by the consignor, copy no 2, 3, and 4 shall surrender the consignor to the carrier and copy no 5 shall be retained by the customs office of the authorising transport.
According to Slovak legislation, the consignee in the SR shall retain copy No 2 of the accompanying document. Copies 3 and 4 shall confirm the receipt of the products and submit both copies to the local customs office.
Copy No 3 certified by the customs office shall be sent to the consignor no later than 15. the day of the month following the calendar month in which he accepted the products.
Copy No 4 shall be retained by the customs office of the consignee.
Transportation is terminated by the receipt of products by the recipient.
The release of collateral tax decides the customs office in the CZECH republic, that the initiation of transport has authorised, within 5 working days after the presentation of copy no 3 of the accompanying document, which is confirmed by the beneficiary and the Slovak customs authority.
Graph 2 - circulation of the accompanying document for Transport initiated in the Czech Republic and completed in the Czech Republic
Transport from SR
The procedure for transport of alcohol and tobacco products from SLOVAKIA to another member state of the European union was 31. December 2005 adapted as follows:
According to the provisions of § 26 para. 4 of law no 105/2004 Z. z.
"When the town liehu from a tax warehouse on the daňovom territory to a tax warehouse or legitimate príjemcovi, or tax splnomocnencovi in inom členskom štáte is odosielatel' (dodávatel') mandatory in the day začatia prepravy zaslať kópiu first dielu sprievodného document electronically or faxom Colnému office Poprad; this kópiu is mandatory zaslať aj colnému office písomne to piatich pracovných days odo of the day začatia prepravy.“
According to the provisions of § 22 para. 4 of law no 106/2004 Z. z.
"When the town tabakových výrobkov from a tax warehouse on the daňovom territory to a tax warehouse or oprávnenému príjemcovi, or tax splnomocnencovi in inom členskom štáte is odosielatel' (dodávatel') mandatory in the day začatia prepravy zaslať kópiu first dielu sprievodného document electronically or faxom Colnému office Poprad; this kópiu is mandatory zaslať aj colnému office písomne najneskor to piatich pracovných days odo of the day začatia prepravy.“
For the transport of other excise products (mineral oil, wine and beer) in the period from 1. May 2004 to 31. December 2005 (hereinafter referred to as "controlled period") the taxpayer had an obligation to notify the Customs office Poprad, respectively. the competent customs office of the initiation of the transport in the regime of conditional exemption from tax.
The transport of these products to the tax administrator until he found out when a local investigation or a tax inspection of the accompanying documents and of the accounting documents of the tax body.
The consignor in the SR is obliged to make an accompanying document in four copies before the commencement of transport.
Copy no 1 shall be kept by the consignor (for transport of alcohol and tobacco products shall send a copy of copy no 1 of the electronically or by fax to the Customs office Poprad and the competent customs office).
Copies 2, 3 and 4 shall accompany the goods transported.
According to the Czech legislation, the consignee in the Czech Republic retains copy No. 2 of the accompanying document issued by the consignor in the SR and confirms receipt of the products on copies No. 3 and 4.
Certified copies No 3 and 4 shall be sent no later than the first working day after the end of transport to the local customs office in the Czech Republic.
The customs office shall retain copy No 4 and copy No 3 on which it shall verify the accuracy and validity shall be returned to the consignee.
The consignee shall send a certified copy No 3 no later than the next working day after receipt of the copy to the consignor to the SR.
Transport in the SR shall be deemed to have ceased on the date of receipt of the products by the consignee.
The service shows the sender, by production of copy no 3 of the accompanying document certified by the beneficiary and the tax administrator in the CR.
Graph 3 — the Circulation of the movement document during transport (alcohol and tobacco), launched in SLOVAKIA and finished in the CZECH republic
In 2006 there were in SLOVAKIA gradually adopted the amendment to all the laws of excise, according to which the consignor of goods in the regime of conditional exemption from tax is obliged before the start of transportation send a copy of copy no 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office locally competent to the sender.
Document evidencing the termination of the transport of alcohol and tobacco products is copy no 3 of the accompanying document certified by the beneficiary and its competent tax administrator.
A document demonstrating the cessation of transport of mineral oils, wine and beer shall be copy No 3 as confirmed by the consignee.
Confirmation of the tax administrator of another member state on the taking over of the goods by the recipient is required, if this administrator is obliged according to the legislation of the competent member state to confirm the copy no 3 of the accompanying document.
2.3. registration of traffic opened and completed by the customs authorities in the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic
A single electronic system is not in place to monitor the transport of goods under the conditional exemption scheme between the member states of the European Union.
Decision 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16. June 2003, establishing an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of excise products, requires the member states and the European Commission to introduce from 1. July 2009 an electronic system (Excise Movement and Control System), which would allow the administrators of the excise taxes in the various member states to obtain information on the carriage of goods in real time.
The system will allow electronic transmission of the accompanying documents, which are currently used only in paper form, and will contribute to reduced to tropes of the movement of goods in the regime of conditional exemption from taxes and to secure more effective control of the movement of tax-free products within all member states.
This system will include national databases of national transport systems.
The customs administration of the Czech Republic Records all traffic initiated and completed in the Czech Republic in the module of registration of selected products (hereinafter referred to as "EVV").
All customs authorities in the Czech Republic have online access to the system.
In the case of transport implemented only on the territory of the CZECH republic may tax get information on starting or stopping of traffic immediately after the registration of the accompanying document to the customs office to EVV.
The customs authority will release the collateral tax on the shipped products provided by the sender at the time of registration of the termination of transport to the customs authority locally competent beneficiaries.
The customs authorities in SR use a database based on the SysNed application software, which ensures the automation of their excise management activities and communication with European Union systems.
By registering a tax warehouse, operator of the tax warehouse or authorized recipient in the application software SysNed this information is automatically transferred to the database "System for Exchange of Excise Data" (hereinafter referred to as the "SEED").
3. Preparation and course of cooperation
The first coordination meeting of representatives of the Sao-CR and representatives of the Sao-SR, which discussed the specific procedure for cooperation in the implementation of parallel controls in the field of excise duties, took place in January 2006.
Both parties have become familiar with excise legislation and with the organization of Excise Management in both states.
Special attention was paid to the procedure of the customs authorities of the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA during the authorisation process, or during start-up and shut-down of transport, products subject to excise duties in the regime of conditional exemption from tax and exchange of information between the administrators of the excise taxes of the two countries.
At the meeting it was agreed that the Czech and the Slovak side of the: - process the total data on the quantity of excisable products being transported from the CZECH republic to SLOVAKIA and vice versa, whose transport was initiated in the audited period, - comparing the data on the dopravách mineral oils - combined nomenclature code 2710 and 2711, and alcohol - combined nomenclature code 2207 and 2208 in the regime of conditional exemption from the levy initiated in the CZECH republic and completed in the SR and on the contrary, in the months of November 2004 and September 2005.
During the inspections, the period under review was extended by October and November 2005, and the transport of tobacco products under the conditional exemption scheme was also subject to scrutiny during those months.
Tables 1 and 2 show the total quantity of excise products transported under the conditional exemption scheme between Czech and Slovak tax entities during the period under review.
4. Comparison of registers of transport goods under the conditional exemption scheme
The Sao-CR forwarded to the Slovak side a database of transport operations in the Czech Republic containing a total of 5,876 items on accompanying documents, of which 5,738 items were mineral oils, 134 items alcohol and 4 items of tobacco products.
The Sao SR forwarded to the Czech party a database of carriers in the SR containing a total of 3,319 items on accompanying documents, of which 696 items related to mineral oil, 2,066 items of alcohol and 557 items of tobacco products.
The Sao-Czech Republic compared the data on the transport registered in the Czech Republic with the data on the completed transport registered in the Czech Republic.
The results of the comparison are presented in Table 3.
The transport data for November 2004 and September 2005 compared the Sao - Czech Republic with the database of the Slovak Customs Administration, which was transmitted to him by the Sao SR at the beginning of the inspection.
The database did not contain data allowing to reliably reconcile individual transport, and therefore managed to assign only 63 % started right.
Individual transport was assigned according to multiple data, e.g. sender, consignee, date of transport, quantity of products transported.
Data on dopravách launched in the CZECH republic and completed in the SR in the months of October and November of 2005 compared to SAO-CR with the database of the Slovak customs administration, which contained all the data according to the accompanying documents, on the basis of which managed to clearly assign 93% of the initiated transport.
In the database of Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, data on the amount of mineral oils were presented in liters or tonnes depending on the type of mineral oil.
The amount of alcohol was in most cases stated in litres, which, however, was possible on the basis of the database referred to the percentage of alcohol converted into litres of absolute alcohol.
The quantity of tobacco products was indicated in pieces, in thousands of pieces and kilograms by type of tobacco products.
The transport started in the CZECH republic, the termination of which is in the Slovak database has failed to reliably verify or for which yielded an indication of the transported quantity of the products was carried out inspection of the accompanying documents.
Accompanying documents on 487 transports of alcohol, mineral oils and tobacco products were inspected.
The inspection of these documents was carried out at the customs offices at which the Sao-Czech Republic carried out the inspection.
For Transport authorised by other customs authorities, accompanying documents were requested through the DGC.
The Czech party asked the Slovak party to verify the implementation of 141 transportation, to which the customs authorities in the CZECH republic did not substantiate the endorsed copy no 3 of the accompanying document, as appropriate disagree number of products listed on the accompanying document with the amount of products listed in the database.
In addition, Transport data registered in the Slovak database was forwarded to the Slovak party, which was not included in the Transport database of the Czech customs administration.
The Sao SR tracked 95 traffic in the database of the Slovak customs administration.
The remaining 46 carriers were verified by the local customs authorities, who proved their termination with copies of accompanying documents.
The Slovak party forwarded the Czech side of the copy of the accompanying documents, on the basis of which the transport identified in the Czech database, with the exception of transportation implemented two Czech tax entities, which in the Czech database initiated by transport were not found.
The examination of these cases was found:
- in the Slovak database of transport was registered 11 transport of ethyl alcohol in the total amount 276,7 liters of alcohol implemented by the Czech tax entity in 2004, and 20 transportation of alcohol in the total amount of 404,66 liters of alcohol implemented in 2005.
The Sao-CR found that this was a transport of taxed products, for the initiation of which the sender does not need the consent of the tax administrator.
The sender informed the tax administrator in writing of the commencement of transport. He carried out the transport on the basis of accompanying documents, which serve for the transport of products under the conditional exemption scheme;
- in the Slovak database of transport were registered a total of 94 transportation of mineral oil, combined nomenclature code 2710 11 21, in a total volume of 173 thousand liters implemented by the Czech tax entity in the period September 2004 to December 2005.
The Sao-CR found that between May 2004 and June 2005 the tax entity carried out transport of 102 thousand litres of non-taxable mineral oils without proper authorisation.
The taxpayer was the holder of a special permit to receive and use products which are exempt, on the basis of which he could tax-free products only deliver to the holder the same permit.
The commencement of transport to the customs office in the Czech Republic did not notify and did not provide tax collateral for the products transported amounting to CZK 1,207,680.
Between July 2005 and December 2005, the tax entity transported 71 thousand litres of taxed mineral oils to the territory of the SR. Even in those cases, he did not comply with the legal obligation by not notifying the customs office of the commencement of transport.
Transportation of the products put into free tax circulation in the tax territory of the CZECH republic to another member state, the consignor may in the CZECH republic to initiate without the consent of the customs office, however, is required before the start of transport of this fact in writing notify the customs office.
Tax entity collecting the products released into free tax circulation in another member state is obliged, before removing to report the amount of and ensure the tax.
Products can be transported only with a simplified accompanying document, the requirements of regulation no 3649/92.
This regulation allows also the use of the accompanying document for transport in the regime of conditional exemption from tax, on which, however, must be clearly stamped that this is a "simplified accompanying document for the purposes of tax control (products subject to excise duty)".
The same legislation shipping and receiving of products put into free tax circulation in another member state is valid also in SR.
In those cases, the tax authorities transported the products put into free circulation with an accompanying document for transport under a conditional exemption scheme of which 3. and 4. the copy of the recipient was submitted to the tax administrator in SR for verification.
The customs authorities of the SR registered these services in the database of services under the conditional exemption procedure, since the accompanying documents did not indicate that they were a simplified accompanying document.
Sao SR compared the database of the Czech customs administration with the database of the Slovak customs administration and found:
- in the databases was the amount of transported products reported inconsistently, e.g., mineral oil was given in litres, hectolitres or in kilograms; alcohol was given in litres or litres of alcohol, which was made difficult by the comparison of the transported amount of goods,
- the quantity of alcohol shipped in the invoices did not coincide with the quantity recorded in the databases,
- not all related invoices were listed in the databases,
- in the database of the Slovak customs administration have been registered two transport alcohol from the CZECH republic to the SR implemented in November 2004 in a total volume of 47 237 liters of alcohol that is in the database of the Czech customs administration were not.
The Slovak party submitted copies of accompanying documents to the Czech party.
5. International exchange of information between customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic
The conditions for cooperation between the administrative authorities of the member states responsible for the administration of excise duties were regulated up to 30. June 2005 Council directive 77/799/EEC concerning mutual assistance by the competent authorities of the member states in the field of direct taxation, certain excise duties and taxation of insurance premiums.
1. July 2005 entry into force of regulation no 2073/2004, which lays down rules and procedures enabling the competent authorities of the member states of the European union cooperation and the exchange of information necessary for a correct assessment of excise taxes.
