Each member state shall designate a central liaison office, which secures contacts with other member states in the field of administration of excise duties and is responsible for the exchange of information about the movement of excise goods.
In the Czech Republic, to ensure the exchange of information on excise duties between the member states of the European Union, the "Excise Liaison Office" (hereinafter referred to as "ELO Czech Republic") was set up for DGC.
Security tasks related to the management systems to control the movement of goods subject to excise duties (SEED, MVS, EWSE) and the exchange of information within the framework of mutual administrative assistance between the member states of the European union and SLOVAKIA he performed with the effect from 1. May 2004 the Office of ELO at the Customs Office of Poprad.
Effective from 1. July 2005 the duties of the Elo office shall be carried out by the Department of Elo (located in Poprad) of the Excise Department of the Customs Directorate of the SR (hereinafter referred to as "ELO SR").
According to the provisions of Article 3 (3), 3 of regulation no 2073/2004 the central liaison office shall be responsible in particular for - the exchange of data held in the electronic register of the SEED, - a system of early warning "Early Warning System Excision" (hereinafter referred to as "EWSE"), - request for verification the movement of goods subject to excise duty dispatched to other member states or from them received "Movement Verification System" (hereinafter "MVS").
The content, scope and functions of SEED, EWSE and MVS systems are regulated in articles 22, 23 and 24 of regulation no 2073/2004.
SEED-a system for the exchange of information on tax entities trading in excise goods.
The system is made up of national registers of payers of excise tax and allows the tax authorities on the territory of the European union to find out whether the products subject to excise duty traded person authorized.
Each National Register shall be made available to the competent authorities of the other member states only for excise purposes.
The central contact authority of each member state ensures that the people involved in the movement of excise goods on the territory of the European union can obtain confirmation of the information held in this database.
In accordance with § 41 of law no 98/2004 Z. z., with § 39 of law no 104/2004 Z. z., with § 46 of Law No. 105/2004 Z. z., with Section 40 of Law No. 106/2004 Z. z. and with Section 39 of Law No. 107/2004 Z. z. ELO SR maintains an electronic database containing a register of tax warehouse operators, beneficiaries and tax warehouses - SEED database.
The customs authorities in the SR contribute to the database of SEED by registering a tax warehouse, operator of the tax warehouse or authorized recipient in the application software SysNed, which is automatically linked with the ELO SR.
For example, if a new tax warehouse operator, beneficiary or tax warehouse is registered in the sysned database, the related data is automatically transferred to the SEED database.
The SAO SR found that the exchange of databases the SEED between the customs administration of the SR and the Customs administration of the CZECH republic is carried out in a controlled period usually once a month, rarely more than once a month.
The customs administration of SR accepted 22 SEED files and sent 25 SEED files.
Data to the SEED database in the Czech Republic are transmitted from the National Register, which records all persons authorized to dispose of excise products and issued permits to dispose of such products.
Individual customs offices in the Czech Republic do not have access to the International SEED database.
Requests from customs authorities to provide information from the SEED database of other member states are obtained only through ELO CR.
EWSE - an early warning system aimed at controlling the transport of excise goods through which the carriage of risky consignments is notified.
For the risk package is considered to be both the transport of certain products subject to excise duty in quantities exceeding the limits set by regulation of the European commission, and, secondly, to the right, you like the risk, evaluate the tax administrator.
The exchange of information is realized in two forms:
- information-is sent when the limits set are exceeded,
- warning message-to be sent if the transport of goods is assessed as risky.
When evaluating the degree of risk of a consignment, ELO SR uses the SEED database for sending the warning message, which checks the data specified in the accompanying document.
In the event that in the database the SEED does not agree data with the data in the supporting document (for example, opposed the registration number of the recipient of the goods or address of the recipient), ELO SR will draw up a warning message that it sends to the office of ELO member state of the recipient of the goods.
ELO shall be governed by the regulations of the commission for the tax and Customs Area CED 317 and Ced 457, which, inter alia, determine the type and quantity of goods in the relevant units of measurement for the preparation of informative and warning reports.
In the controlled period, ELO SR sent one warning message to the Czech Republic.
In the Czech Republic, information on commenced transport of products in quantities exceeding the specified limits is automatically generated when entering data from the accompanying document into the database when approving transport.
Re-evaluate if the tax administrator in the CR on the basis of its own analysis of the parcel as a risk, treated a so-called warning message, which through the ELO of the CZECH republic shall send to the responsible member state.
In 2005, ELO cr sent two warning messages to ELO sr.
MVS - system controls movement of the goods - allows, through the application of MVS to control the individual transport of products subject to excise duty and control of the established routes of transport between the entities referred to in the accompanying document.
The exchange of information takes place on the basis of a request in which the Elo of the sending country specifies its requirements.
The system is used in particular in cases where the sender takes over the confirmed copy no 3 of the accompanying document and requires e.g. a refund of excise taxes, and in cases where the data referred to in the accompanying document cannot be checked in the international database of SEED.
In the audited period ELO SR sent 33 requests to the CR.
ELO CR sent 25 requests to the MVS to ELO SR.
The customs authorities in the CZECH republic the most commonly examined the data referred to in the accompanying documents, in particular the amount received, or sent products or whether the sender of the products referred to in the accompanying document is entitled to dispose of the products subject to excise duty, if this fact could not be verified in the international database of SEED.
Applications received by MVS in both countries have been forwarded to customs offices locally responsible for the consignees or consignors of excise products.
The customs authorities examined the data requested and notified the result of the investigation via ELO to the other member state.
6. Summary
The cooperation of the SAO, the CZECH republic and the SAO SR to compare the basic legal regulations governing the area of consumption taxes in both states, the procedure of the customs authorities of the CZECH republic and SLOVAKIA in the initiation and termination of transport of the products in the regime of conditional exemption from tax between the two states, the registration of such transport and further to compare the exchange of information between customs authorities in the framework of international cooperation.
6.1 comparing the legislation governing excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic, differences were identified:
(A) in the procedure of tax entities and tax administrators when commencing the transport of products under a conditional exemption scheme.
Transportation of the products in the regime of conditional exemption from tax can tax entity in the CZECH republic start only with the consent of the tax administrator that the initiation of transportation shall, under the conditions that the shipped products protection was provided taxes in the amount of tax on them attributable.
The commencement of the transport of products under the conditional exemption scheme in the SR is not subject to the authorization of the tax administrator.
During the controlled period, the tax entity was obliged to notify the tax authority of the start of transport of alcohol and tobacco products.
The transport of mineral oils, beer and wine could commence without informing the tax administrator of this fact.
In 2006 there were in SLOVAKIA gradually adopted the amendment to all the laws of excise, according to which the consignor of goods in the regime of conditional exemption from tax is obliged before the start of transportation send a copy of copy no 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs authority that is locally competent to the sender;
(B) within the time limits for dispatch of copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
The consignee in the Czech Republic is obliged not later than the next working day after the end of transport to send copies No 3 and 4 of the accompanying document to the tax administrator for verification.
Certified copy No 3 shall be sent to the consignor no later than the following working day after receipt of it from the tax administrator.
The consignee in the SR is obliged to send to the consignor of the products copy No 3, confirmed by the tax administrator and the consignee of the products no later than 15. the day of the month following the month in which he accepted the goods.
6.2. Customs authorities in the SR and in the Czech Republic keep electronic records of transport products under a conditional exemption procedure.
The content and manner of keeping this register is not regulated in the Czech Republic or in the Czech Republic.
Customs authorities in both countries enter in the register all data from accompanying documents on the basis of which transport is carried out.
For monitoring the transport of goods in the regime of conditional exemption from tax between the member states of the European union there is currently no single electronic system that would allow administrators to excise duties in individual member states to obtain information on the carriage of goods in real time.
Pursuant to decision 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16. June 2003 is from 1. July 2009 foresees the introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the transport of excise products.
On the basis of the cooperation agreement in the control activity, the Czech party transmitted to the Slovak party a database of transport products under the conditional exemption scheme initiated in the Czech Republic and completed in the Czech Republic.
The database contained 5,876 items related to transported mineral oils, alcohol and tobacco products.
The Slovak party transmitted to the Czech party a database of transport products under the conditional exemption scheme started in the Czech Republic and ended in the Czech Republic.
The database contained 3,319 items related to transported mineral oils, alcohol and tobacco products.
The Czech side compared the data on the transport registered in the Czech Republic with the registration of the traffic completed in the Czech Republic.
The Slovak party compared the data on the transport of goods under the conditional exemption scheme started in the Czech Republic and ended in the Czech Republic.
The comparison of data was made difficult by the fact that the quantity of goods transported was not reported uniformly in the databases.
In cases where it was not possible to clearly assign the data on the individual dopravách in both registers, inspection of the accompanying documents and violation of the regime of conditional exemption from tax, no cases of tax evasion have been identified.
On the basis of the findings of parallel checks, it can be concluded that member states can obtain valuable information from the transport register to improve the quality of Excise Management.
Establishment of an electronic system for the movement and control of excisable goods within the meaning of the decision of the European parliament and of the Council no. 1152/2003/EC will enable the electronic transmission of the accompanying document and a more efficient control of the movement in the regime of conditional exemption from tax on the territory of the European union.
Communique
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak languages.
The report was signed by the president of the highest Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the president of the highest Audit Office, Czech Republic.
Administration of Value Added Tax in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Report on the results of the follow-up
Introductory word
Taxes generally represent a key source of public revenue.
It goes without saying that Supreme Audit Institutions (Sai) should focus their attention on this area.
An example is value added tax fraud ("VAT").
In their case, a loss of EUR 100 billion is estimated annually in the European Union (also "EU").
Already in 2005, participants VI. the EUROSAI Congress in Bonn agreed on the need for very close cooperation.
As part of this cooperation, SAI can exchange control procedures, find the best solution, etc.
VAT is a very suitable area for control cooperation as it is the only tax harmonised within the EU.
The supreme audit office of the Czech republic (hereinafter the "SAO") and the Federal court of auditors (Bundesrechnungshof, as well as "BRH") implemented the first parallel control action in the field of VAT in 2006.
The relevant report was published in 2008.
Because fraudulent conduct related to VAT not confined to a single country, but is widespread throughout the EU, close cooperation is required between the SAI to the security of a comprehensive evaluation of the steps taken to solve this problem.
The two SAI therefore decided to further develop cooperation in this area and carried out a subsequent parallel check.
1. Introduction
Control number: (CZ) 09/11 (d) VIII 2 - 2009 - 0892
Subject of inspection: (CZ) administration of Value Added Tax (D) bilateral audit with Sao (follow-up)
Objective of control:
(CZ) the Aim of the audit was to examine the procedure of the financial authorities in the administration of VAT, in particular to verify the procedure for the solution of selected cases of business transactions between the Czech republic and the Federal republic of Germany (hereinafter "Germany"), and to examine the procedures of the tax administrations of the two countries in the framework of international cooperation.
(D) the Audit was designed to evaluate the measures adopted by the tax administration to implement the recommendations issued by the SAO and BRH.
It was also intended to cover other VAT-related areas.
The resulting Control findings were intended to be compared with the established best practice (if any).
The period under review was 2006 to 2008 and, in the case of factual context, the period preceding and subsequent, until the end of the control.
2. Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
Subsequent control of VAT management in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of an agreement between the two SAI.
In the course of previous parallel checks, suspicious cases of intracommunitary transactions were detected.
Some of them required further vetting.
Based on the control findings, both SAI formulated recommendations on VAT management.
Carried out follow-up actions used to evaluate the measures taken in response to these recommendations and to examine the selected suspicious cases.
The inspection also focused e.g. on selected cases of high-risk intrakomunitárních transactions, mutual assistance for the recovery of claims and the implementation of controls on VAT for large taxpayers.
In the control of VAT management in selected areas in both countries, the inspectors came up with the following Control findings:
1. Recommendations from previous inspection
* Recommendation 1: conditions for registration of payers should be harmonised within the EU
In previous parallel checks, comparisons of VAT registration systems in both countries were found to differ.
Since different registration methods cause problems, both SAI recommended harmonising the conditions for registration of payers within the EU.
This recommendation was presented at EU level.
A proposal for amendment of Council regulation (EC) no 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing regulation (EEC) no 218/92 (hereinafter referred to as "Council regulation (EC) no 1798/2003") demanded the expansion of existing databases within the EU, including the database of tax identification numbers of VAT payers.
It also amended common standards for registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
SAI expected that the EU member states agree on the appropriate standards that will support their decision as quickly as possible, to exclude unreliable traders from the VAT system.
However, the latest version of that document, agreed by the EU member states under ECOFIN, does not contain the issue already mentioned.
Both SAI regret that the idea of Common Minimum Standards has been abandoned.
However, they continue to regard this intention as a relevant tool for preventing fraud in the field of VAT.
* Recommendation 2: monthly reporting of summary reports
In the framework of international cooperation was in the previous control action recommended to all EU member states have imposed monthly deadline for the submission of summary reports and allow for the more timely examination of the values intrakomunitárních transactions.
Council directive 2008/117/EC amending directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion connected with intra-Community transactions, it shortens the period of time for which submitted a summary report on the implementation inside the EU, for one month.
In the Czech republic, this measure was implemented through the law on value added tax with effect from 1. January 2010, in Germany was implemented from 1. July 2010.
In Germany not the obligation to submit a recapitulative statement month introduced within a specified time limit in accordance with the applicable EU rules, while in the Czech republic, yes.
* Recommendation 3: Comparison of data in VAT returns and aggregate reports in Germany with a view to achieving greater reliability of data in VIEs and consideration of the interconnection of both VAT returns and aggregate reports
The German tax administration accepted the BRH recommendations and set up a working group to explore possible solutions.
Work is still ongoing and the BRH will closely monitor further developments.
• Recommendation 4: Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level On the basis of the results of the previous control actions with both SAI agreed that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by only one member state.
The successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system must be exchanged and implemented in individual EU member states.
If not, perpetrators of fraudulent activity, you will choose the member state with the weakest risk management system.
The review found that our two member states use different risk management systems that have their strengths and weaknesses.
In this area by the SAO control system EUROCANET, which allows the exchange of information within the EU, while the BRH is focused on the German participation in the so-called platform for risk management.
2. Follow-up of selected cases of intracommunitary transactions
In the course of the previous control actions have been jointly audited business transactions for which there were doubts about their implementation or discrepancies in the reporting of business transactions in tax returns or recapitulative statements payers of both countries.
Both SAI selected nine cases for follow-up control, which included intracommunitary movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany.
The checks carried out by the tax authorities of the countries concerned were not concluded at the date of completion of our previous joint control action.
Follow-up actions to verify that the majority of tax proceedings in connection with those selected cases of business transactions between payers from the Czech republic and Germany has been concluded and that the tax administration of the Czech republic or Germany has taken adequate measures (e.g. additional additional assessment of VAT or to prevent tax refund on entry).
3. Control of selected cases of risky intracommunitary transactions
High-risk cases of intracommunity transactions carried out by EU payers that were included in EUROCANET were selected for inspection.
EUROCANET is a tool for detecting risk tax payers within the EU.
Member states ' participation in this system shall be voluntary.
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has a passive status.
It is not satisfactory for an active participant in the system if some member states refuse active participation.
Due to the fact that the German tax administration involved in the exchange of data in the system EUROCANET, it was not possible to obtain any information about who the suppliers with a German VAT ID were identified as risk.
The SAO in the framework of the action control found as cases of ordinary business transactions, and cases with suspected involvement in a revolving transactions or fraud in respect of VAT.
Tax administrators have limited possibilities of controlling risk transactions, in particular as regards the so-called missing traders, while the mere physical scans of documents can hardly prove to the tax body of any fraudulent conduct.
A similar situation for tax authorities occurs when imports and exports to third countries are linked to intracommunitary carousel trades.
In such cases it would be appropriate to ensure greater mutual cooperation in customs and financial authorities with a view to identify the goods and discrepancies in the transport documents and also keep track of its physical movement within the EU towards the end consumer.
Germany, like some other countries, is hesitant to actively participate in EUROCANET because of the lack of a sufficient legal base.
In Germany, other tools are used to detect at-risk tax payers, which have so far proved successful for the German tax administration.
There is a need to communicate and exchange experience between EU member states in this area.
The EU Council reached political agreement on the proposal for a regulation amending Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003.
Its main innovation lies in the creation of the eurofisc network.
The experience gained so far in the use of EUROCANET should be the basis for the creation of this new VAT fraud network.
4. Mutual assistance in the recovery of claims
In the area of international recovery assistance to all EU member states governed by the same european legislation.
Therefore, the method of processing applications for international assistance in debt collection in the Czech Republic and Germany is identical.
The SAO and the BRH carried out a comparison of the statistics submitted by both member states to the European Commission for the years 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics did not coincide.
Both SAI deemed useful statistics again to discuss on the EU level in order to find a way to avoid ongoing incompatibilities.
Without this, the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, SAI agree in the opinion that reliable statistics should contain more information on VAT.
It would probably be useful for the Commission, on the basis of more detailed statistics, to draw up an analysis to help member states strengthen the effectiveness of combating VAT fraud.
In both SAI's view, this means helping member states with low enforcement success rates to raise the recovery rate to at least the EU average.
If a member state so wishes, the commission should take an active part in this process.
5. Control of large tax entities
The SAI analysed the legal situation regarding VAT control for large tax entities (also "VDS") in both countries.
In addition, in the form of a questionnaire, they collected information from tax authorities on areas that SAI considers essential for managing the issue.
The responses received clearly show that the situation in both countries is evolving differently.
The Czech Republic has a system based on a large amount of relevant data (e.g. information from tax controls, balance sheet data and profit and loss statements, etc.) to regulate the selection of risk-prone cases.
This ensures effective management and analysis of VAT control in general.
In 2012, it is planned to establish a specialized tax office for the administration of VDS.
In Germany, a similar system does not yet exist, which makes it difficult to manage and analyse VAT control in general.
Germany is so far more focused on the selection of individual relevant cases, in particular on the basis of data from tax returns to VAT and the recapitulative statement.
The analysis of these data is based on different risk management components that will be strengthened.
3. Course of control action
3.1 the course of the control action in the Czech Republic
The inspection was carried out between May 2009 and February 2010 by Department II. - by the Department of revenue of the state budget and territorial unions IX. Pilsen, X. České Budějovice, XIII. Brno and XV. Ostrava.
The persons controlled were: Ministry of Finance of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "Czech Ministry of Finance") and 25 financial authorities (hereinafter referred to as "FÚ"): Fú Brno II, Fú Brno III, Fú Brno IV, fú in Breclav, Fú in Domažlice, Fú in Hodonín, FÚ in Hradec Králové, Fú in Cheb, Fú in Jablonec over Nisa, Fú in Karlovy Vary, Fú in Kralupy Vltava, fú in kraslice, fú Ostrava I, fú Ostrava III, fú in písek, FÚ in Pilsen, Fú for Threshold 1, Fú for threshold 4, FÚ for threshold 8, FÚ in RAKOVNIK, Fú in Sokolov, Fú in Tábor, Fú in Vysoké Mýta, FÚ in Zlin and Fú in Žamberk.
The control conclusion of this control action was approved by the College of the Supreme Audit Office on 27. April 2010.
3.2 the course of the control action in Germany
The audit was conducted in the period from February 2009 to February 2010 the control unit for indirect taxes and staff designated regional audit offices in Berlin, Frankfurt and Munich.
After selecting a sample of cases, a number of Länder were notified of the mission of the control action.
In addition to interviews at the Federal ministry of finance held a control action in these federal countries: • Bavaria, • Hamburg, • Hesse, • North Rhine-Westphalia • Saxony.
Included were tax files of the following financial authorities: • Erlangen, Zentralfinanzamt München (Central financial office in Munich), Hof, Schwandorf, Regensburg, Weiden in der Oberpfalz, Grafenau; • Hamburg-Nord (Hamburg-nord), Hamburg-Hansa, Hamburg für Großunternehmen (Hamburg-VDS);
In addition, the negotiation with the tax authorities Mühlacker, Reutlingen, Starnberg, Verden, Erfurt, Leipzig, Halle-Süd (Halle-south) and with the financial directorates in Frankfurt / Main, Chemnitz and Münster.
The report on the audit findings was submitted to the Federal Ministry of Finance in April 2010.
3.3 cooperation between the two control institutions
In the preparation of parallel control actions in September 2008 a meeting was held of representatives of both audit institutions to discuss and determine the themes of control.
Finally, in December 2008, the top officials of both SAI signed a cooperation agreement on the implementation of parallel controls.
At a meeting in Bonn in June 2009, the inspection teams to inform each other of the initial results achieved during the preparation of the checks, discuss the possible audit approaches and agree together the next procedure.
The second meeting took place in Prague on 2 days. - 4. December 2009.
The control teams exchanged the findings together until then and agreed a timetable for compiling a joint report.
Both SAI in the implementation of parallel control actions to focus on: • subsequent verification of the implementation of the recommendations made in the previous report, • verification of selected cases intrakomunitárních transactions between taxpayers from the Czech republic and Germany, which have not been resolved during the previous parallel control, • verification of selected cases intrakomunitárních transactions between taxpayers from the Czech republic and Germany, which have been classified as cases with high risk, • control the procedure for tax administrations in the field of international aid in the recovery of accounts receivable VAT • tax audits of large companies.
The report on the results of the parallel control actions was prepared during the June 2010 workshop.
4. Control of VAT management in selected areas
4.1 evaluation of recommendations from the previous review
4.1.1 evaluation of recommendations in the Czech Republic
Recommendation 1
Conditions for registration of payers should be harmonised within the EU
Based on the results of the previous inspection action, the Sao recommended the modification of the conditions of registration for VAT and the introduction of a new rule for the cancellation of registration in the Czech Republic.
The revised conditions should allow for a more effective reduction of the risk of possible tax evasion for VAT collection.
In this context, it was found that the financial authorities in some cases did not use the right to cancel the registration for VAT payers who failed to meet the obligations arising from the act no. 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter referred to as the"VAT Act").
The amendment of the provision introducing the obligation of tax administrators to cancel VAT registration to payers when the VAT return is repeatedly filed has not yet been proposed by the Czech Ministry of Finance.
According to the law on VAT, the tax administrator can cancel the registration of the payer of the tax "ex officio" in cases, when: a) the payer did not materialize without notice due to the tax authorities for a period of twelve consecutive months of performance, b) the payer does not fulfill his obligations arising from this act, c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
In the previous control action, it was found that the applicable legislation allowed the mo for Threshold 1 to cancel the VAT registration at 31. in January of the following calendar year, so-called non-established payers who have not received any obligation to grant and pay tax during the current calendar year.
For Threshold 1, the Mo often did not revoke the VAT registration for these payers, since the relevant provision provided for an insufficient period for the cancellation of the registration.
This problem was eliminated by an amendment to the VAT Act with effect from 1. January 2009.
The tax administrator is entitled to cancel the registration of neusazeného tax payer in the case that the tax payer has not delivered in the previous calendar year any goods or services subject to tax or the goods or services are exempt from tax with right to deduct VAT.
Recommendation 2
Monthly reporting of summary reports
In the framework of international cooperation, the previous control action recommended that all EU states introduce a monthly deadline for submitting summary reports.
The Council Directive reduces the period for which intra-EU summary reports are submitted to one month. This measure was implemented in the Czech Republic through the VAT Act with effect from 1. January 2010.
The obligation to submit summary reports in electronic form is also newly established.
The aggregate report shall be submitted by the payer even if there are services for which the place of performance is determined in accordance with § 9 (2). 1 of the law on VAT, provided to another member state to a person registered for tax in another member state and if such services must declare and pay tax to their beneficiaries.
This obligation is based on council directive 2008/8/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC as regards the place of supply of services.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and aggregate reports with a view to achieving greater reliability of data in VIES this recommendation concerned the German tax administration.
The Czech administration carried out a comparison of the data about intrakomunitárních transactions reported in the VAT returns and recapitulative statements by Czech payers automatically in system ADIS.
Recommendation 4
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level
Proper collection of VAT is one of the prerequisites for the proper functioning of the EU internal market.
The fight against VAT fraud is therefore a priority area and has been given considerable attention in recent years.
The importance of this struggle is evidenced by, inter alia, the conclusions of a study published by the European commission in October 2009, in which the external evaluator tried to determine the difference between the authorized and actually collected amount of VAT in the EU-25 member states (hereinafter referred to as "EU-25") during the period 2000-2006.
Based on the analysis of the available data, the author of the analysis concluded that the estimated amount of losses from uncollected VAT for this period is in the 90 to 113 billion EUROS, with the average per year in the EU-25 picks 12% of the legitimate VAT.
For the Czech Republic, the VAT loss for 2006 was even estimated at 18%.
In the framework of international cooperation was in the previous control action noted that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by only one member state.
The successful criteria, components and approaches of this system must be shared and implemented in each EU member state.
As regards the risk management system, the SAO has carried out an audit of the EUROCANET system for the exchange of information in the EU.
Cases of risky intracommunity transactions carried out by EU taxpayers included in EUROCANET have been selected for inspection (see Chapter 4.3).
Objectives improve administrative cooperation and increase the efficiency of the fight against VAT fraud should also be achieved through the establishment of the EUROFISC network, which should improve the cooperation of the responsible authorities in a form allowing disclosure of fraud already in their bud.
This network should later become an important source of information in assessing the risks of intra-community transactions.
The ECOFIN Council approved the creation of the EUROFISC network as early as 7. October 200812 and at the same time set out the basic principles to be followed by this network.
Type of EUROFISC is already a functioning system for the fast and selective exchange of information EUROCANET, which was developed by the belgian tax administration, in cooperation with other member states and with the support of the European commission and OLAF.
The aim of this system is to detect risky business transactions and entities involved in organised VAT fraud.
4.1.2 evaluation of recommendations in Germany
The evaluation of the recommendations from the first report yielded the following findings:
Recommendation 1
Conditions for registration of payers should be harmonised within the EU
The German tax administration has established a well-functioning system of registration of tax payers, which is based on a detailed questionnaire.
The Federal Ministry of Finance notified the Commission of this scheme in October 2007.
Improvement of the system is carried out on an ongoing basis.
Data from the questionnaire are currently electronically processed and will subsequently be used for the survey as part of risk management already during registration.
The commission presented a proposal amending Council regulation (EC) no 1798/2003, which included common standards for the registration and deregistraci tax payers.
Member states requested further clarification and detailed elaboration of this issue.
BRH asked the Federal Ministry of finance to ensure the already reached level of standards in this area in Germany.
Recommendation 2
Monthly reporting of summary reports
8. the law on the transposition of EU directives into national law was adopted in April 2010.
This law contains provisions relating to the monthly submission of summary reports on intracommunitary deliveries.
Those provisions took effect on 1. July 2010.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and aggregate reports with a view to achieving greater reliability of data in VIES and consideration of the interconnection of both VAT returns and aggregate reports
Established a joint working group consisting of staff from the länder and the Federal ministry of finance.
The group has developed a strategy to automatically compare data from VAT returns and aggregate reports.
This strategy has so far been discussed in the Länder.
In addition, the Working Party looked at the instrument intended to optimise the control procedure for transactions in the internal market.
Recommendation 4
Sharing of successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level the exchange of relevant information takes place at EU level.
Germany is a participant in this exchange within the so-called risk management platform.
The European Commission supported the idea of this platform and on the basis of a written consultation of 18. October 2006 the establishment of a risk management platform was added to the Fiscalis 2006-2007 action plan.
Platform members are further divided into sub-groups, which deal with individual topics, such as: • risk management tools, • influencing the negotiations, • evaluation, • the update guide to risk management.
In early 2010, reports on the results of the activities of these subgroups were published.
4.1.3 evaluation
Registration
The issue of the conditions for VAT registration and cancellation of this registration in different countries has been addressed at EU level.
The draft amendment to Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003 included the extension of existing databases within the EU, including the VAT tax identification numbers database.
It also regulated common minimum standards for registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
For the time being, the issue of registration and cancellation of registration has been left to the national legislation of the EU member states.
Member states requested further clarification and detailed elaboration of this issue.
BRH has asked the Federal Ministry of finance to ensure that the level of standards already achieved in Germany does not fall.
8. in June 2010, the ECOFIN Council reached political agreement on that proposal for a regulation.
The intention of Common Minimum Standards has been abandoned.
Member states shall implement national procedures and only have the duty to inform about these practices, the Committee for administrative cooperation.
Both SAI expressed regret that the Commission failed to persuade member states about the necessity of common standards for the registration and deregistraci payers, because both SAI considered this measure as an important element of prevention in the fight against VAT fraud.
They would therefore welcome further efforts by the Commission in this regard.
Monthly reporting of summary reports
In the framework of international cooperation was in the previous control action recommended to all EU member states have imposed monthly deadline for the submission of summary reports, allowing for more timely screening values intrakomunitárních transactions.
Council directive 2008/117/EC amending directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion connected with intra-Community transactions, it shortens the period of time for which submitted a summary report on the implementation inside the EU, for one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the VAT Act with effect from 1. January 2010, in Germany took effect 1. July 2010.
Germany did not impose a monthly aggregate reporting obligation under the established calendar, while the Czech Republic did (in accordance with EU directives).
Comparison of data in VAT returns and summary reports in Germany with a view to achieving greater reliability of data in VIEs and consideration of the interconnection of both VAT returns and summary reports
The German tax administration accepted the BRH recommendations and set up a working group to find possible solutions.
Work is ongoing so far and the BRH will closely monitor further developments.
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level
Germany and the Czech Republic apply different approaches to the risk management system for the purpose of identifying risk-prone traders.
The SAO has audited the EUROCANET system for the exchange of information in the EU (see Chapter. 4.3).
The BRH focused on German participation in the so-called risk management platform.
4.2. follow-up of selected cases of intracommunitary transactions
In the previous control action was jointly investigated the implementation of commercial transactions, for which there were doubts about their implementation, or inconsistencies in the way the payers of both countries, these business transactions reported in your VAT returns or recapitulative statements.
Both audit institutions selected for the subsequent control of the nine cases involving intracommunity movement of goods between the Czech republic and Germany, whose control by the tax administrations of both countries has not been completed during the previous joint action control.
1)
The Czech payer was acquired at 1. quarter 2005 goods worth EUR 22 686 from the German payer.
This acquisition of goods, the Czech payer in his VAT declaration admitted, because the German payer had in that period allocated a VAT ID, but only the tax number intended for domestic transactions in Germany.
On the basis of international administrative cooperation under Council regulation (EC) no 798/2003 received the Czech tax administrator information, according to the German law on VAT does not have a payer who supplies the goods to other member states, allocated a VAT ID, in order to intracommunity supplies of goods exempt from VAT.
The subsequent control of the SAO audit it was found that on the basis of the checks carried out by the Czech tax administrator filed a Czech payer the additional tax to VAT, in which he admitted the acquisition of goods in the indicated value and at the same time in this tax return to claim the VAT deduction in the same amount.
2)
The Czech payer was 4. quarter 2004 acquire from the German payer goods worth 12 561 euros.
The acquisition of these goods was denied by the Czech payer and did not indicate in his VAT return.
At the request of Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003, the German tax administration refused cooperation as the turnover of transactions did not exceed EUR 15 000.
Since the Czech tax administrator did not obtain the evidence, ended the control without the award and the tax liability remained charged the original amount.
The subsequent control of the SAO found that the Czech tax administrator has received from Germany two spontaneous information according to Council regulation (EC) no 1798/2003, which indicated that the German payer of specified goods charged to Slovakia.
The Czech payer acquired the goods from the Slovak payer and indicated this acquisition in a proper VAT return for the month of October 2004.
3)
The Czech payer was 4. quarter 2004 acquire from the German payer a passenger car worth 48 500 euros.
The acquisition of the goods in question was not admitted by the Czech taxpayer.
This payer has not filed VAT returns since August 2004, therefore the tax administrator has calculated VAT of CZK 0 for that quarter.
On the basis of the information obtained in the framework of the international exchange of information according to Council regulation (EC) no 1798/2003 of Germany urged in march 2007 the tax payer to submit additional tax returns for VAT, which, however, the payer did not file.
The subsequent control, it was found that the tax administrator did in 2007, the other acts in the tax procedure, from which it emerged that the personal automobile Czech payer sold a used car dealer in the Czech republic.
The Czech tax administrator issued the tax assessment for the tax period December 2004 establishing the additionally assessed VAT for the acquisition of goods from another member state and its subsequent sale in the amount of 295 379 CZK.
By order of the regional court, the Czech payer was annulled with liquidation and a liquidator was appointed.
In the absence of foreclosures of the affected property of the tax borrower, this arrears appear impregnable.
4)
The Czech payer was to deliver new vehicles (passenger cars) to Germany during 4. quarter 2004 and 1. quarter 2005 totalling EUR 198 167.
From the responses to the request for information according to Council regulation (EC) no 1798/2003 showed that against the German entity currently underway in Germany, the outstanding tax-criminal proceedings.
Following a follow-up check, BRH obtained information that after the completion of the Tax Procedure in Germany, it was established that the German taxpayer had been incorporated into fraudulent activities.
The intracommunitary acquisition of goods was taxed at EUR 182 424 (2004) and EUR 369 690 (2005).
The Sao subsequently found out that the Czech payer was involved in Carousel deals with new means of transport.
On the basis of the information of the German tax authorities, relating to the verification of delivery of the goods, was in the Czech tax entity started checking the VAT for the tax period April, may and June 2005.
The tax administrator, on the basis of control findings and information obtained in the framework of the international exchange of information additionally assessed VAT for the period may 2005 in the amount of $ 703 031 CZK and for the period June 2005 in the amount of $ 726 551 USD.
5)
The Czech payer and was to acquire a machine totalling EUR 58 000 from the German payer in February 2005.
This German payer was supposed to deliver at 3. quarter 2004 Czech payer B machine worth EUR 88 027, but payer B denied this acquisition of goods.
The subsequent inspection of the Sao found that payer B had acquired the machine from a German company that had established an organizational component in the Czech Republic.
The Czech payer and did not declare the acquisition of goods from the German payer in his VAT return.
From the replies from the German tax administrator on the request for information according to Council regulation (EC) no 1798/2003 showed that the German payer did not materialize intracommunity delivery of the machine in a value of 58 000 EUROS, but the delivery of the goods within the Czech republic.
The BRH subsequently found that after the tax inspection the intracommunitary delivery of the machine had been re-qualified for domestic delivery of the machine and the VAT exemption had been abolished.
6)
The German taxpayer was 3. quarter 2004 to deliver to the Czech payer goods worth EUR 11 600.
The goods were purchased and subsequently sold in Germany in 2005.
The Sao subsequently found that the Czech tax administrator had issued an additional VAT Return where the acquisition of goods from another EU member state, including the acquisition of goods at that value, was wrongly indicated.
BRH found that, after receiving a reply to a request for information pursuant to Council regulation (EC) no 1798/2003 fixed the German tax administrator tax returns for VAT to the German payer and the additionally assessed VAT in € 1 600€.
Further movement of goods in Germany and the application of VAT in Germany is subject to tax control.
Summary report of the German payer has not yet been fixed, because the bug summary report in Germany can be carried out only payer, that the summary report has filed.
7)
The Czech tax administrator has received from the German tax administration request for information pursuant to Council regulation (EC) no 1798/2003, whether the Czech taxpayer acquired in February 2005 from a German payer's personal automobile at a price of 47 EUR 400.
After the tax procedure carried out in February 2005, the Czech tax administrator imposed a tax liability of CZK 0 on the Czech taxpayer and informed the German tax administrator that he could not confirm the acquisition of the car by the Czech taxpayer.
The subsequent inspection of the Sao found that the registration of the Czech VAT payer was cancelled in 2007 for non-compliance and the Czech tax administrator sent documents to the police of the Czech Republic.
Subsequent control of the BRH found that the German payer changed its registered office and the new locally competent tax administrator on the basis of the checks carried out, canceled the exemption from VAT for the supply of car to the Czech payer.
The German taxpayer has not yet corrected the data in the summary report and has lodged an appeal against the tax administrator's decision.
8)
According to data from the VIES system, the German payer supplied the Czech taxpayer in the period from 3. quarter 2004 to 1. quarter 2005 goods totalling EUR 33 205.
The subsequent control of the SAO found that the Czech tax administrator trying to find out the causes of differences arising for the Czech tax payer in the procurement of goods in the period from 3. quarter 2004 to 1. quarter 2005.
The Czech taxpayer has repeatedly filed an additional VAT return for 1. quarter 2005.
The Czech tax administrator did not clarify the difference in the value of the Goods acquired in the amount of CZK 134 273 for the period 3. quarter 2004 to 1. quarter of 2005, because, according to the statement of the Czech tax administrator it was not possible to accurately capture business transactions for each quarter, and therefore the tax administrator accepted from the additional tax returns.
9)
The German taxpayer delivered at 3. quarter 2004 to the Czech payer of goods worth EUR 46 854.
For the same period, the Czech payer granted intracommunitary acquisition of goods worth only EUR 14 856.
The Czech tax administrator verified the amount of deliveries made in the framework of the international exchange of information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003.
The reply to the request for information received from Germany were accompanied by 3 invoices with a total listed value of the delivery goods 31 998 EURO, which is the value corresponding to the difference between the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in the VAT return and the data referred to in VIES.
The subsequent control of the SAO found that the Czech payer filed after many urgencích tax additional tax VAT return for the tax period July 2004 until January 2007.
At the same time, in this tax return, the taxpayer invoked the right to deduct VAT, thereby leaving the tax liability for that tax period unchanged.
Subsequent checking verified that for the selected cases of business transactions between payers from the Czech republic and Germany were most of the tax proceeding is completed and that the tax authorities in the Czech republic and Germany have made adequate arrangements (i.e., retrospectively assigned a VAT or to prevent tax refund on entry).
4.3. control of selected cases of risk intracommunitary transactions
4.3.1 results of the inspection in the Czech Republic
EUROCANET can be an important source of information for the detection of high-risk entities within a member state, in which the acquisition of goods.
In the Czech Republic, the signal information obtained from EUROCANET was compared by the relevant local tax authorities with data on the purchasers.
Starting with 1. quarter of 2008 sends Czech republic into the system of the EUROCANET data on risk transactions and tax entities acting as contractors.
In the framework of international cooperation, nine Czech tax entities included in EUROCANET were selected for control.
These entities acted either as suppliers or as purchasers of goods.
Relevant data from tax managers from other member states were captured in EUROCANET.
Due to the fact that the German tax administration did not participate in the exchange of data in the system EUROCANET, it was not possible to obtain any information that would help figure out whether they were contractors with a German VAT ID identified the German tax administration as risky entities.
The audit revealed cases of ordinary commercial transactions, as well as cases suspected of involvement in Carousel trades or fraudulent conduct relating to VAT.
Where applicable, the tax authorities used the exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) no 1798/2003.
Perhaps:
* The tax authorities did not reveal any suspicions of involvement in risky transactions when verifying signal information.
The tax authorities shall monitor such tax entities on an ongoing basis for their inclusion in EUROCANET.
• Financial authorities during the verification, the risk of transactions not shown in the submitted accounts, derogations from the rules applicable for the calculation of the tax base and VAT, although they found inconsistencies in the area of transportation and storage of goods or revealed a business relationship with the suspects or nekontaktními companies from other member states.
* Verification of business transactions was complicated as some taxpayers did not cooperate with tax administrators and could not be contacted.
Locally competent tax authorities have mostly examined risk tax entities and risk transactions listed in eurocanet signal information.
The tax administrator in examining risk transactions, in particular in connection with the screening of the so-called missing traders , they have limited options and only from physical control of the documents it is difficult to prove to the tax entity of fraudulent actions.
Tougher requirements for VAT registration and more flexible cancellation of registrations would help reduce missing trader fraud.
In the case of the tax entities involved in a revolving fraud and other fraudulent activities is occurring to register for VAT for the purpose of reporting of fictitious supplies of goods within the EU or for the purpose of issuance of a formally proper tax documents to payers, who on the basis of unduly draw deductions of input VAT.
In cases where there is suspicion of the involvement of tax bodies to the revolving stores and other fraud and leads to the import and export of goods from third countries, it would be appropriate to ensure greater mutual cooperation in customs and financial authorities.
Closer cooperation between these institutions would help in the identification of goods and irregularities in the transport documents and also in monitoring of the physical movement of goods within the EU towards the end consumer.
The participation of EU member states in EUROCANET is voluntary.
The fact that the activities of the system EUROCANET did not participate in the three large member states (Germany, Italy and the United kingdom), reviewed by the European parliament in late 2008, as the weakness of this system, which would be the establishment of compulsory in the EUROFISC network should be removed.
4.3.2 results of the inspection in Germany
BRH analysed the information available to the Federal central financial authority, which contained data from EUROCANET.
These figures were a criterion for the collection of six files of German taxpayers for inspection.
Germany, like some other countries, has refused to actively participate in EUROCANET.
Thus, Germany has a passive status, which means that it does not send data to Brussels, but is only the recipient of data from EUROCANET.
The justification for this position is contained in the following statement:in the government's view, it is not legally permissible for state (public) institutions to provide data to EUROCANET.
Currently there is no legal base that would allow it to violate the valid regulations on the secrecy of tax information.
In addition, the government has no reliable information on the use of such data within EUROCANET by other member states.“17 Since October 2007, is made by the Federal central tax office analysis of data from the system EUROCANET and submits them to the tax authorities of the länder in accordance with the agreed procedure.
The German financial authorities receive the control information on the direct commercial relations of payers (registered for the specific tax authorities) with traders from other member states, who were included into the system of the EUROCANET.
The German financial authorities, however, do not receive any information about whether such a trader from another member state has some risky trading relationships with traders from other member states who also maintain a commercial intercourse with the German trader.
4.3.3 evaluation
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has a passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active participant if some member states refuse active participation.
As a result of this, the control in the area had to be carried out in different ways.
However, the results did not reveal major differences in the detection of VAT fraud cases, since EUROCANET is not the only systemic risk management tool.
The tax administration of both countries have a variety of other tools to detect fraudulent transactions, however, it is necessary to create within the EU a comprehensive risk management system.
The EU Council reached political agreement on the draft regulation, the main benefit of which lies in the establishment of the eurofisc network.
Experience gained in the use of EUROCANET data should also be part of the projected VAT fraud network.
Member states should therefore communicate their experiences at European level.
On the other hand, cases submitted to the courts at national and european level show that it is apparently necessary discussion between the member states and the Commission about the conditions of the tax exemptions in the intrakomunitárních transactions.
4.4 mutual assistance in the recovery of claims
4.4.1 international assistance for debt collection in the Czech Republic
In particular, the following directives are the basic arrangements for international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU:
• Council directive no. 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims resulting from operations forming part of the system of financing the European agricultural guidance and guarantee fund, as well as agricultural levies and customs duties;
• Council directive no. 2001/44/EC amending directive no. 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims resulting from operations forming part of the system of financing the European agricultural guidance and guarantee fund, and of agricultural levies and customs duties, value added tax and certain excise taxes;
• Commission directive no. 2002/94/EC, implementing certain provisions of Council directive no. 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims relating to certain levies, duties, taxes and other measures.
In the Czech Republic, Council Directive 76/308 / EEC was implemented by Act No. 252/2000 Coll., on international assistance in the recovery of certain financial claims.
Following the adoption of council directive 2001/44/EC, it was necessary to implement this directive into the Czech legal order and at the same time to amend that Act No. 252/2000 Coll.
In this connection, a new law No. 191/2004 Coll.was adopted., on international assistance in the recovery of certain financial claims.
Commission Regulation (EC) no 1179/2008 of 28 is a new regulation in the system for regulating international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU. 11. 2008.
The annex to the regulation sets out new models of applications which apply from 1. 1. 2009, newly establishes the obligation of electronic communications and the obligation of the requesting authority to certify the conformity of the sent documents with the original document.
Guiding principles for providing international cooperation in debt collection:
1. reciprocity;
2. assistance shall always be provided only upon request containing the requisites prescribed;
3. the aid does not apply to financial claims which have the nature of criminal penalties in the requested state;
4. in the provision of international assistance for the recovery of claims shall be governed by the national legal order of the state, which was to help asked;
5. foreign receivables do not take precedence in recovery;
6. assistance shall be granted only in the recovery of undisputed claims;
7. the principle of exhaustion (the requesting state has, without success, used all applicable possibilities to recover the claim under its legal order).
Act No. 191/2004 Coll. defines the three forms, which assistance takes place, and that the provision of information, service of documents and custom recovery.
Procedure for sending claims for recovery to other EU member states
The locally competent financial office electronically sends a request for information, request for service or request for enforcement of the receivables together with the relevant documents to the Czech ministry of finance through the financial directorate.
The Czech ministry of finance shall ensure translation of the application into the relevant language, scans it, including its annexes and through the CCN/CSI network shall send to the competent authority of the tax administration of the designated state.
For recovery, two basic requirements apply: the claim must be more than EUR 1 500 and must not be older than 5 years.
If those requirements are not met, the requested authority may refuse enforcement.
Procedure for receiving claims for recovery from other EU member states
When receiving an application from another member state, the Czech Ministry of Finance must confirm receipt of the application as soon as possible, not later than seven days.
If the Czech ministry of finance decides not to accept an application, it shall notify the applicant authority of the reasons for rejection and indicate the specific provisions of the directive which it relies.
This communication must be sent no later than three months after the date of confirmation of receipt of the application.
After receipt of the request of the Czech ministry of finance shall verify whether the request of all the formalities under the law, and should request without delay to the pass through of the financial directorate of the locally competent tax office for processing.
If the request for recovery of accepted, the tax administrator, inter alia, determines the debtor's assets, e.g. the acquisition of statements from the cadastre, the survey accounts in banks, verification of vehicle registration, the dmv, etc.
After a lapse of six months from the date of acknowledgement of receipt of the request, should the Czech ministry of finance requesting authority to disclose the outcome of the investigation, which was carried out in order to obtain the required information.
In the case of non-contact tax entities where the claim cannot be recovered, the requesting authority should also be informed of this fact.
Any sum recovered by the tax authority shall be transferred to the applicant authority in CZK within one month from the date on which recovery was effected.
It is not excluded, that the Czech tax administrator to enforce foreign claims authorized an extension to its payment or payment in instalments, unless with the consent of the state which the enforcement requested.
For the period of recovery, the debtor is prescribed interest or penalty payments under Act No. 337/1992 Coll., about the administration of taxes and fees.
This interest or penalty payment belongs to the state which requested the recovery.
In the case of received applications for enforcement, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not refer the applications to the tax authorities locally in time for processing, in particular in 2006 and 2007.
A similar situation was detected in the framework of the international assistance for recovery even in the case of applications received from the tax administrators from the Czech republic.
The audit revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not act in accordance with Act No. 191/2004 Coll. because failing to notify the locally competent authority of the member state on the progress made in the enforcement within six months from the date of confirmed receipt of the request.
This situation has been improving since 2008.
Statistics
The Czech Ministry of Finance in accordance with the provisions of § 13 Para. 4 of Act No. 191/2004 Coll. processed every year until 15. march statistical data for the European commission, indicating the number of requests for information, delivery or enforcement of, sent or received in the past year stating the amount of the claims to which the requests relate.
The european commission prepares on the basis of information provided by all EU member states report on the status of recovery of claims by the EU Council and the European parliament.
Scrutiny it was found that the Czech ministry of finance podhodnotilo statistical data due to errors in the entry of the claims involved in 2008, about 5 to 250 thous. EUR, and placing an incorrect value of the claim to be recovered on the VAT (it was a shift in the decimal point after the conversion of receivables of the Czech crowns to the value in euros).
This error was subsequently translated into European Commission statistics.
Information on mutual assistance, including recoveries, is presented in the table below.
4.4.2 international assistance for debt collection in Germany
The legal authority to international administrative assistance in tax matters derives from the law of the European communities, Council directive no. 2008/55/EC of 26. May 2008 (EC debt collection directive) and Commission regulation of 28. November 2008 (EC implementing directive).
In the interests of more accessible wording and better clarity, the EC debt collection directive codifies council directive 76/308/EEC of 15. March 197621, the provisions of which have already been substantially amended several times.
The provisions apply, inter alia, to the recovery of VAT, income tax and capital gains tax, including accessories.
The EC debt collection directive was transposed into national German law by the state tax collection act (EC) of 3. May 2003.
The enforcement procedure in Germany is governed by the German fiscal code.
Article 117.2 of the code stresses that the tax authorities may provide international legal and administrative assistance on the basis of international agreements and legal instruments of the European communities, which are in force in the national jurisdiction, and on the basis of the law of the EC administrative assistance.
Part six of the German fiscal code (articles 249-346) enshrines statutory provisions governing the Enforcement Procedure.
The administrative operations of the tax authorities shall be governed, in particular, by execution instructions and enforcement instructions.
The federal ministry of finance reached an agreement with representatives of the highest tax authorities of the länder (Länder) as regards the principle of administrative assistance in levying taxes, and shift their own responsibility in this matter to the Federal central tax office.
The general prerequisites for submitting claims for recovery are the following:
* Legal requirements must be fulfilled (§251 and § 254 of the German fiscal code [AO]).
* All available domestic enforcement resources have already been exhausted.
* Claims that are the subject of requests for recovery assistance must be final.
• No more than 5 years may elapse until the date of application.
* The total amount of the claim must be more than EUR 1 500.
Procedure for sending claims for recovery to other EU member states
The German request for recovery of the outstanding tax liabilities shall be sent from the implementing bodies of the financial authorities to the competent foreign authority, such as the Czech CUSTOMS, and through the intermediary of the office and of the Federal central tax office.
The procedure follows the methodological guidance on international administrative assistance in tax matters (debt collection) of 19. January 2004.25 the Working Party of the federal government and the provincial governments is currently reviewing this methodological instruction in order to adapt it to the debt collection directive.
The application, including the annexes, shall be submitted by the tax office to the electronically intermediate authority.
This office will check the correctness of the application by page of the content and form.
If the application is not correct, it is returned to the relevant tax office.
If it meets all the requirements, it is referred to the federal Central Tax Office.
The federal central tax office subsequently ensure the necessary communication with the competent foreign authority and will also ensure the translation of the application.
Procedure for receiving claims for recovery from other EU member states
Requests for recovery received from other member states ' registers by the Federal central tax office and within 10 days send a confirmation of their receipt.
In addition, the federal Central Tax Office will check whether formal requirements have been met.
The federal central tax office submits these requests require an intermediary office, which is further advancing to the competent financial authorities and monitors their execution.
The federal Central Tax Office also sends preliminary or final reports.
Where the processing of an application takes more than 6 months, the intermediary office shall invite a preliminary report to be submitted pursuant to Article 16 of Commission directive 2002/94/DG.
Once the formal and factual requirements of the application have been checked, the implementing services shall notify the enforcement method.
Any recovered amounts must be transferred to the bank account indicated in the application within one month from their receipt.
