4.4.3 control of debt collection, case studies
In the framework of international cooperation was to control the selected 21 requests for international assistance for the recovery of claims between the Czech republic and Germany.
The examination of ten selected cases was found, among other things:
1.
20. 10. 2006 received the Czech ministry of finance of Germany the request for recovery of VAT for the years 2004 and 2005 in the total amount of eur 3 883 EUR, i.e. 109 820 CZK for Czech tax entity.
The Czech Ministry of finance sent a request for recovery to the tax administrator on 26. 2. 2008.
In order to secure the recovery of the claim, the Czech tax administrator established a lien on real estate owned by the Czech tax entity.
Since it was not possible even to pay the entire debt collected by the mortgage, a repayment schedule was agreed with the Czech tax entity with repayments of min. 2 000 CZK per month.
31. 8. 2009 was sent to the German tax administration information on the state of recovery of the claim, saying on 25. 8. 2009 this claim was partially recovered in instalments of CZK 49,600.
This amount was sent to Germany and further on 28. 8. A further payment of CZK 3,000 was sent to Germany in 2009.
2.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received on 7. 1. 2008 request for recovery of tax arrears in the Czech tax entity, which he owed in Germany the amount of 180 869 EUROS, i.e. 4 434 915 CZK, VAT and income tax and accessories.
The Czech Ministry of finance sent the application to the tax administrator on 27. 11. 2008.
The tax administrator verification of ownership of accounts with banks, securities, real estate, motor vehicles and movables found that the borrower does not own any exekuovatelný property.
In addition, the local investigation found that the borrower did not stay at the address of permanent residence for almost a year.
His whereabouts in the Czech Republic are unknown.
This communication was received by the Czech Ministry of Finance on 6. 4. 2009 and 16. 4. 2009 the tax administrator's reply was sent to the German tax administration.
3.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received from Germany on 21. 11. 2007 application for recovery concerning tax arrears on sales tax and accessories of the Czech tax entity amounting to EUR 3 139, i.e. CZK 84 846.
The Czech Ministry of finance sent a request for recovery of this claim on 6. 8. 2008 tax administrators, although already on 18. 2. 2008 the Czech Ministry of Finance received information from Germany that the Czech tax entity had paid the claim in Germany.
Czech Ministry of Finance on 9. 12. 2008 notified the tax administrator that the application for recovery is settled by payment of the claim by the Czech tax entity in Germany.
However, the claim in question was also paid in the framework of enforcement in the Czech Republic and referred to Germany on 27. 10. 2008.
The fault of long time periods, in which the Czech ministry of finance has informed the charge of the tax administrator, occurred in this case to pay the claim twice - alone entity in Germany and vymožením claims the Czech tax administrator.
In cooperation with the BRH, it was found that the amount recovered from the Czech republic should be offset against the claims of another request for recovery of $ 6 649 EUROS, which should be to the Czech republic sent in September 2008.
The Czech ministry of finance records for this company, only a request for recovery in the amount of 3 139 EUR, request for recovery of $ 6 649 EUROS in the records of the Czech ministry of finance for the companies concerned does not occur.
4.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received 15. 9. 2008 from Germany request for the recovery of tax arrears in the Czech tax entity, which he owed in Germany on income tax and VAT and accessories amount 39 957 EUROS, i.e. 956 654 CZK.
On 19. 12. 2008 the Czech Ministry of finance sent a request to the Czech tax administrator.
1. 6. 2009 procedure has been initiated enforcement claims, was an execution of the commandment of receivables in accounts with banks in the Czech republic and on the payroll deduction (the deduction amounted to 7 000 CZK).
In dealing with the tax administrator, the debtor stated that he did not agree with the amount of the claim and considered it questionable.
The Czech tax administrator found that the taxpayer was in the past willing to pay 250 EUROS a month, which wasn't the German tax authorities accepted.
The tax entity has promised to discuss the application with the German tax administrator in order to achieve a change in the amount of its claim.
The recovery of the claim was still ongoing at the time of the Sao audit operation.
5.
On 19. 11. 2007 the Czech ministry of finance has received from Germany a request for recovery related to the Czech tax entity that owed income tax for the year 2005 and the turnover tax for the period 2003-2007 and accessories a total of 113 444 EUR, i.e. 3 116 304 USD.
The Czech Ministry of finance sent an application to the Fu for Threshold 1, which is responsible for the administration of tax for non-established tax entities in the Czech Republic, up to 14. 11. 2008, since on the basis of that address of the tax entity it was not possible to determine the local tax administrator.
In the investigation carried out, the MO received information that the debtor had on 19. 9. 2008 income of EUR 4 704; however, for this amount the mergers could no longer issue an execution order, since the Czech Ministry of Finance submitted a request for recovery only after that date.
26. 1. 2009 the Czech tax administrator started the recovery of the claim and issued an execution order for the commandment of the debtor's money claim in accounts held with banks and savings and credit unions.
The recovery of the claim was still ongoing at the time of the Sao audit operation.
6.
The Czech tax administrator requested international cooperation in the recovery of VAT and costs totalling CZK 146 223 742 on 3. 10. 2006.
The Czech Ministry of finance sent this request for enforcement to the German tax administration only on 13. 5. 2008.
German tax administrator on 8. 9. 2008 transferred to the Czech authorities through the Federal Bank the amount obtained from the execution of funds in the debtor's account amounting to EUR 17 700, i.e. CZK 439 226.
In verifying the volume of receivables recovered, an error was found in the recalculation of the amount recovered.
The recovery amount of CZK 146 223 742 was converted at EUR 1 = CZK 25,065 erroneously to EUR 583 378.
The correct recalculation of the recovery amount shall be EUR 5 833 781,83.
A request for recovery was therefore sent to Germany, which was lower by EUR 5 250 404.
7.
Czech tax administrator on 1. 3. 2007 sent to the Czech ministry of finance a request for recovery of the tax arrears in the Czech tax entity that owed money to the VAT and accessories the amount of 1 970 632 CZK, i.e. 79 847 EUROS.
The Czech Ministry of finance sent the application to the German tax administration on 10. 11. 2008.
German tax administrator on 4. 2. 2009 urged the borrower to pay an arrears.
In view of the significant declines in the company's turnover in 2. mid-2008 and in particular 1. by mid-2009 and The Associated liquidation situation of the company, the following payments were made to pay the arrears: on 8. 4. 2009 amount EUR 4 600, on 6. 5. 2009 amount of EUR 3 000 and 16. 6. 2009 amount EUR 2,500.
These payments were sent to the account of the tax administrator in the Czech Republic.
23. 6. 2009 the German tax administrator agreed with the debtor that up to 30. 6. 2009 will pay an additional instalment of EUR 2,500.
8.
Request for recovery in the total amount of 398 653 EUROS, i.e. 9 832 779 CZK, including a claim for real estate transfer tax, was from the Czech tax administrator delivered to the Czech ministry of finance 22. 5. 2008.
The Czech Ministry of finance sent a request for enforcement to the German tax administration on 2. 10. 2008.
3. 4. 2009 received the Czech ministry of finance, the German tax administration that the application was returned to the German tax authorities back.
The German tax administration justified the reimbursement by the fact that the property transfer tax is not a tax within the meaning of Article 2 (2). (e), (f), (g) or (e) (h) Council Directive 2008/55/EC.
In addition, the German tax administration stated that Article 2 (2) (2) should be applied. (g) concerns claims relating to income tax and property taxes.
Likewise, Article 3 of council directive 2008/55/EC shall apply to taxes on income and property listed in Article 1 (1). 3 in conjunction with para. 4 Council Directive 77/799 / EEC.
The Czech Ministry of Finance proposed to draw up and submit a new application for recovery excluding the arrears on property transfer tax amounting to CZK 61 759 and specifying the arrears on VAT, corporation tax and personal income tax, which will be re-sent to the German tax administration.
The Czech finance ministry received a new request to the Czech tax administrator for recovery of tax arrears related to the same tax entity that owes the income tax and VAT amount 7 079 735 CZK.
9.
On 6. 2. 2006 sent the Czech tax administrator, the Czech ministry of finance request, which concerned the recovery of tax arrears in the Czech tax entity owed on personal income tax and the VAT amount 3 445 782 CZK, i.e. 123 328 EUR.
Of this amount, VAT was CZK 1,133,967.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the request to the German tax administration until 18. 4. 2007.
The Czech Ministry of Finance forwarded to the Czech tax administrator the reply of the German tax administration of 9. 7. 2007 to 11. 11. 2008.
In reply it was stated that the German tax administrator issued on 11. 6. 2007 execution order for a bank account with the bank, which, however, said that it had no business relations with the tax entity.
By this, the German tax administration considered the application to be settled.
10.
26. 9. 2005 the Czech tax administrator sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of tax arrears for VAT totalling CZK 1,296,845, i.e. EUR 43,591.
The request from the Czech tax administrator was received by the Czech Ministry of Finance on 10. 10. 2005.
Czech Ministry of Finance on 15. 12. 2005 sent a request to the German tax administration.
The Czech tax administrator before submitting a request for enforcement by execution on monetary funds of the debtor on accounts with the bank and a deduction of wages, and established the right of lien to immovable things.
Requests for enforcement were preceded by a request for information sent to the German tax authority on 16. 3. 2005.
From the reply to the request for information received by the Czech tax administrator 16. 9. 2005, it emerged that the Czech tax entity was staying in Germany and had an income of EUR 8 437 from non-business activities.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received a response to the request for recovery on 20. 4. 2006, but forwarded it to the Czech tax authority on 12. 2. 2008.
In response it was stated that Germany could not be initiated any enforcement proceedings, and because of the insolvency of the debtor - was not with him detected no assets and his income from non-business activities are already subject to other enforcement actions.
In doing so, the German tax administration considered the application for recovery to be settled.
4.4.4 comparison and evaluation
In the area of international recovery assistance to all EU member states governed by the same european legislation.
Therefore, the method of processing applications for international assistance in debt collection in the Czech Republic and Germany is identical.
The SAO and the BRH carried out a comparison of the statistics submitted by both member states to the European Commission for the period 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics did not coincide.
In its 2006 report, the European Commission recommended that member states pay increased attention to the management of their statistics.
In the 2009 report, the Commission concluded that the incidence of mismatches in statistics had decreased even though the number of applications had increased.
Both SAI consider it important that the issues of Statistics be renegotiated at EU level.
This discussion should focus on how to avoid persistent inconsistencies, otherwise the data reported by EU states in the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, both SAI concur in the opinion that reliable statistics are required to report the annual number of applications and also the nature of the claims (i.e. claims relating to VAT, income tax, etc.) and the amount of claims recovered by the member states.
Both SAI considered important that the Commission provide a more detailed analysis of the statistics submitted by the member states, because it can assist member states in assessing their own effectiveness in fighting fraud on the VAT.
The fact that the recovery rate can be calculated broken down by member state, both SAI consider it useful for member states with a lower recovery rate to intensify their efforts and seek to improve the recovery rate at least to the level of the EU average.
If a member state so wishes, the commission should take an active part in this process.
In particular, in 2006 and 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not submit applications for debt collection to the tax authorities locally in a timely manner.
A similar situation was found for applications for international assistance received from tax authorities in the Czech Republic.
The audit revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not act in accordance with Act No. 191/2004 Coll. about the international assistance for the recovery of claims, because it had not informed the competent authority of the member state on the progress made in the enforcement within six months from the date of confirmed receipt of the request.
4.5 control of large tax entities
4.5.1 control of large tax entities in the Czech Republic
General information
The VAT audit of large tax entities is governed by the same rules as that of other tax entities.
The procedural procedure for controlling VDS is based on Act No. 337/1992 Coll., about the administration of taxes and fees.
The Czech ministry of finance has defined VDS as natural or legal persons that were founded or established for business purposes and whose net turnover for the tax period referred to in the income tax return of natural/legal persons reached the amount of 2 billion CZK or higher.
The inclusion of the tax entity in the VDS occurred after the filing of the income tax return for the relevant tax period, for the first time in 2003.
Tax entity ceased to be referred to as the VDS, if in three consecutive tax periods from the end of the period, when he filed a tax return on the basis of which was between the VDS included, its net turnover for the tax period fell below the threshold.
The tax entity may not be excluded from the VDS register without carrying out a tax inspection of at least one tax per tax period.
All VDS were checked at least in a five-year period until the end of 2009.
Since the year 2010 must be at least once every 2 years carried out a written evaluation of the tax entity and the chosen subsequent procedure must be eliminated tax risks and their negative impact on the correct determination of and recovery of tax.
The control of the FU is aimed at at least one type of tax; as a rule, the tax administrator chooses several tax periods at once.
The VDS were controlled by the specialised inspection departments, which are set up for a total of 13 FUS, or by the inspection departments of the locally relevant FUS.
The Department of specialised inspections shall carry out tax checks within the scope established by the director of the financial Directorate.
In addition to large tax entity audits, it also examines
* tax entities operating in unusual and specific business fields;
* entities for which the implementation of tax control is professionally and time-consuming;
* entities with a branched territorial and organizational structure;
* entities suspected of large-scale tax evasion;
• entities linked in chains and networks, suspected of extensive tax evasion and the unjustified lure of excessive deductions.
The number of tax inspections carried out by the Departments of specialised M & A checks and the results of those checks are set out in Table 3.
The Czech Ministry of Finance proposed an amendment to Act No. 531/1990 Coll., on territorial financial bodies, which consists in the establishment of the specialized tax office with nationwide coverage for selected tax entities (including for legal persons created for the purpose of business, which reached a turnover of more than 2 billion CZK).
4.5.2 control of large tax entities in Germany
General information
Checks on VAT for large companies is governed by the same rules as the tax control in general, i.e. the relevant provisions are enshrined in the following legislation: • the German fiscal code (AO), • the law on fiscal administration (FVG), • regulations on tax inspections (BpO).
Other methodological documents are also in force.
German fiscal code
Statutory provisions relating to control are enshrined in articles 193-203 of the German fiscal code in section IV - Tax inspection on the spot. These articles in particular provide the rules of admissibility of tax inspection on the spot (i.e. in the premises of the enterprise), their range around the page of the course, the rules for the division of responsibilities, the form and content of the notice of inspection, control principles, the obligations of the entity to cooperate and the prerequisites for the implementation of the final discussion and communication of the inspection report.
On-the-spot tax inspections are carried out by the responsible tax authorities (article 195 of the code).
The Fiscal Governance Act referred to in Article 5.1 (1), in connection with Article 5.1 (1), 19 of the act, participation in on-the-spot tax inspections carried out by the federal Central Tax Office is compulsory.
The authorities involved shall agree together on the spot the nature and extent of the federal Central Tax Office's participation in tax controls.
In addition, it has the Federal central tax office the right to require specific businesses, which selects, were subjected to scrutiny at a time you designate.
In this case, it can declare the rules for the implementation and content of the inspection at the premises of these companies.
The regulations on tax inspections According to the article 108.7 of the German constitution were regulations on tax inspections (German acronym BpO 2000) agreed by the Federal council (Bundesrat, upper house of the German parliament, in which are represented the governments of the länder).
These administrative regulations apply for the on-site inspection by the financial authorities of the länder and the Federal central tax office.
Undertakings shall be classified according to size at regular intervals in accordance with Article 3 of BPO 2000.
Large enterprises are subject to subsequent control (article 4.2 BpO).
Pursuant to Article 33.1 of BPO 2000, each informed Tax Authority must keep a register of Company groups as defined in BPO 2000.
Methodological guidelines
In addition to the above, the additional methodology for tax administration provides the following guidelines:
* Single manual for special VAT checks in Germany ;
* a USLO manual setting out a methodology for the use of intracommunitary business relationship data held in VIES;
* ZAUBER manual that sets the methodology for using the Zauber database;
* work aids for various and special items.
The classification of tax entities is based on criteria such as turnover and net profit, with different limits by type of business.
The data is published by the Federal Ministry of Finance.
They are evaluated every three years and fixed for the next three years.
The number of companies to control - not just large enterprises - must be determined at regular control intervals.
In general, inspections of large enterprises are carried out on an ongoing basis.
Checks are usually declared including VAT checks.
This means that in the course of the inspection, checks shall be definitively carried out mainly on income tax, excise duty and VAT - i.e. checks on all types of relevant taxes.
VAT checks may be carried out either by tax inspectors or by VAT inspectors.
Implementation varies and depends on the organizational arrangement of the Länder.
The number of tax periods covered by checks usually ranges from three to five years.
BPO 2000 envisages a three-year Control Period.
The subject of examination is all taxes of the company.
4.5.3 control management of large tax entities
Both SAI decided not to investigate individual cases of VDS checks carried out, but focused on management issues in order to get an overview of how tax administrations manage VAT checks at VDS.
In the form of a questionnaire, they collected information from tax authorities about the areas they consider essential for managing the issue.
• What statistical records and analyses regarding VAT control for VDS are available to the management of tax administrations?
Especially:
• Are there any statistics or records of rates in which a distinction is made between combating VAT fraud and generally controlling VAT?
Czech Republic: No, the ADIS system does not allow such a resolution with the current data version.
Germany: the tax administration does not distinguish between the control proposed to combat VAT fraud and the general control of VAT.
• Are there any statistics or records of the timeliness of VAT checks (in connection with the time period of controlled transactions)?
Czech Republic: Records on the timeliness of inquiries with relevance for intracommunitary acquisition of goods for selected VAT payers are reported in the ADIS system.
In addition, the information registered in ADIS also includes data on the type of Question Time.
Germany: No, the unified statistics at the federal level for tax inspectors to contain only information on the average time of the last inspection (information on the year).
This figure does not provide an overview of the selected control periods with respect to individual entrepreneurs.
VAT controllers focus on the latest tax assessment period; they also have the right to carry out VDS checks.
However, statistics produced at the federal level for special VAT control services do not provide information on the classification of tax entities.
• There are any statistics or records on the nature of the additional tax revenues generated, broken down e.g. by the following criteria:
and. net tax increase (e.g. in cases where a tax entity has unlawfully applied a reduced VAT rate instead of the standard tax rate);
II. only nominal increase in tax liability (e.g. transfer of a fully qualified VAT case to another tax period);
III. additional collection of the income tax (payment of the additional tax due).
Czech Republic:
The Czech tax administration monitors the number of carried out verification of the tax, the volumes of the additionally assessed tax broken down by type of tax, according to the number of controlled taxpayers and in the number of audited tax period.
Other tax procedures (local inquiries, complaints) are followed in the same way.
As a separate task, time data and amounts of additional taxes paid are recorded.
General Debt Statistics broken down by type of tax, but not by the declared tax or by the Tax Administrator shall also be kept.
Germany: no, uniform statistics at the federal level for tax controllers and special VAT control services do not distinguish between those criteria.
Moreover, most tax administrations visited do not distinguish these differences.
• Are there areas of control that generate high additional returns?
Czech republic: Yes, the tax administrator has the right to collect tax payer for verification on the basis of criteria, which can be build on the selected indicators in special sections of the ADIS.
Germany: there are no regulations at the federal level.
It follows from this that uniform statistics at the federal level for tax controllers and special VAT control services do not provide such data.
However, there is one coordinated approach by the finance ministers of the federal states and the federal government.
In the database ZAUBER must tax investigation or tax investigators from the German länder to write them levied an increased tax (VAT) the obligation, if it exceeds a certain amount.
In this case, they must specify, for example, the nature of the tax increase measured.
* What findings are most common?
Czech Republic:
- VDS make an unauthorised right to deduct input tax for supplies and services:
* which have not been used to carry out any economic activity under § 72 (2). 1 of the VAT Act;
• which have been used for representation pursuant to § 75 para. 3 of the VAT Act;
• on the basis of tax documents that did not comply with the requirements set out in § 73 para. 1 of the VAT Act;
- The VDS have not declarised output VAT pursuant to § 21 (2). 1 of the VAT Act.
Germany: it was noted that there are no regulations at the federal level.
It follows from this that uniform statistics at the federal level for tax controllers and special VAT control services do not provide such data.
VAT findings are not independently registered by the Länder if they result from the VDS tax controls.
However, in the database ZAUBER, where tax auditors or by investigators from the länder to write them levied an increased tax (VAT) the obligation, if it exceeds a certain amount, is the Federal central tax office able to these information to analyze.
* Does the tax administration analyse the areas of control resulting from high "yield" and infer the consequences for management?
Czech Republic: yes, for example, they are launching national audits on risk commodities or the subject of economic activity.
Germany: there are no regulations at the federal level.
Uniform statistics at the federal level for tax controllers and special VAT control services do not provide data on Audit areas resulting in high "revenues".
There are different views on the process of analysis, as well as on the management of cases in terms of significance.
Some regional financial authorities provide special information, but their use is at the discretion of the financial authorities.
4.5.4 comparison and evaluation
Differences in the responses of both the member states show that the Czech republic provides a system that collects the amount of data of the carried-out tax inspections and further data from the statements of the accounts - the balance sheet and statements of profit and loss.
Based on a wide range of data, the Czech Republic is able to regulate the selection of cases with a risk-prone nature.
The same applies to the analysis and management of VAT control in general.
In 2012, the establishment of a specialized tax office for the administration of VDS is planned in the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the tax administration does not collect this information.
It follows from this that it is more difficult to carry out these tasks in a similar way.
However, Germany's philosophy places more emphasis on the selection of individual cases on the basis of data from the tax returns submitted.
The risk management components will therefore be strengthened and improved.
On the basis of adequate reference notes, expert auditors must be able to measure the exact amount of VAT.
Both SAI concur in the opinion that member states should be able to ensure adequate financial management and adequate risk management system.
This will help reduce outages in VAT revenue.
As a result, the return on VAT collection will increase and the level of risk detection among unreliable entrepreneurs will improve.
5. Conclusion
Cooperation between the two SAI on parallel controls of VAT management has met the objectives set by the SAO and the BRH.
Both SAI know each other better applicable systems in the following areas: • intracommunity transactions, • risk management, VAT, in particular as regards the choice of transaction is prone to risk, • assistance in recovery of VAT and • control of VAT for large taxpayers.
Thanks to mutual cooperation, differences in VAT fraud detection strategies and differences in the above VAT management areas in the Czech Republic and Germany were revealed.
The control findings were compared and best practices were identified on their basis.
In addition, both SAI hope that the results achieved will provide an impetus for stakeholders to start discussing approaches and strategies within the member states, among them at European Commission level.
The extremely valuable experience and knowledge gained from the cooperation of both SAI can serve as an encouragement for the implementation of future VAT management control actions.
6. Communique
Report has been drawn up in Czech, English and German language and signed by the president of the Supreme audit office of the Czech republic and the president of the Federal court of auditors (Bundesrechnungshof) of the Federal republic of Germany.
Edition deadline: June 2010.
